PART ARCH-42: FILL PACK (Work Package 76)

Module: fill
Layer: 55
Prefix: fl_
File: packs/fill/prolog/fill.pl
Test: packs/fill/test/test_fill.pl
Depends: grid

Position in Dependency Order:
The fill pack sits above the grid pack (Layer 56). It operates on
list-of-lists grids and r(R,C) cell regions. No imports from other packs.

Exported Interface:

fl_fill_region/4      - fill region cells with a color
fl_fill_bbox/4        - fill bounding box with a color
fl_fill_row/4         - fill entire row with a color
fl_fill_col/4         - fill entire column with a color
fl_fill_cells/4       - fill specific cells with a color
fl_fill_border/3      - fill outermost grid border with a color
fl_outline_region/4   - fill border cells of a region
fl_fill_interior/4    - fill interior cells of a region
fl_solid_rect/4       - create new uniform-color grid
fl_checkerboard/5     - create new alternating-color grid
fl_draw_hline/6       - draw horizontal line segment
fl_draw_vline/6       - draw vertical line segment
fl_fill_main_diag/3   - fill main diagonal
fl_stamp/6            - overlay subgrid with transparency

Design Notes:

fl_fill_region and fl_fill_cells are identical in behavior (both fill a
list of r(R,C) cells); fl_fill_cells is provided as a semantically clear
name for the "I have specific target cells" use case.

fl_fill_border composes four fill_row and fill_col calls sequentially,
which is simpler than a single-pass membership test and avoids corner cells
being double-painted.

fl_outline_region and fl_fill_interior use the same fl_all_neighbors_in_/2
predicate from the measure-pack convention, but define it locally to avoid
cross-pack dependency.

fl_stamp uses the same SR0 convention as other packs for extracting the
first row of the stamp for its column count, with a fallback of SW=0 if
the stamp is empty.

fl_draw_hline and fl_draw_vline are thin wrappers over fl_fill_bbox,
provided for semantic clarity when the caller is thinking in terms of
line segments rather than rectangular regions.

END OF PART ARCH-42


PART ARCH-43: PATTERN PACK (Work Package 77)

Module: pattern
Layer: 56
Prefix: pt_
File: packs/pattern/prolog/pattern.pl
Test: packs/pattern/test/test_pattern.pl
Depends: grid

Position in Dependency Order:
The pattern pack sits above the grid pack (Layer 56). It works on
list-of-lists grids and flat row lists. No imports from other packs.

Exported Interface:

pt_row_period/2       - smallest tiling period of a row list
pt_col_period/3       - smallest tiling period of a column
pt_grid_period_h/2    - horizontal tiling period of the whole grid
pt_grid_period_v/2    - vertical tiling period of the whole grid
pt_tile_unit_h/2      - extract minimal horizontal tile
pt_tile_unit_v/2      - extract minimal vertical tile
pt_tile_unit/2        - extract minimal 2D tile
pt_is_tiling/2        - test if grid is an exact tiling of a tile
pt_count_tile/3       - count all positions where tile matches
pt_find_tile/3        - list all match positions
pt_extract_tile/5     - extract H x W subgrid at r(R,C)
pt_unique_rows/2      - number of distinct rows
pt_unique_cols/2      - number of distinct columns
pt_has_uniform_rows/1 - test all rows identical

Design Notes:

pt_list_period_ uses the standard between/3 + cut pattern: try periods
from 1 upward and return the first that satisfies period_ok_/2.

pt_period_ok_ uses negation-as-failure over the index set: a period P
is valid if there is no index i where List[i] != List[i mod P].

pt_grid_period_h uses the same negation-as-failure approach over the
row list: a horizontal period P is valid if no row fails period_ok_.

pt_find_tile uses findall over all valid (R,C) offsets and delegates
cell-by-cell comparison to pt_tile_matches_at_.

pt_extract_tile uses a maplist over row offsets (DR 0..H-1), applying
pt_drop_ then pt_take_ to slice each row correctly.

pt_has_uniform_rows uses sort/2: if all rows are identical, sort
produces a singleton list. This is the most concise correct test.

END OF PART ARCH-43


PART ARCH-44: COMPARE PACK (Work Package 78)

Module: compare
Layer: 57
Prefix: cp_
File: packs/compare/prolog/compare.pl
Test: packs/compare/test/test_compare.pl
Depends: grid

Position in Dependency Order:
The compare pack sits at Layer 57. It operates on list-of-lists grids
and r(R,C) region lists. No imports from other packs.

Exported Interface:

cp_diff_cells/3        - cells where two grids differ
cp_same_cells/3        - cells where two grids are equal
cp_added_color/4       - cells where a color was gained
cp_removed_color/4     - cells where a color was lost
cp_changed_to/4        - cells that changed to a specific color
cp_changed_from/4      - cells that changed from a specific color
cp_diff_map/3          - 0/1 grid of per-cell difference flags
cp_similarity/3        - equal-cell count and total as EqCount-Total
cp_region_diff/3       - set difference of two cell regions
cp_region_intersect/3  - set intersection of two cell regions
cp_region_union/3      - set union of two cell regions
cp_region_equal/2      - test order-independent region equality
cp_grids_equal/2       - test structural grid equality
cp_color_shift/3       - Old-New color pairs for all changed cells

Design Notes:

cp_diff_cells, cp_same_cells, cp_added_color, cp_removed_color,
cp_changed_to, cp_changed_from all use the same include/3 over
cp_all_positions_ pattern, varying only the filter predicate.

cp_changed_to and cp_added_color are semantically equivalent;
both are exported because callers reasoning about "what changed"
use different vocabulary than callers reasoning about "what was added."

cp_diff_map uses maplist over row pairs with a per-column flag mapping.
The flag predicate uses 0/1 integer values matching the ARC-AGI convention
of 0 = background.

cp_similarity returns EqCount-Total (a Prolog pair) rather than a float,
to preserve exactness. The caller can compute EqCount / Total if a ratio
is needed.

cp_region_diff, cp_region_intersect, cp_region_union delegate to the
corresponding library(lists) predicates (subtract/3, intersection/3,
union/3), which treat lists as sets.

cp_color_shift is distinct from cp_diff_cells in that it returns value
pairs rather than cell positions, which is the appropriate representation
when the caller wants to analyze the color transformation rule.

END OF PART ARCH-44


PART ARCH-45: SPATIAL PACK (Work Package 79)

Module: spatial
Layer: 58
Prefix: sp_
File: packs/spatial/prolog/spatial.pl
Test: packs/spatial/test/test_spatial.pl
Depends: grid

Exported Interface:

sp_direction/3          - cardinal direction between two cells
sp_distance_manhattan/3 - Manhattan distance
sp_distance_chebyshev/3 - Chebyshev distance
sp_neighbors4/3         - 4-connected in-bounds neighbors
sp_neighbors8/3         - 8-connected in-bounds neighbors
sp_adjacent4/2          - 4-connected adjacency test
sp_adjacent8/2          - 8-connected adjacency test
sp_bbox_contains/2      - cell inside bounding box test
sp_in_region/2          - cell region membership test
sp_row_between/4        - filter region by row range
sp_col_between/4        - filter region by column range
sp_closest/3            - nearest region cell by Manhattan distance
sp_farthest/3           - farthest region cell by Manhattan distance
sp_centroid/3           - integer centroid of a region

Design Notes:

sp_direction uses nine named compass points including same (for identical cells).
The implementation dispatches on the signs of DR and DC.

sp_neighbors4 and sp_neighbors8 generate all candidates then filter with
sp_in_bounds_, which is consistent with the include-over-candidates pattern
used throughout the platform.

sp_adjacent4 and sp_adjacent8 are thin tests over distance predicates
rather than repeating the distance arithmetic inline.

sp_in_region uses member/2 with a cut to suppress the choicepoint that
member would otherwise leave; this makes the predicate deterministic when
used in tests and rule conditions.

sp_closest and sp_farthest use maplist to compute all distances, then
min_list/max_list to find the extremum, then nth0 to retrieve the
corresponding region cell. The cut after nth0 returns the first tied cell.

sp_centroid uses integer division (//), which truncates toward zero,
consistent with the ms_centroid predicate in the measure pack.

END OF PART ARCH-45


PART ARCH-46: INDUCTION PACK (Work Package 80)

Module: induction
Layer: 59
Prefix: id_
File: packs/induction/prolog/induction.pl
Test: packs/induction/test/test_induction.pl
Depends: grid

Exported Interface:

id_color_map/3       - infer OldColor-NewColor pairs from grid pair
id_is_recolor/2      - test consistent color substitution
id_uniform_output/2  - test uniform single-color output
id_output_color/2    - get uniform output color
id_size_ratio/3      - compute dimension ratio
id_is_scale/2        - test uniform integer scale
id_scale_factor/3    - get integer scale factor
id_changed_cells/3   - cells that changed
id_unchanged_cells/3 - cells that did not change
id_input_colors/2    - distinct colors in input
id_output_colors/2   - distinct colors in output
id_new_colors/3      - colors gained in output
id_lost_colors/3     - colors lost from input
id_grid_dims/3       - grid row and column count

Design Notes:

id_color_map uses findall over changed cells and sort/2 to deduplicate
OldColor-NewColor pairs. This produces a canonical map form.

id_is_recolor calls id_color_map then verifies consistency using
negation-as-failure over all positions: a map is inconsistent if any cell
with a known OldColor has an OutV that differs from the expected NewColor.

id_is_scale checks that both dimension ratios are equal positive integers
by testing mod/div conditions; id_scale_factor delegates to id_is_scale.

id_changed_cells and id_unchanged_cells follow the same include-over-positions
pattern as the compare pack, maintaining platform consistency.

id_size_ratio uses integer division (/) which in SWI-Prolog returns an
integer for exact ratios and truncates otherwise.

END OF PART ARCH-46


PART ARCH-47: GRAVITY PACK (Work Package 81)

Location: packs/gravity/
Module: gravity
Layer: 60
Prefix: gv_
Pack descriptor: packs/gravity/pack.pl
Implementation: packs/gravity/prolog/gravity.pl
Tests: packs/gravity/test/test_gravity.pl

Dependencies:
  - grid pack (for r(R,C) cell conventions and list-of-lists grid format)
  - library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3
  - library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3, include/3, foldl/4

Architecture role:
The gravity pack sits at Layer 60, immediately above the induction pack
(Layer 59). It provides the fundamental directional settling operations
that turn static grid states into dynamic physics-like transformations.

The pack is built on two internal primitives:
  gv_compact_list_bottom_/3  - sort non-BG to end of a list
  gv_compact_list_top_/3     - sort non-BG to front of a list

Both primitives use include/3 to partition a list into background and
non-background elements, then concatenate. All higher-level predicates
(fall, settle, float, stack) are built by applying these primitives
column-wise or row-wise via maplist/3 or foldl/4.

The gv_settle_color/4 and gv_float_color/4 predicates extend the
partition into three categories: Color cells, Other non-BG cells, and BG
cells. This allows Color cells to fall through BG while being blocked
by non-BG non-Color cells.

gv_apply_col/4 and gv_apply_row/4 provide a hook for custom transforms
using the same column/row extraction machinery.

Exported predicates (14):
  gv_col_values/3    - column extraction
  gv_set_col/4       - column replacement
  gv_compact_col/3   - all non-BG sink to column bottoms
  gv_compact_row/3   - all non-BG shift to row lefts
  gv_fall_down/3     - non-BG falls to bottom
  gv_fall_up/3       - non-BG rises to top
  gv_fall_left/3     - non-BG shifts left
  gv_fall_right/3    - non-BG shifts right
  gv_settle_color/4  - Color falls to bottom past BG
  gv_float_color/4   - Color rises to top past BG
  gv_stack_down/4    - alias for gv_settle_color
  gv_stack_up/4      - alias for gv_float_color
  gv_apply_col/4     - custom column transform
  gv_apply_row/4     - custom row transform

Test coverage: 29 PLUnit tests.

END OF PART ARCH-47


PART ARCH-48: NOISE PACK (Work Package 82)

Location: packs/noise/
Module: noise
Layer: 61
Prefix: ns_
Pack descriptor: packs/noise/pack.pl
Implementation: packs/noise/prolog/noise.pl
Tests: packs/noise/test/test_noise.pl

Dependencies:
  - grid pack (for r(R,C) cell conventions and list-of-lists grid format)
  - library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3
  - library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3, include/3, foldl/4
  - msort/2 (SWI-Prolog built-in)

Architecture role:
The noise pack sits at Layer 61, above the gravity pack (Layer 60). It
provides two complementary capabilities: binary mask operations and
noise/density analysis.

Binary mask operations:
  ns_mask_apply, ns_mask_invert, ns_mask_and, ns_mask_or are pure
  pointwise operations on grids of 0s and 1s. They allow combining,
  inverting, and applying masks to color grids.

  ns_mask_from_color builds a mask from a color criterion.
  ns_mask_to_region and ns_region_to_mask convert between mask
  representation (list-of-lists of 0/1) and region representation
  (list of r(R,C) cells). This bridges the mask world and the region
  world used by the scene, shape, and spatial packs.

Noise analysis:
  ns_color_count counts occurrences of a given color in a grid.
  ns_majority_color finds the dominant color by counting all colors
  and returning the one with the highest count.
  ns_noise_cells identifies cells that deviate from the majority.
  ns_denoise replaces those cells with the majority color.
  ns_sparse_cells and ns_dense_cells classify cells by how often their
  color appears: sparse cells belong to rarely-occurring colors;
  dense cells belong to frequently-occurring colors.

ns_isolate_color implements a common ARC-AGI operation: keep one
color visible and zero out the rest.

Exported predicates (14):
  ns_mask_apply/4      - apply binary mask with fill color
  ns_mask_invert/3     - flip all mask bits
  ns_mask_and/3        - pointwise AND
  ns_mask_or/3         - pointwise OR
  ns_mask_from_color/3 - build mask from color
  ns_mask_to_region/2  - mask to r(R,C) region list
  ns_region_to_mask/4  - region list to mask
  ns_noise_cells/3     - cells differing from majority color
  ns_denoise/3         - replace noise with majority color
  ns_majority_color/2  - most frequent color
  ns_color_count/3     - count of a specific color
  ns_sparse_cells/3    - cells with rarely-occurring color
  ns_dense_cells/3     - cells with frequently-occurring color
  ns_isolate_color/3   - keep one color, zero out the rest

Test coverage: 33 PLUnit tests.

END OF PART ARCH-48


PART ARCH-49: GENERATE PACK (Work Package 83)

Location: packs/generate/
Module: generate
Layer: 62
Prefix: ge_
Pack descriptor: packs/generate/pack.pl
Implementation: packs/generate/prolog/generate.pl
Tests: packs/generate/test/test_generate.pl

Dependencies:
  - grid pack (for r(R,C) cell conventions and list-of-lists grid format)
  - library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3
  - library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3

Architecture role:
The generate pack sits at Layer 62, above the noise pack (Layer 61). It
provides constructive operations: building new grids from scratch using
visual patterns, arithmetic rules, or explicit cell-color maps.

All predicates are purely constructive (no reading of an existing grid,
except ge_repeat_pattern which reads a pattern grid to tile it).

Implementation patterns:
- ge_uniform uses maplist/2 with =.
- ge_gradient_h/ge_gradient_v use numlist/3 + maplist/3 + mod arithmetic.
- ge_checkerboard, ge_border_rect, ge_diagonal, ge_antidiagonal, ge_frame,
  ge_cross all use maplist/3 at row level and maplist/3 at cell level with
  a per-cell predicate that computes color from (R, C) coordinates.
- ge_stripes_h/ge_stripes_v use numlist + nth0 to cycle through the Colors list.
- ge_from_map starts from a zero grid (ge_uniform) and applies a fold
  using an internal helper, foldl_map_/3.
- ge_repeat_pattern uses mod arithmetic on both row and column indices.

Exported predicates (14):
  ge_uniform/4          - uniform color fill
  ge_gradient_h/4       - horizontal gradient
  ge_gradient_v/4       - vertical gradient
  ge_checkerboard/5     - alternating two colors
  ge_stripes_h/4        - horizontal color stripes
  ge_stripes_v/4        - vertical color stripes
  ge_border_rect/5      - bordered rectangle
  ge_diagonal/4         - main diagonal pattern
  ge_antidiagonal/4     - anti-diagonal pattern
  ge_frame/5            - outermost ring only
  ge_cross/5            - row+column cross through center
  ge_identity_grid/3    - N x N identity matrix pattern
  ge_from_map/3         - build from cell-color map
  ge_repeat_pattern/4   - tile a pattern grid

Test coverage: 29 PLUnit tests.

END OF PART ARCH-49


PART ARCH-50: ARCHITECTURE - LOOKUP PACK (Work Package 84)

Pack name: lookup
Layer: 63
Module: lookup
File: packs/lookup/prolog/lookup.pl
Manifest: packs/lookup/pack.pl
Tests: packs/lookup/test/test_lookup.pl

Dependencies:
- library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, subtract/3
- library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3, include/3
Note: msort/2, length/2 are SWI-Prolog built-ins, not imported.

Meta-predicate declarations:
  :- meta_predicate lk_map_values(+, 2, -).
  :- meta_predicate lk_apply_val_(2, +, -).
These ensure that predicates passed as arguments to lk_map_values are
called with the correct module qualification.

Architecture role:
The lookup pack sits at Layer 63, above the generate pack (Layer 62).
It provides a named, testable API for association list operations and
grid random-access, replacing ad-hoc member/2 searches and nth0 chains
in higher-level reasoning packs.

Implementation patterns:
- lk_get/lk_put/lk_delete use recursive list traversal with cuts for
  determinism on the first-match case.
- lk_keys/lk_values use maplist/3 with helper predicates that extract
  the key or value from a K-V pair.
- lk_map_values uses maplist/3 with a meta-predicate; requires the
  :- meta_predicate declaration to preserve module qualification.
- lk_grid_row wraps nth0/3; lk_grid_col uses maplist(lk_nth0_(C)).
- lk_color_positions uses findall to collect Color-r(R,C) pairs, then
  groups by color via lk_group_by_key_ (findall + sort).
- lk_position_color uses findall to collect r(R,C)-Color pairs directly.
- lk_invert uses maplist/3 with lk_swap_pair_ to flip each K-V pair.

Exported predicates (14):
  lk_get/3              - association list lookup by key
  lk_put/4              - add or replace key-value pair
  lk_keys/2             - extract all keys
  lk_values/2           - extract all values
  lk_has_key/2          - key membership test
  lk_delete/3           - remove a key-value pair
  lk_map_values/3       - transform all values in a map
  lk_from_pairs/2       - build a map from Key-Value pairs
  lk_grid_row/3         - row lookup in a grid
  lk_grid_col/3         - column lookup in a grid
  lk_grid_cell/4        - cell lookup by (R,C)
  lk_color_positions/3  - Color to positions index map
  lk_position_color/3   - position to Color index map
  lk_invert/2           - invert association list keys and values

Test coverage: 30 PLUnit tests.

END OF PART ARCH-50


PART ARCH-51: ARCHITECTURE - CONNECT PACK (Work Package 85)

Pack name: connect
Layer: 64
Module: connect
File: packs/connect/prolog/connect.pl
Manifest: packs/connect/pack.pl
Tests: packs/connect/test/test_connect.pl

Dependencies:
- library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, subtract/3
- library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3, include/3
Note: length/2, msort/2 are SWI-Prolog built-ins, not imported.

Architecture role:
The connect pack sits at Layer 64, above the lookup pack (Layer 63).
It provides the fundamental flood fill and connected component
operations that grid reasoning at higher levels depends on. The
cc_enclosed predicate implements the "enclosed region" test used in
tasks where a closed outline surrounds a fill area.

Implementation patterns:
- cc_dfs_/8: core DFS flood fill with a stack, a visited accumulator,
  and a neighbor function (cc_neighbors4_ or cc_neighbors8_).
  Each step: skip if visited, skip if OOB or wrong color, else expand.
- cc_extract_/7: iteratively extracts connected components from a pool
  of same-color cells using cc_dfs_ + subtract/3 to remove found cells.
- cc_all_cells_/5: findall over all (R,C) pairs in row/col numlist.
- cc_largest_from_/3, cc_smallest_from_/3: linear scan to find the
  component with the maximum or minimum length.
- cc_is_border_/4: include-ready predicate; true if any 4-neighbor is
  OOB or absent from Region (uses memberchk for membership test).
- cc_all_in_region_/4: strict check that all 4 neighbors are in-bounds
  AND in Region; OOB neighbors cause failure (grid-edge cells cannot
  be interior cells).
- cc_enclosed: finds BG cells on the grid border, floods from them,
  then returns BG cells that were not reached (the enclosed ones).
- cc_multi_dfs_/7: sequential flood fill from a list of seed cells,
  threading the visited set through for correctness.

Exported predicates (14):
  cc_flood4/4           - 4-connected flood fill from one seed
  cc_flood8/4           - 8-connected flood fill from one seed
  cc_components4/3      - all 4-connected components of a color
  cc_components8/3      - all 8-connected components of a color
  cc_count4/3           - number of 4-connected components
  cc_count8/3           - number of 8-connected components
  cc_sizes4/3           - sorted sizes of 4-connected components
  cc_sizes8/3           - sorted sizes of 8-connected components
  cc_largest4/3         - largest 4-connected component
  cc_largest8/3         - largest 8-connected component
  cc_smallest4/3        - smallest 4-connected component
  cc_border_cells/3     - border cells of a region
  cc_interior_cells/3   - interior cells of a region
  cc_enclosed/3         - BG cells enclosed inside a closed shape

Test coverage: 33 PLUnit tests.

END OF PART ARCH-51


PART ARCH-52: ARCHITECTURE - MORPH PACK (Work Package 86)

Pack name: morph
Layer: 65
Module: morph
File: packs/morph/prolog/morph.pl
Manifest: packs/morph/pack.pl
Tests: packs/morph/test/test_morph.pl

Dependencies:
- library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3
- library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3
Note: length/2, forall/2 are SWI-Prolog built-ins, not imported.

Architecture role:
The morph pack sits at Layer 65, above the connect pack (Layer 64).
It provides morphological operations that transform grid shapes:
expanding (dilation), shrinking (erosion), cleaning (open), filling
(close and fill_holes), outlining (boundary, ring), and resizing (pad,
unpad). These operations are the standard toolkit for transforming
objects in visual grid reasoning.

Implementation patterns:
- mo_rebuild_/5: core grid reconstruction using findall over row/col
  index lists. Applies a CellPred(Grid, Rows, Cols, R, C, Out) for
  each (R,C) pair to build the output row-by-row.
- Cell predicates (mo_dilate4_cell_, mo_erode4_cell_, etc.) compute the
  output value for each cell based on its current value and neighbors.
- mo_has_color4_/6, mo_has_color8_/6: check if any neighbor has Color;
  use cut after first match for determinism.
- mo_all4_color_/6, mo_all8_color_/6: check all in-bounds neighbors
  have Color; OOB neighbors cause failure (treated as not-Color).
- mo_fill_holes4: implements enclosed-region detection inline using
  flood fill from border BG seeds; avoids external pack dependency.
- mo_pad/3: builds pad rows with maplist(=(PadColor)) and appends to
  padded rows using mo_pad_row_.
- mo_unpad/2: removes head and last element from rows and removes
  first/last row; uses mo_drop_last_ for tail-removal.
- Wrapper predicates (mo_dilate4_cell_wrap_ etc.) adapt cell predicates
  to the 6-arity signature expected by mo_rebuild_.

Exported predicates (14):
  mo_dilate4/4        - 4-connected dilation
  mo_dilate8/4        - 8-connected dilation
  mo_erode4/4         - 4-connected erosion
  mo_erode8/4         - 8-connected erosion
  mo_dilate4_n/5      - N rounds of 4-connected dilation
  mo_erode4_n/5       - N rounds of 4-connected erosion
  mo_open4/4          - morphological open (erode then dilate)
  mo_close4/4         - morphological close (dilate then erode)
  mo_boundary4/3      - 4-connected boundary cells
  mo_boundary8/3      - 8-connected boundary cells
  mo_ring4/4          - 4-connected outward ring
  mo_fill_holes4/4    - fill enclosed background holes
  mo_pad/3            - add one-cell border to grid
  mo_unpad/2          - remove one-cell border from grid

Test coverage: 26 PLUnit tests.

END OF PART ARCH-52


PART ARCH-53 - REWRITE PACK

Work Package: 87
Layer: 66
Module: rewrite
Prefix: rw_
File: packs/rewrite/prolog/rewrite.pl
Test: packs/rewrite/test/test_rewrite.pl
Pack metadata: packs/rewrite/pack.pl
Depends on: grid (list-of-lists format)

Responsibility:
  Rule-based cell-value transformation of list-of-lists grids.
  Covers color substitution, region painting, masking, overlay composition,
  patch stamping, diff application, color normalization, color inversion,
  background remapping, border painting, rectangle fill, and conditional recoloring.

Exports:
  rw_map_color/3      - apply a color substitution map
  rw_replace_color/4  - replace one color with another
  rw_swap_colors/4    - swap two colors

  rw_remap_bg/4       - replace background color throughout

  rw_conditional uses a meta_predicate declaration so the Goal closure is

PART ARCH-54 - RUN PACK

Work Package: 88
Layer: 67
Module: run
Prefix: rn_
File: packs/run/prolog/run.pl
Test: packs/run/test/test_run.pl
Pack metadata: packs/run/pack.pl
Depends on: grid (list-of-lists format)

Responsibility:
  Run-length encoding and decoding of value sequences and grid rows/columns.
  Provides compact representation of repeated values, positional lookup in
  encoded sequences, and structural analysis (maximum run, run count, uniformity,
  position enumeration).

Exports:
  rn_encode/2       - encode a list to Value-Count pairs
  rn_decode/2       - decode Value-Count pairs to a flat list
  rn_row_encode/3   - encode one grid row
  rn_col_encode/3   - encode one grid column
  rn_grid_rows/2    - encode all rows
  rn_grid_cols/2    - encode all columns
  rn_length/2       - total element count of a run list
  rn_at/3           - value at a 0-indexed position
  rn_max_run/3      - longest run of a given value
  rn_count_runs/3   - number of distinct runs of a given value
  rn_uniform/1      - true when all values are the same
  rn_trim/3         - remove leading and trailing background values
  rn_repeat/3       - repeat and merge adjacent boundary runs
  rn_positions/3    - 0-indexed positions of a given value

Implementation notes:
  The core rn_encode uses rn_take_same_ which collects a run via if-then-else
  on integer comparison to avoid choicepoints. rn_at uses a similar if-then-else
  structure. rn_uniform matches the head and second run value directly in the
  clause head. rn_repeat builds the repeated run list via findall and then
  merges adjacent same-value runs via rn_merge_adjacent_.

PART ARCH-55 - ARITH PACK ARCHITECTURE

Work Package 89 - Layer 68 - Module: arith - Prefix: ar_

Location: packs/arith/
  pack.pl        - pack metadata; name(arith); requires([grid])
  prolog/arith.pl - 14 ar_* predicates; module arith
  test/test_arith.pl - 39 PLUnit acceptance tests

Layer Assignment: Layer 68 (above run at Layer 67)

Module arith imports:
  library(lists)  - member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, append/3, min_list/2, max_list/2
  library(apply)  - maplist/2, maplist/3

Internal helpers (not exported):
  ar_add_row_/3        - add corresponding cells of two rows
  ar_add_cell_/3       - add two cell values
  ar_sub_row_/3        - subtract corresponding cells
  ar_sub_cell_/3       - subtract two cell values
  ar_mul_row_/3        - multiply corresponding cells
  ar_mul_cell_/3       - multiply two cell values
  ar_mod_cell_/3       - cell-wise modulo
  ar_sadd_cell_/3      - add scalar to a cell
  ar_smul_cell_/3      - multiply cell by scalar
  ar_list_sum_/2       - recursive list sum
  ar_abs_diff_row_/3   - absolute difference of two rows
  ar_abs_diff_cell_/3  - absolute value of difference of two cells
  ar_clamp_cell_/4     - clamp a cell value to [Lo, Hi]

Design decisions:
  Binary grid operations (add, sub, mul, abs_diff) use maplist/4 over row pairs,
  then maplist/4 over cell pairs. This avoids explicit indexing.

  Scalar operations (mod, scalar_add, scalar_mul, clamp) use maplist(maplist(F)),
  threading the scalar via partial application.

  ar_list_sum_ is a recursive predicate rather than sum_list/2 from library(lists)
  to avoid an unnecessary import.

  ar_col_sums builds a list of column indices via numlist/3 and maps ar_col_sum/3
  over it. ar_col_sum extracts a column via maplist(nth0(C), Grid, Col).

  ar_cell_max and ar_cell_min flatten the grid with append/2 and delegate to
  max_list/2 and min_list/2.

  ar_cell_clamp uses a three-way if-then-else for determinism (no choicepoints).

END OF PART ARCH-55


PART ARCH-56 - OBJ PACK ARCHITECTURE

Work Package 90 - Layer 69 - Module: obj - Prefix: obj_

Location: packs/obj/
  pack.pl          - pack metadata; name(obj); requires([grid, connect])
  prolog/obj.pl    - 14 obj_* predicates; module obj
  test/test_obj.pl - 40 PLUnit acceptance tests

Layer Assignment: Layer 69 (above arith at Layer 68)

Module obj imports:
  library(lists)   - member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, append/3, max_list/2, min_list/2, subtract/3
  library(apply)   - maplist/2, maplist/3
  library(connect) - cc_components4/3

Object representation: obj(Color, SortedCells)
  Color is a non-negative integer.
  SortedCells is the msort of the r(R,C) cell list (standard term order).

Internal helpers (not exported):
  obj_from_cells/3   - constructs obj term (same as exported, used internally)
  obj_cell_r_/2      - extract row coordinate from r(R,C)
  obj_cell_c_/2      - extract column coordinate from r(R,C)
  obj_list_sum_/2    - recursive sum of a list of integers
  obj_normalize_cell_/4 - subtract (MinR, MinC) from a cell for shape normalization
  obj_wrap_/3        - wrap a component cell list as an obj term
  obj_size_key_/2    - pair an object with its size for keyed sorting
  obj_strip_key_/2   - extract the object from a size-keyed pair

Design decisions:
  obj_all uses findall to collect values and to flatten the per-color object
  lists. This avoids choicepoints from append/2 applied to a list of lists.

  obj_all uses sort/2 (not msort/2) to simultaneously sort and deduplicate
  the color list. sort/2 is a SWI-Prolog built-in.

  obj_largest and obj_smallest use a deterministic cut (!) after the first
  member/2 match to avoid leaving choicepoints.

  obj_sort_size uses msort/2 on size-keyed pairs (Size-Obj) to sort stably
  by size, then strips the keys and optionally reverses for descending order.

  obj_shape normalizes by the top-left of the bounding box (MinR, MinC), making
  shapes translation-independent. Two objects with the same shape can be matched
  without knowing their grid positions.

END OF PART ARCH-56


PART ARCH-57 - PIPELINE PACK ARCHITECTURE

Work Package 91 - Layer 70 - Module: pipeline - Prefix: pl_

Location: packs/pipeline/
  pack.pl                  - pack metadata; name(pipeline); requires([grid])
  prolog/pipeline.pl       - 14 pl_* predicates; module pipeline
  test/test_pipeline.pl    - 39 PLUnit acceptance tests

Layer Assignment: Layer 70 (above obj at Layer 69)

Module pipeline imports:
  library(lists)   - member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, append/3
  library(apply)   - maplist/2, maplist/3, foldl/4

Dynamic fact: pl_handler_/2
  Stores step handlers as pl_handler_(Name, Goal).
  Manipulated by pl_register/2, pl_registered/2, pl_unregister/1.

Step dispatch model:
  A step is any Prolog term. Its name is the functor of the term (or the
  atom itself for atomic steps). A handler is a 3-argument callable:
  Handler(StepTerm, In, Out). The StepTerm is passed to the handler so
  that compound step terms (e.g., scale(2)) can carry parameters.

  pl_step/4 checks a local Name-Goal registry first, then the dynamic
  pl_handler_/2 facts. If neither has a handler, Out = In (passthrough).
  The local registry allows transient override without asserting global facts.

  pl_run/3 uses foldl to thread the grid through all steps, calling
  pl_step/4 for each step with an empty local registry.

pl_filter and pl_partition use findall for determinism. The findall-based
implementation avoids choicepoints that would arise from recursive two-clause
definitions where first-argument indexing does not disambiguate the base case
from the recursive case when Goal is a meta-argument.

pl_take and pl_drop use explicit cuts (!) to commit to the base cases, which
cover the N=0 case and the empty-list case before the recursive clause.

END OF PART ARCH-57


PART ARCH-58 - CONTEXT PACK ARCHITECTURE

Work Package 92 - Layer 71 - Module: context - Prefix: ctx_

Location: packs/context/
  pack.pl                - pack metadata; name(context); requires([grid])
  prolog/context.pl      - 14 ctx_* predicates; module context
  test/test_context.pl   - 41 PLUnit acceptance tests

Layer Assignment: Layer 71 (above pipeline at Layer 70)

Module context imports:
  library(lists)   - member/2, subtract/3, append/3
  library(apply)   - maplist/2, maplist/3

Data representation: a context map is a Prolog list [Key1-Value1, Key2-Value2, ...]
where keys are unique Prolog terms. The list is ordered by insertion; ctx_put
prepends the new binding after deleting any old one, so the most recently added
binding appears first.

Internal helpers:
  ctx_key_/2              - extract key from K-V pair
  ctx_value_/2            - extract value from K-V pair
  ctx_map_entry_/3        - apply a value-transform goal to one K-V pair
  ctx_from_pairs_/3       - recursive fold for ctx_from_pairs
  ctx_merge_/3            - recursive fold for ctx_merge

Design decisions:
  ctx_get uses clause-head pattern matching with a cut for the matching clause.
  This gives deterministic first-match semantics matching the unique-key invariant.

  ctx_delete uses if-then-else to avoid choicepoints when scanning the list.

  ctx_select uses a cut in the base case (empty key list) so that when none
  of the priority keys are present, the base clause commits without leaving
  a choicepoint.

  ctx_filter_keys uses findall for determinism (avoids choicepoints from
  meta-argument Goal defeating first-argument indexing).

  ctx_dispatch uses if-then-else to dispatch to either the found goal or
  the default goal. Only one branch is taken.

  ctx_merge is implemented as a fold of ctx_put over Map2 entries applied
  to Map1, ensuring Map2 bindings override Map1 for shared keys.

END OF PART ARCH-58


PART ARCH-59 - SCORE PACK ARCHITECTURE (LAYER 72)

What changed: Added the score pack at Layer 72.

Why: Scoring and ranking are needed to select the best hypothesis after rule
application. This pack provides a clean API separating measurement concerns
from rule generation concerns.

Pack: score
Layer: 72
Module: score
Prefix: sc_
File: packs/score/prolog/score.pl
Tests: packs/score/test/test_score.pl
Requires: grid (for list-of-lists grid representation)

Exports:
  sc_exact/2         - structural grid equality
  sc_cell_match/3    - count cells where two grids agree
  sc_cell_total/2    - total cell count
  sc_accuracy/3      - pixel accuracy as float in [0.0, 1.0]
  sc_color_recall/4  - per-color recall
  sc_color_precision/4 - per-color precision
  sc_color_f1/4      - per-color F1 score
  sc_pair_score/3    - accuracy on one Input-Expected pair
  sc_pairs_score/3   - mean accuracy over a list of pairs
  sc_perfect/3       - exact-match test for one pair
  sc_pairs_perfect/2 - all-pairs exact-match test
  sc_rank/3          - rank candidates by accuracy descending
  sc_best/3          - pick highest-accuracy candidate
  sc_threshold/4     - filter candidates by minimum accuracy

Design decisions:
  sc_accuracy uses float/1 conversion before division to guarantee float output
  even when Match and Total are integers. Without this, integer division
  would return 1 instead of 1.0 for a perfect match, breaking pattern
  matching in sc_rank where the result is compared as 1.0-Grid.

  sc_count_matches_, sc_count_color_, and sc_count_tp_ are recursive helpers
  using if-then-else for determinism. They operate on flat lists produced by
  append/2 from the grid rows.

  sc_rank uses msort (built-in) followed by reverse/2 to sort descending.

  sc_threshold uses findall for determinism; no choicepoints.

  sc_mean_ uses foldl from library(apply) for accumulation.

END OF PART ARCH-59


PART ARCH-60 - INDUCT PACK ARCHITECTURE (LAYER 73)

What changed: Added the induct pack at Layer 73.

Why: Observing what changed between input and output is the first step of
rule induction. Before a system can hypothesize a rule, it must observe the
evidence: which cells changed, which colors substituted for which others,
whether the grid size changed, and what the background color is.

Pack: induct
Layer: 73
Module: induct
Prefix: in_
File: packs/induct/prolog/induct.pl
Tests: packs/induct/test/test_induct.pl
Requires: grid

Exports:
  in_delta/3          - list of r(R,C)-Old-New triples for changed cells
  in_constant/2       - identity rule test
  in_color_map/3      - consistent color substitution map for one pair
  in_color_map_pairs/2 - intersected color map across all pairs
  in_size_change/4    - grid size delta for one pair
  in_size_change_pairs/3 - consistent size delta across all pairs
  in_color_palette/3  - union color set for one pair
  in_palette_pairs/3  - separated input/output color sets across all pairs
  in_invariant_cells/3 - positions with same color in both grids
  in_changed_cells/3  - positions where grids differ
  in_consistent_delta/2 - same change pattern across all pairs
  in_bg_color/2       - most frequent color in one grid
  in_bg_color_pairs/2 - consistent background color across all pairs
  in_common_keys/3    - shared entries in two color maps

Design decisions:
  in_delta uses findall for determinism. Iterates over row and column indices
  via nth0/3 and filters cells where Old != New.

  in_color_map uses sort to deduplicate raw pairs, then in_check_consistent_map_
  to verify no color maps to two different outputs. Fails on conflict.

  in_color_map_pairs uses foldl over in_intersect_map_, which itself uses
  library(lists) intersection/3. Empty pairs list returns empty map
  via the base clause.

  in_bg_color builds a Counted list of Count-Color pairs, then uses
  max_member/2 from library(lists) to find the most frequent color.
  In case of a tie, max_member picks the largest color value.

  All predicates that iterate over pairs use findall or forall for
  determinism; no recursive two-clause definitions that could leave
  choicepoints.

END OF PART ARCH-60


PART ARCH-61 - HYP PACK ARCHITECTURE (LAYER 74)

What changed: Added the hyp pack at Layer 74.

Why: The induct pack observes; the hyp pack applies. A hypothesis is a 2-argument
callable that transforms an input grid into a candidate output grid. The hyp pack
provides the application, testing, and selection infrastructure.

Pack: hyp
Layer: 74
Module: hyp
Prefix: hy_
File: packs/hyp/prolog/hyp.pl
Tests: packs/hyp/test/test_hyp.pl
Requires: grid, induct

Exports:
  hy_color_sub/3    - apply color substitution map to grid
  hy_identity/2     - identity hypothesis
  hy_from_map/3     - alias for hy_color_sub as partial-application goal
  hy_test/4         - test one hypothesis on one pair
  hy_test_all/4     - test one hypothesis on all pairs, return mean
  hy_verify/3       - exact-match test for one pair
  hy_verify_all/2   - exact-match test for all pairs
  hy_select/3       - select best hypothesis from a list
  hy_rank/3         - rank hypotheses by mean accuracy
  hy_apply_map/3    - alias for hy_color_sub
  hy_compose/4      - sequential two-map color substitution
  hy_invert_map/2   - swap keys and values of a color map
  hy_map_lookup/3   - color lookup with identity fallback
  hy_describe/2     - human-readable hypothesis description

Design decisions:
  hy_color_sub uses maplist twice (rows then cells) with an if-then-else
  lookup helper for determinism; no choicepoints from member/2 on Map.

  hy_test uses findall (via hy_cell_match_) to count matching cells for
  determinism, then float(Match)/float(Total) for float accuracy.

  hy_test_all uses maplist over pairs, then foldl in hy_mean_ for the sum.

  hy_verify_all uses forall/2 (built-in) for determinism.

  hy_rank does NOT have meta_predicate on hy_select or hy_rank because
  their third argument is an output, not a goal argument. Declaring it as
  2 in meta_predicate would cause the output to be module-qualified, breaking
  unification in the caller.

  hy_describe uses cuts in the first two clauses to prevent the catch-all
  third clause from leaving a choicepoint after the atom or compound cases match.

END OF PART ARCH-61


PART ARCH-62 - SYM PACK ARCHITECTURE (LAYER 75)

What changed: Added the sym pack at Layer 75.

Why: Symmetry detection and spatial transforms are foundational operations
for grid reasoning. Factoring them into a dedicated pack makes them reusable
across rule induction, hypothesis testing, and analogy detection.

Pack: sym
Layer: 75
Module: sym
Prefix: sy_
File: packs/sym/prolog/sym.pl
Tests: packs/sym/test/test_sym.pl
Requires: grid

Exports:
  sy_reflect_h/2    - left-right mirror
  sy_reflect_v/2    - top-bottom mirror
  sy_transpose/2    - main diagonal reflection
  sy_rotate90/2     - 90 CW rotation
  sy_rotate180/2    - 180 rotation
  sy_rotate270/2    - 270 CW rotation (= 90 CCW)
  sy_has_h_symm/1   - horizontal symmetry test
  sy_has_v_symm/1   - vertical symmetry test
  sy_has_rot2_symm/1 - 2-fold rotational symmetry test
  sy_has_rot4_symm/1 - 4-fold rotational symmetry test
  sy_symmetries/2   - list all symmetry names present
  sy_make_h_symm/2  - enforce horizontal symmetry
  sy_make_v_symm/2  - enforce vertical symmetry
  sy_d4_orbit/2     - compute full D4 orbit

Design decisions:
  All rotation predicates are defined compositionally from reflect_h, reflect_v,
  and transpose. This avoids duplicating index arithmetic.
    rotate90  = transpose then reflect_h
    rotate180 = reflect_v then reflect_h
    rotate270 = reflect_h then transpose

  Anti-diagonal reflection (the 8th D4 element) = rotate90 then reflect_v.

  sy_transpose uses numlist to generate column indices, then maplist with
  a lambda to extract each column as a new row. The empty-grid base clause
  is needed because numlist fails for length 0.

  sy_has_* predicates use structural unification (Grid = reflected Grid)
  via the definitional equality sy_reflect_*(Grid, Grid).

  sy_d4_orbit uses sort/2 to deduplicate: equal grids (same dimensions
  and same cells) unify via standard Prolog term ordering.

  sy_make_h_symm and sy_make_v_symm use if-then-else to handle the
  center element in odd-width / odd-height cases without choicepoints.

END OF PART ARCH-62


PART ARCH-63 - SEEK PACK (LAYER 76)

What changed: Added the seek pack at Layer 76.

Why: Spatial pattern search (where does sub-pattern X appear in grid G?),
template matching (which position has the most cell agreements?), D4
transform discovery (which rotation/reflection maps G1 to G2?), and scale
detection (is G2 a Factor-times enlargement of G1?) are all general-purpose
operations needed for visual rule induction. These fill the gap between the
perceptual packs (grid, scene, sym) and the reasoning packs (score, induct, hyp).

Location: packs/seek/
Files:
  pack.pl              - name(seek), version('1.0.0'), requires([grid])
  prolog/seek.pl       - module seek; 14 exported dn_* predicates; Layer 76
  test/test_seek.pl    - 49 PLUnit tests; 14 test groups

Dependencies: library(lists) for member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, append/3,
max_member/2, memberchk/2, reverse/2; library(apply) for maplist/2,
maplist/3, include/3.

Exported predicates:
  sk_positions/3        - all (R,C) positions of a value
  sk_rows_with/3        - row indices containing a value
  sk_cols_with/3        - column indices containing a value
  sk_border_cells/2     - outermost ring cell positions
  sk_interior_cells/2   - strictly interior cell positions
  sk_fits/4             - exact sub-grid match test
  sk_find_sub/4         - enumerate sub-grid positions (nondeterministic)
  sk_all_subs/3         - collect all sub-grid positions
  dn_count_sub/3        - count sub-grid occurrences
  sk_match_count/5      - count matching cells at a position
  sk_best_fit/4         - position with maximum match count
  sk_find_d4/3          - discover D4 transform between grids
  sk_upscale/3          - cell-block upscaling
  dn_find_scale/3       - discover integer scale factor between grids

Private helpers:
  sk_col_has_val_/3    - column membership test for include/3
  sk_d4_pair_/3        - named D4 transform application
  sk_transpose_/2      - grid transposition (rows become columns)
  sk_upscale_row_/3    - single-row horizontal tiling
  sk_repeat_rows_/3    - vertical row repetition

Design decisions:
  sk_border_cells uses once/1 inside findall to prevent duplicates from
  the disjunction (R=0 or R=NRowsM1 or C=0 or C=NColsM1) producing
  multiple solutions for corner cells.

  sk_find_d4 uses once/1 to commit to the first matching transform.
  This makes the predicate deterministic when Name is unbound.

  sk_upscale_row_ uses findall(Cell, (member(Cell, Row), between(1, Factor, _)),
  TiledRow) to repeat each cell Factor times in place.

  sk_repeat_rows_ uses findall to build Factor copies of each row and
  append/3 to concatenate them vertically.

  D4 transforms are implemented directly (without importing sym) using
  maplist(reverse, ...) for reflect_h and reverse/2 for reflect_v,
  with sk_transpose_/2 for the diagonal operations.

END OF PART ARCH-63

Why: Color remapping is a core operation in visual rule learning. The remap
pack provides the value-transformation layer that maps discovered rules onto
grid outputs. It sits above the search layer (seek, Layer 76) and below the
induction layer, producing transformed grids from learned color maps.

         rm_clamp/4, rm_conditional/4, rm_binarize/4, rm_remap_bg/4,
         rm_palette/2, rm_reindex/3

PART ARCH-65 - LOGIC PACK (Layer 78)

What changed: Added packs/logic/ as the 97th work package (PR 99).

Why: Boolean grid operations are needed to combine masks, compare grids as
sets, and reduce grid content to presence flags. The logic pack sits at
Layer 78, above the remap pack (Layer 77), and provides the composable
mask and boolean layer that the higher-level induction packs can use.

Location: packs/logic/
  pack.pl                   - pack metadata (name, version, requires)
  prolog/logic.pl           - module logic, Layer 78
  test/test_logic.pl        - 42 PLUnit acceptance tests

Module: logic
Prefix: lg_
Layer: 78
Exports: lg_and/4, lg_or/4, lg_xor/4, lg_not/4, lg_diff/4, lg_overlay/4,
         lg_mask_apply/4, lg_mask_from/4, lg_any_row/3, lg_any_col/3,
         lg_all_row/3, lg_all_col/3, lg_eq/3, lg_neq/3

Dependencies: library(lists) [member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3],
              library(apply) [maplist/3, maplist/4]
No inter-pack runtime dependencies.

All binary operations (lg_and, lg_or, lg_xor, lg_diff, lg_overlay,
lg_mask_apply, lg_eq, lg_neq) use maplist/4 for paired row iteration and
