PART ARCH-66 - WINDOW PACK (Layer 79)

What changed: Added packs/window/ as the 98th work package (PR 100).

Why: Neighborhood access is a cross-cutting concern in visual reasoning.
Many higher-level operations (flood fill, connectivity, local feature
detection) depend on efficiently enumerating adjacent cells. The window
pack centralizes this in a single, tested layer rather than duplicating
neighbor-enumeration logic across many packs.

Location: packs/window/
  pack.pl                   - pack metadata (name, version, requires)
  prolog/window.pl          - module window, Layer 79
  test/test_window.pl       - 42 PLUnit acceptance tests

Module: window
Prefix: wn_
Layer: 79
Exports: wn_neighbors4/4, wn_neighbors8/4, wn_count4/5, wn_count8/5,
         wn_extract/6, wn_slide/4, wn_pad/4, wn_local_max4/3,
         wn_local_min4/3, wn_halo4/3, wn_convolve/3, wn_center/3,
         wn_manhattan/5, wn_cells_at_dist/5

Dependencies: library(lists) [member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, append/3],
              library(apply) [maplist/2, maplist/3, maplist/4, include/3, foldl/4]
No inter-pack runtime dependencies.

wn_neighbors4 and wn_neighbors8 enumerate direction offsets using a member/2
call inside findall. Bounds are checked with =< comparisons using the precomputed
NRowsM1 and NColsM1 values to avoid redundant arithmetic.

wn_halo4 uses sort/2 to deduplicate the result; a halo cell may be adjacent to
multiple Val cells and would otherwise appear multiple times in findall output.

wn_convolve delegates extraction to wn_extract and uses wn_dot_ for the
element-wise sum. wn_dot_ uses foldl/4 to accumulate the sum from row sums.

END OF PART ARCH-66


PART ARCH-67 - SORT PACK (Layer 80)

What changed: Added packs/sort/ as the 99th work package (PR 101).

Why: Ordering operations are needed when a task requires ranking or sorting
objects, rows, or columns by count or sum. The sort pack provides the
ordering layer above the logic and remap packs.

Location: packs/sort/
  pack.pl                   - pack metadata (name, version, requires)
  prolog/sort.pl            - module sort, Layer 80
  test/test_sort.pl         - 42 PLUnit acceptance tests

Module: sort
Prefix: so_
Layer: 80
Exports: so_row_sums/2, so_col_sums/2, so_row_count/3, so_col_count/3,
         so_sort_rows_asc/3, so_sort_rows_desc/3, so_sort_cols_asc/3,
         so_sort_cols_desc/3, so_max_row/3, so_min_row/3, so_max_col/3,
         so_min_col/3, so_sorted_vals/2, so_cell_rank/4

Dependencies: library(lists) [member/2, nth0/3, nth1/3, numlist/3,
              max_member/2, min_member/2], library(apply) [maplist/3, include/3]
No inter-pack runtime dependencies.

so_sort_rows_asc uses msort with Count-I keys for stable ascending sort.
so_sort_rows_desc uses NegCount-I keys (NegCount = -Count) so that rows with
more Val cells sort first; this avoids reversing which would break tie-breaking.

so_sort_cols_asc and so_sort_cols_desc delegate to the row-sort predicates
via so_transpose_/2, following the pattern: transpose, sort rows, transpose back.

so_cell_rank uses nth1/3 to find the position of the cell value in the sorted
distinct palette; a cut prevents choicepoint accumulation.

END OF PART ARCH-67


PART ARCH-68 - TILE PACK (Layer 81, Work Package 102)

Location: packs/tile/
  pack.pl               - pack metadata
  prolog/tile.pl        - 14 ti_* predicates
  test/test_tile.pl     - 42 PLUnit acceptance tests

Layer 81 sits above the sort pack (Layer 80) and provides tiling and stamping
operations. It depends only on library(lists) and library(apply).

ti_tile_h and ti_tile_v use foldl over numlist to append N copies of a row
or a grid. ti_tile composes these: tile horizontally NC times then vertically
NR times.

ti_split_rows and ti_split_cols partition a grid by indexing into it with
numlist-generated ranges. ti_split composes them. ti_flatten_tiles inverts
ti_split by joining tile rows horizontally then stacking vertically.

ti_stamp overlays a motif at an offset using maplist/4 over row and column
indices. Out-of-bounds motif cells are silently ignored via nth0 failure.
ti_stamp_all folds ti_stamp over a list of R-C positions.

ti_extract_tile computes row and column ranges from tile indices and extracts
the sub-grid directly. ti_is_tiling uses ti_extract_tile to compare all tiles
to the reference tile at (0,0) via forall.

ti_find_period_h and ti_find_period_v use between/3 to search for the minimum
period and commit with a cut. ti_row_period_ checks periodicity per row.
ti_col_period_ checks that Grid[I] == Grid[I mod P] for all I.

ti_checkerboard assigns V1 or V2 based on (RI+CI) mod 2.

END OF PART ARCH-68


PART ARCH-69 - TRACE PACK (Layer 82, Work Package 103)

Location: packs/trace/
  pack.pl               - pack metadata
  prolog/trace.pl       - 14 tr_* predicates
  test/test_trace.pl    - 42 PLUnit acceptance tests

Layer 82 sits above the tile pack (Layer 81) and provides run detection, ray
casting, path drawing, and boundary operations. Depends only on library(lists)
and library(apply).

tr_runs_row uses findall to enumerate valid Start-End pairs: a start is the
first non-Bg cell after a Bg boundary; an end is the last non-Bg cell before
the next Bg boundary; forall verifies all intermediate cells are non-Bg.
tr_spans_h maps tr_runs_row over each row. tr_spans_v uses a private
tr_transpose_ helper to convert columns to rows first.

tr_ray_h and tr_ray_v build a candidate list (ascending or descending via
reverse) using numlist/3, then use member/2 with a cut to find the first
non-Bg cell. If the initial step is out of bounds the predicate fails.

tr_line_h and tr_line_v build ordered column or row index lists and map them
to R-C pairs via a closure that captures the fixed coordinate from the outer
clause.

tr_path_vals uses maplist/3 with nth0/3 to extract values. tr_draw_path
folds tr_set_cell_ (a private maplist/4-based cell setter) over the path.

tr_bbox_border uses a helper with two clauses (top/bottom rows; left/right
columns) to enumerate border cells and sort to deduplicate corners.

tr_perimeter and tr_outline both use findall with a disjunctive inner goal and
sort to deduplicate cells that qualify via multiple conditions or neighbors.

tr_edge_cells delegates to tr_bbox_border with the full grid extent.

tr_midpoint uses integer division (//).

END OF PART ARCH-69


PART ARCH-70 - LABEL PACK (Layer 83, Work Package 104)

Location: packs/label/
  pack.pl               - pack metadata
  prolog/label.pl       - 14 lb_* predicates
  test/test_label.pl    - 42 PLUnit acceptance tests

Layer 83 sits above the trace pack (Layer 82) and provides connected component
labeling and region query operations. Depends on library(lists) and library(apply).

lb_bfs_ implements breadth-first flood-fill: each step takes the first cell from
the BFS queue, finds its unvisited non-Bg 4-neighbors via findall, deduplicates
with sort, appends them to both Visited and Queue, and recurses until the queue
is empty. The component is the final Visited list.

lb_partition_components_ drives BFS from the lexicographically first unvisited
cell, uses subtract/3 to remove the discovered component from the remaining cell
list, increments the label, and recurses to discover the next component.

lb_label builds a flat R-C-Label lookup list from the label pairs, then
constructs LabelGrid row by row using maplist/4 with nth0 coordinate checks.

lb_components strips labels from the label pairs, returning only cell lists.
lb_count delegates to lb_components and calls length/2.

lb_cells_of, lb_size_of, and lb_sizes_all use findall over the LabelGrid rows.
lb_bbox_of finds min and max coordinates of the cell list using min_member/2
and max_member/2.

lb_neighbors_of collects 4-adjacent labels that differ from both Label and Bg,
deduplicates with sort. The Bg parameter is required to exclude background.

lb_fill_label, lb_merge_two, lb_select_label, and lb_color_labels are all
single-pass maplist transformations over the grid with element-wise conditions.

lb_keep_largest labels the grid, finds the largest component with
lb_max_size_acc_ (a linear fold), then rebuilds the grid preserving only
that component. Handles the all-background case by returning the input grid.

lb_remove_small uses include/3 to filter the Label-Size list to kept labels,
then rebuilds the grid preserving only cells whose label is in the kept set.

END OF PART ARCH-70


PART ARCH-71 - MORPH PACK (Layer 84, Work Package 105)

Location: packs/morph/
  pack.pl               - pack metadata
  prolog/morph.pl       - 14 mo_* predicates
  test/test_morph.pl    - 42 PLUnit acceptance tests

Layer 84 sits above the label pack (Layer 83) and provides morphological
operations on grids. Depends on library(lists) and library(apply) only.

mo_dilate and mo_erode are the primitive one-step operations. Each iterates
over cells using maplist/4 with a lambda that computes RI and CI from index
lists (numlist). The Bg-cell check and the neighbor search are both inline
first-match patterns using Prolog's backtracking if-then-else.

mo_dilate_n and mo_erode_n use foldl over numlist(1, N, Steps); each fold
step applies mo_dilate or mo_erode to the accumulator. N=0 is handled by
a first clause with a cut.

mo_open, mo_close, and mo_smooth are simple compositions: open = erode then
dilate; close = dilate then erode; smooth = open then close.

mo_boundary uses the same cell-iteration pattern as mo_dilate. A non-Bg cell
is a perimeter cell if it is on the grid edge (RI or CI equals 0 or the
grid's maximum) or has a Bg 4-neighbor within bounds. The disjunction is
handled by Prolog's ; operator inside a maplist lambda.

mo_interior calls mo_boundary to get BoundaryGrid, then subtracts: a cell
is interior iff its Grid value is non-Bg and its BoundaryGrid value is Bg.

mo_dilate_val is structurally identical to mo_dilate but replaces the
neighbor-value copy with a fixed Val.

mo_bfs_bg_ is a shared BFS helper that expands through Bg cells. It mirrors
lb_bfs_ from the label pack but stops on Bg boundaries rather than non-Bg
boundaries. Each step finds in-bounds Bg 4-neighbors not in Visited via
findall, deduplicates with sort, extends Visited and Queue, and recurses.

mo_grow_from collects Bg cells adjacent to Seeds as the initial frontier,
then calls mo_bfs_bg_ to reach all connected Bg territory. The marking pass
uses memberchk/2 to test each grid cell against the reached set.

mo_dist_to_bg collects all Bg cell positions with findall, then for each
non-Bg cell computes the minimum L1 distance over the Bg set using findall
and min_member/2.

mo_ring calls mo_dilate_n twice (N and N-1 steps), then marks cells that
are non-Bg in the N-step result but Bg in the (N-1)-step result. The N=0
clause returns all-Bg using a maplist/3 with a lambda that assigns Bg to
every position.

mo_fill_holes finds border Bg cells as seeds, calls mo_bfs_bg_ to
discover all exterior Bg territory, then marks interior Bg cells (those not
in the exterior set) with FillVal using memberchk/2.

END OF PART ARCH-71


PART ARCH-72 - WALK PACK (Layer 85, Work Package 106)

Location: packs/walk/prolog/walk.pl
Module:   walk
Prefix:   wk_
Layer:    85 (Grid Traversal Patterns)

Interface
  wk_row_scan/2      wk_col_scan/2       wk_zigzag_scan/2
  wk_diag_scan/2     wk_antidiag_scan/2  wk_spiral_in/2
  wk_border_walk/2   wk_diag_extract/3   wk_antidiag_extract/3
  wk_diag_of/2       wk_antidiag_of/2    wk_cells_to_vals/3
  wk_vals_to_cells/4 wk_inner_cells/2

Dependencies: library(lists), library(apply)
Test file:    packs/walk/test/test_walk.pl (42 tests)

Internal structure:

wk_dims_/3 is a private helper that extracts NRows and NCols from a grid
using length/2 twice. It returns NC=0 for an empty grid (no rows). All
public predicates call wk_dims_/3 first.

wk_row_scan and wk_col_scan use findall with two between/3 calls in
different nesting order: R outer and C inner for row-major; C outer and R
inner for column-major.

wk_zigzag_row_/3 is a private helper that builds one row's cell list and
reverses it for odd row indices. wk_zigzag_scan/2 calls this via maplist/3
over numlist(0, NR1, RowIdxs) then flattens with append/2.

wk_diag_scan and wk_antidiag_scan both use numlist to enumerate diagonal
indices, then maplist to compute the row range for each diagonal via
max/2 and min/2, then numlist for the row list within each diagonal, then
maplist to compute C from R and D. The resulting nested lists are flattened
with append/2.

wk_ring_cells_/5 is a private helper that implements one clockwise border
ring. It uses findall with between/3 for the top row, right column, bottom
row (collected forward then reversed), and left column (collected forward
then reversed). The right column and bottom row are skipped for single-row
or single-column grids by guarding with NR > 1 and NC > 1 conditions.

wk_spiral_in_/5 is a private recursive predicate. It calls wk_ring_cells_
to peel the outermost ring, then recurses with R0+1, C0+1, NR-2, NC-2.
Base cases are NR =< 0 and NC =< 0, each guarded with a cut.

wk_border_walk/2 simply calls wk_ring_cells_(0, 0, NR, NC, Cells) without
recursion: it returns only the outermost ring.

wk_diag_extract and wk_antidiag_extract compute the row range for the
given diagonal index using max/2 and min/2, then use numlist and maplist
to extract values with nth0/3.

wk_diag_of and wk_antidiag_of are single-clause predicates computing
D = C - R and D = R + C respectively using is/2.

wk_cells_to_vals uses maplist/3 with a lambda that calls nth0/3 twice
(once for the row, once for the column) to extract each value.

wk_set_cell_/5 is a private helper that uses length/2 and append/3 twice:
once to split the grid at row R and once to split the row at column C. The
row and grid are reassembled with append/3. This gives O(NR + NC) time
per cell write.

wk_vals_to_cells/4 is a two-clause recursive predicate. The base clause
(empty lists) is deterministic via a cut. The step clause calls wk_set_cell_
then recurses.

wk_inner_cells computes NR2 = NR-2 and NC2 = NC-2 before the if-then-else
so both values remain bound in the else branch; the condition checks only
the arithmetic comparisons.

END OF PART ARCH-72


PART ARCH-73 - STEP PACK (Layer 86)

Location:  packs/step/
Module:    step
Prefix:    st_
Layer:     86
WP:        107

Files:
  packs/step/pack.pl              - pack metadata (name, version, requires)
  packs/step/prolog/step.pl       - 14 exported st_* predicates
  packs/step/test/test_step.pl    - 42 PLUnit acceptance tests

Exports:
  st_step/3         one unbounded step in a direction
  st_step_in/4      one bounded step (fails if out of bounds)
  st_ray/4          all in-bounds cells in a direction (excluding start)
  st_ray_to/5       ray stopping before a given cell value
  st_walk/4         all in-bounds cells including start
  st_dirs4/1        the four cardinal directions
  st_dirs8/1        the eight principal directions
  st_rotate_cw/2    90-degree clockwise rotation of a direction
  st_rotate_ccw/2   90-degree counter-clockwise rotation of a direction
  st_opposite/2     reverse a direction (negate both components)
  st_normalize/3    compute unit step direction between two cells
  st_path/3         follow a list of directions from a start cell
  st_first/5        first cell in a direction with a given value
  st_to_edge/4      count steps until the grid boundary

Private helpers:
  st_dims_/3             row and column count from a grid
  st_ray_acc_/6          reverse-accumulating ray traversal
  st_ray_to_acc_/8       ray traversal stopping at a value
  st_path_acc_/4         reverse-accumulating path follower
  st_first_acc_/7        step-by-step value search
  st_to_edge_acc_/6      step counter until boundary

Dependencies:
  library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, append/3, reverse/2
  library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3

Design notes:

st_step/3 is a pure arithmetic predicate with no backtracking potential.

st_ray/4 and st_ray_to/5 accumulate cells in reverse order (prepend each
new cell) and call reverse/2 once at the end. This gives O(N) performance
instead of O(N^2) from repeated append. The accumulator predicate is private.

st_walk/4 calls st_ray/4 and prepends the start cell; no independent logic.

st_dirs4 and st_dirs8 are deterministic constant predicates returning
hard-coded direction lists. They use no library imports.

st_rotate_cw and st_rotate_ccw each use a single is/2 expression pair.
CW rotation: (DR,DC) -> (DC,-DR); CCW: (DR,DC) -> (-DC,DR).
Both formulas are verified against all four cardinal directions.

st_normalize/3 uses explicit if-then-else chains instead of sign/1 because
sign/1 returns -1.0/0.0/1.0 (floats), which would not unify with the
integer direction components used throughout the pack.

st_path/3 uses an accumulator private predicate (st_path_acc_/4). The base
clause carries a cut to prevent a spurious choicepoint when the direction
list is empty.

st_first/5 and st_to_edge/4 use step-by-step recursion with between/3 for
bounds checking. Both fail gracefully when the answer does not exist.

END OF PART ARCH-73


PART ARCH-74 - PIVOT PACK (Layer 87)

Location:  packs/pivot/
Module:    pivot
Prefix:    pv_
Layer:     87
WP:        108

Files:
  packs/pivot/pack.pl              - pack metadata
  packs/pivot/prolog/pivot.pl      - 14 exported pv_* predicates
  packs/pivot/test/test_pivot.pl   - 42 PLUnit acceptance tests

Exports:
  pv_centroid/2           integer centroid of a cell list
  pv_to_rel/3             convert absolute cell to pivot-relative offset
  pv_from_rel/3           convert pivot-relative offset to absolute cell
  pv_rotate_cell_cw/3     rotate one cell 90 degrees CW around pivot
  pv_rotate_cells_cw/3    rotate a cell list 90 degrees CW around pivot
  pv_rotate_cells_180/3   rotate a cell list 180 degrees around pivot
  pv_rotate_cells_ccw/3   rotate a cell list 90 degrees CCW around pivot
  pv_reflect_cells_h/3    reflect cell list horizontally around pivot column
  pv_reflect_cells_v/3    reflect cell list vertically around pivot row
  pv_reflect_cells_diag/3      reflect across main diagonal through pivot
  pv_reflect_cells_antidiag/3  reflect across anti-diagonal through pivot
  pv_orbit/3              sorted D4 orbit of one cell around pivot
  pv_sym_closure/3        sorted D4 symmetry closure of a cell list
  pv_stamp_at/5           paint offset cells at pivot position in a grid

Private helpers:
  pv_sum_rc_/3                  row/col accumulator for pv_centroid
  pv_rotate_cell_180_/3         single-cell 180-degree rotation
  pv_rotate_cell_ccw_/3         single-cell CCW rotation
  pv_reflect_cell_h_/3          single-cell horizontal reflection
  pv_reflect_cell_v_/3          single-cell vertical reflection
  pv_reflect_cell_diag_/3       single-cell diagonal reflection
  pv_reflect_cell_antidiag_/3   single-cell anti-diagonal reflection
  pv_set_cell_/5                write a value at Grid[R][C]

Dependencies:
  library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, append/3, reverse/2
  library(apply): maplist/3, foldl/4

Design notes:

The pivot pack extends the sym pack (sy_*) from whole-grid transforms to
cell-list transforms centered at any pivot position. The sym pack applies
isometries to an entire grid; the pivot pack applies the same D4 group
operations to a sorted list of R-C cells relative to an arbitrary pivot.

All 8 D4 transforms are implemented as private single-cell helpers (one
clause each). The public list-level predicates map these helpers over the
input with maplist/3, giving O(N) performance.

pv_centroid uses foldl/4 with a private accumulator to sum all R and C
values, then divides with integer // to produce the floor average.

pv_orbit calls all 7 non-identity D4 transforms plus identity, collects
the results in a list, and calls sort/2 to deduplicate. For cells on
symmetry axes (DR=0, DC=0, |DR|=|DC|, DR=-DC), some transforms coincide
and the orbit has fewer than 8 elements.

pv_sym_closure uses findall/3 to collect all orbit members for every cell
in Cells, then sort/2 to deduplicate.

pv_stamp_at handles out-of-bounds offsets silently by checking bounds
before calling pv_set_cell_. The base clause carries a cut.

pv_set_cell_ uses length/2 and append/3 twice to split and reassemble the
grid at the target row and column, giving O(NR + NC) per cell write.

END OF PART ARCH-74


PART ARCH-75 - PROJECT PACK (Layer 88, Work Package 109)

Version: v68
What changed: Added PART ARCH-75 for the project pack at Layer 88.

Layer 88 sits above the pivot pack (Layer 87) and provides axis-projection and shadow-casting operations on grids.

MODULE: project
PREFIX: pj_
LAYER: 88
WORK PACKAGE: 109
FILE: packs/project/prolog/project.pl

Dependencies: library(lists), library(apply). No other PrologAI pack dependencies.

The project pack provides 14 predicates in four functional areas:

Area 1 - Shadow Casting (PJ-PJ-001 through PJ-PJ-005):
Each non-BG cell casts its value through BG cells in one direction until hitting another non-BG cell or the grid boundary. Four directional variants (down, up, left, right) plus a direction-dispatch predicate.

Area 2 - Occupied Axis Detection (PJ-PJ-006 through PJ-PJ-007):
Identifying which rows and columns contain at least one non-BG cell. Returns sorted index lists.

Area 3 - Cell Counting and Projection (PJ-PJ-008 through PJ-PJ-011):
Counting non-BG cells per row and per column, and collapsing a 2D grid to a 1D row or column by taking the first non-BG value along each axis.

Area 4 - Boundary Finding (PJ-PJ-012 through PJ-PJ-014):
Finding the topmost, bottommost, or leftmost non-BG cell index within a given column or row.

The core algorithm shared by all shadow predicates is pj_prop_fwd_: a linear scan that propagates the most recent non-BG value forward through BG cells. Column operations extract a column as a list, apply pj_prop_fwd_, and write back. Row operations apply pj_prop_fwd_ directly to each row list.


END OF PART ARCH-75


PART ARCH-76 - DIFF PACK (Layer 89)

Pack: diff
Prefix: df_
Layer: 89
Work Package: 110
File: packs/diff/prolog/diff.pl

The diff pack occupies Layer 89, above the project pack (Layer 88) and below
future higher-order analysis packs.

Purpose: multi-pair grid difference analysis.

The diff pack provides two families of operations.

Family 1 - Single-pair cell analysis (DF-DF-001 through DF-DF-006):
Comparing two grids of the same size to find changed cells, added cells,
removed cells, recolored cells, stable cells, and palette additions/losses.
These predicates operate on one input-output pair.

Family 2 - Multi-pair contrastive analysis (DF-DF-007 through DF-DF-010):
Given a list of In-Out pairs, find which cells changed in EVERY pair
(df_common_diffs), which cells were stable in every pair (df_common_stable),
which cells were always added (df_always_added), and which were always removed
(df_always_removed). These predicates enable cross-pair pattern discovery.

Family 3 - Diff application and manipulation (DF-DF-011 through DF-DF-014):
Counting total changes, applying a diff list to a grid, inverting a diff
list, and filtering diffs by a goal predicate.

A diff term has the form diff(R, C, V1, V2): row index, column index, old
value, new value.

The internal helper df_dims_ extracts row and column bounds. The helper
df_set_cell_ performs single-cell replacement using append/3 decomposition.
All four multi-pair predicates use df_intersect_all_ to find the common
elements across a list of cell sets.

Dependencies: none. The diff pack is self-contained.


END OF PART ARCH-76


PART ARCH-77 - ORDER PACK (Layer 90)

Pack: order
Prefix: od_
Layer: 90
Work Package: 111
File: packs/order/prolog/order.pl

The order pack occupies Layer 90, above the diff pack (Layer 89).

Purpose: spatial ordering, ranking, and selection of objects.

The order pack operates on obj(Color, Cells) terms, where Cells is a sorted
list of r(R, C) cell coordinates. The pack provides four groups of operations.

Group 1 - Centroid computation (OD-OD-001):
od_centroid computes the integer floor centroid (CR, CC) of an object's cell
list. It is the foundational operation used internally by all other predicates.

Group 2 - Full-list sorting (OD-OD-002 through OD-OD-005):
od_sort_row, od_sort_col, od_reading_order, and od_sort_color sort an entire
list of objects. The sorting key is computed for each object, keysort is
applied, and the keys are stripped. od_reading_order uses a compound R-C key
so that Prolog's standard term ordering sorts by row first, then by column.

Group 3 - Extremal selection (OD-OD-006 through OD-OD-009):
od_topmost, od_bottommost, od_leftmost, and od_rightmost select the single
object at an extreme position. These are implemented as first or last elements
of the corresponding sorted lists.

Group 4 - Index and proximity access (OD-OD-010 through OD-OD-014):
od_nth_row and od_nth_col retrieve the N-th object in a spatial ordering.
od_nearest and od_farthest select the object whose centroid has the minimum
or maximum Manhattan distance to a reference grid position. od_rank_row
computes the 1-based rank of a specific object within the row ordering.

Dependencies: none. The order pack is self-contained. It implements its own
centroid computation over raw r(R, C) cell lists without importing the obj pack.

Internal helpers: od_sum_rc_ (foldl accumulator for centroid sums), od_strip_
(key stripping for simple keys), od_strip2_ (key stripping for compound keys),
od_rank_find_ (recursive 1-based position search using == comparison).


END OF PART ARCH-77


PART ARCH-78 - ASSEMBLE PACK (Layer 91, Work Package 112)

File: packs/assemble/prolog/assemble.pl
Module: assemble
Prefix: as_
Layer: 91 (above order pack at Layer 90)

Purpose: Grid assembly, concatenation, and composition. Provides 14 predicates
for combining grids, scaling, cropping, framing, and compositing operations
that are not provided by any existing pack.

Distinction from existing packs:
- tile pack (Layer 81): repeats the SAME tile N times. The assemble pack joins
  DIFFERENT grids (as_hcat, as_vcat, as_grid_of).
- seek pack (Layer 76): has sk_upscale (each cell expands to K x K block) but
  not downscaling. The assemble pack adds as_downscale (K x K blocks collapse
  to one cell by majority vote).
- grid pack (Layer 44): has gd_overlay (overlays non-background cells) but not
  unconditional paste. The assemble pack adds as_paste (always overwrites).
- window pack (Layer 79): has wn_extract (extract sub-grid) but not
  crop-or-pad-to-size. The assemble pack adds as_crop_to.
- sym pack (Layer 75): has reflection predicates but not mirror-concatenation.
  The assemble pack adds as_flip_h_cat and as_flip_v_cat (reflect and join).

Predicate groups:
Group 1 - Multi-grid joining (AS-AS-001 through AS-AS-003):
as_hcat joins a list of grids side by side. as_vcat stacks a list of grids
vertically. as_grid_of assembles a 2D matrix of grids into one combined grid
by applying as_hcat to each row then as_vcat to the row strips.

Group 2 - Scaling and resizing (AS-AS-004, AS-AS-014):
as_downscale reduces K x K non-overlapping blocks to single cells by majority
vote. as_crop_to pads with a background color or crops to an exact target size.

Group 3 - Framing and centering (AS-AS-005, AS-AS-006):
as_border adds a W-cell wide colored frame on all sides. as_center_in places
a smaller grid at the integer floor center of a larger canvas.

Group 4 - Quadrant extraction (AS-AS-007):
as_quarter extracts one of four named quadrants (tl/tr/bl/br) using floor
division to locate the boundary row and column.

Group 5 - Mirror-concatenation (AS-AS-008, AS-AS-009):
as_flip_h_cat concatenates a grid with its left-right mirror. as_flip_v_cat
stacks a grid with its top-bottom mirror.

Group 6 - Interleaving (AS-AS-010, AS-AS-011):
as_zip_h interleaves columns from two same-size grids. as_zip_v interleaves
rows. Both use the shared helper as_zip_lists_.

Group 7 - Paste and mask (AS-AS-012, AS-AS-013):
as_paste unconditionally overwrites a sub-region. as_mask_fill replaces cells
at positions where a same-size mask grid is non-zero.

Dependencies: none. The assemble pack is self-contained; it imports only
standard library predicates.

Internal helpers: as_make_row_ (N-element uniform list), as_make_grid_ (N-row
uniform grid), as_zip_lists_ (element-wise interleaving), as_crop_ (sub-grid
extraction by bounds), as_qbounds_ (quadrant row/column bounds), as_paste_row_
(single-row paste), as_majority_ (most common value in a list).


END OF PART ARCH-78


PART ARCH-79 - REGION PACK (Layer 92, rg_* prefix)

Work Package 113

Layer: 92
Pack: region
Prefix: rg_
Source: packs/region/prolog/region.pl
Tests: packs/region/test/test_region.pl

Purpose: divide a grid into rectangular sections by finding rows and columns
where every cell equals a designated separator value (Sep). Provides predicates
to identify separator rows/columns, compute non-separator spans, cut grids into
lists of sub-grids along either axis, assemble a 2D matrix of all sections, and
extract the specific section containing a given cell coordinate.

The section identification strategy: a row is a separator row if every cell
equals Sep. A column is a separator column if every cell equals Sep. The
resulting non-separator regions are contiguous bands between (and possibly
before the first or after the last) separator rows/columns.

Spans representation: each horizontal or vertical section is represented as an
R0-R1 inclusive pair giving its start and end index. The helper
rg_spans_from_seps_/4 computes this list from a sorted separator index list.

Predicate groups:

Group 1 - Separator detection (RG-RG-001 through RG-RG-004):
rg_is_sep_row and rg_is_sep_col are cell-level tests. rg_sep_rows and
rg_sep_cols collect all separator indices.

Group 2 - Span computation (RG-RG-005, RG-RG-006):
rg_spans_h and rg_spans_v delegate to rg_spans_from_seps_ to convert separator
index lists into non-separator span pairs.

Group 3 - Grid splitting (RG-RG-007, RG-RG-008):
rg_cut_h and rg_cut_v split the grid into lists of sub-grids along their
respective axes. Each sub-grid excludes its bounding separator row/column.

Group 4 - Section matrix (RG-RG-009 through RG-RG-011):
rg_sections assembles a 2D list-of-lists by first cutting horizontally then
cutting each strip vertically. rg_section_h and rg_section_v retrieve a
specific section by 1-indexed number.

Group 5 - Section counting (RG-RG-012, RG-RG-013):
rg_count_h and rg_count_v return the number of sections along each axis.

Group 6 - Region query (RG-RG-014):
rg_region extracts the sub-grid containing a specific cell coordinate pair
(R, C), combining rg_spans_h, rg_spans_v, and rg_extract_subgrid_.

Dependencies: none. The region pack is self-contained; it imports only
standard library predicates (nth0/3, numlist/3 from library(lists);
maplist/2, maplist/3, include/3 from library(apply)).

Internal helpers: rg_spans_from_seps_ (recursive span building from separator
list), rg_find_span_ (linear search for a span containing a given index),
rg_extract_subgrid_ (sub-grid extraction by inclusive row and column bounds).

Relationship to existing packs:
The crop pack (Layer 45) splits at a fixed index.
The tile pack (Layer 81) splits into equal bands.
The region pack splits at CONTENT-defined separator rows/columns.
These are complementary; none replaces another.


END OF PART ARCH-79


PART ARCH-80 - NEIGHBOR PACK (Layer 93, nb_* prefix)

Work Package 114

Layer: 93
Pack: neighbor
Prefix: nb_
Source: packs/neighbor/prolog/neighbor.pl
Tests: packs/neighbor/test/test_neighbor.pl

Purpose: local cell neighborhood analysis. Each predicate operates at the
level of individual cells and their immediate surroundings, providing
raw neighbor access, boundary classification, value counting, color
contact queries, grid-modifying flood fill, and single-step dilation.

This layer is distinct from:
- The connect pack (Layer 64): returns cell-set regions (cc_flood4 returns
  a list of r(R,C) terms, not a modified grid; cc_border_cells takes an
  existing region as input, not a background color).
- The trace pack (Layer 82): tr_outline works on a specific region; tr_edge_cells
  returns cells on the grid border only, not relative to a background color.
- The scene pack (Layer 37): sc_* predicates work on whole obj(Color,Cells) objects.
- The obj pack (Layer 69): obj_* predicates analyze whole objects.

The neighbor pack fills the gap of cell-level local operations.

Predicate groups:

Group 1 - Raw neighbor access (NB-NB-001, NB-NB-002):
nb_4neighbors and nb_8neighbors return nb(Row,Col,Val) lists. The nb/3 term
carries both the coordinate and the value in a single structured term.

Group 2 - Boundary and interior classification (NB-NB-003 through NB-NB-006):
nb_is_boundary and nb_is_interior test individual cells relative to a Bg color
treating OOB as Bg. nb_boundary_cells and nb_interior_cells collect these
across the entire grid using findall + between/3 iteration.

Group 3 - Neighbor value analysis (NB-NB-007 through NB-NB-009):
nb_count_same, nb_count_diff, and nb_adjacent_colors analyze the value
distribution among 4-neighbors of a single cell.

Group 4 - Color-level contour and contact (NB-NB-010 through NB-NB-012):
nb_contour finds all cells of a specific color that touch something different.
nb_color_touches tests for any adjacency between two colors.
nb_touching_pairs enumerates all such adjacency pairs.

Group 5 - Grid-modifying operations (NB-NB-013, NB-NB-014):
nb_flood_fill produces a modified grid (not a cell list) by replacing the
seed color throughout its 4-connected component with FillVal.
nb_dilate expands a color region by one cell in all 4-connected directions.

Dependencies: none. The neighbor pack imports only nth0/3, nth0/4, and
member/2 from library(lists). No PrologAI pack is imported.

Internal helpers: nb_cell_ (cell value lookup), nb_set_cell_ (cell value
replacement using nth0/4 in insertion mode), nb_set_cells_ (bulk replacement
over a list of R-C pairs), nb_fill_step_ (recursive worklist flood fill step).


END OF PART ARCH-80


END OF PART ARCH-80


PART ARCH-81 - PERMUTE PACK (Layer 94, pm_* prefix)

Work Package 115

Layer: 94
Pack: permute
Prefix: pm_
Source: packs/permute/prolog/permute.pl
Tests: packs/permute/test/test_permute.pl

Purpose: arbitrary reordering, swapping, cyclic shifting, permutation
discovery, lexicographic sorting, and insertion or deletion of rows and
columns in a grid. All predicates treat the grid as a list of rows, where
each row is a list of cell values.

This layer is distinct from:
- The crop pack (Layer 45): trims a rectangular sub-grid by fixed bounds.
- The tile pack (Layer 81): splits a grid into equal-sized bands.
- The region pack (Layer 92): splits at content-defined separator lines.
- The flip pack (Layer 20): reflects rows or columns in fixed orientations.
- The rotate pack (Layer 21): rotates by multiples of 90 degrees.
The permute pack handles general index permutations that none of the above
cover.

Predicate groups:

Group 1 - Direct permutation (PM-PM-001, PM-PM-002):
pm_permute_rows and pm_permute_cols apply an explicit index list, where
the caller supplies the desired order. The same mechanism underlies all
swap and cycle operations.

Group 2 - Pairwise swap (PM-PM-003, PM-PM-004):
pm_swap_rows and pm_swap_cols exchange exactly two indices. pm_swap_cols
is implemented by constructing a swap permutation and delegating to
pm_permute_cols, avoiding a separate code path.

Group 3 - Cyclic shift (PM-PM-005, PM-PM-006):
pm_cycle_rows and pm_cycle_cols move the last N elements to the front after
modular reduction. Both predicates use append/3 for the split-and-rejoin.

Group 4 - Permutation discovery (PM-PM-007, PM-PM-008):
pm_find_row_perm and pm_find_col_perm infer the permutation that transforms
Grid1 into Grid2. Internal helpers pm_first_row_idx_ and pm_first_col_idx_
use nth0 and between with cut for first-match semantics.

Group 5 - Lexicographic sort (PM-PM-009, PM-PM-010):
pm_sort_rows delegates directly to msort. pm_sort_cols extracts column
lists, sorts them with msort, then reconstructs the grid row-by-row from
the sorted column lists.

Group 6 - Structural editing (PM-PM-011 through PM-PM-014):
pm_insert_row and pm_delete_row add or remove a complete row using append
and nth0/4. pm_insert_col and pm_delete_col add or remove a single element
from every row using maplist with append or nth0/4.

Dependencies: none. The permute pack imports nth0/3, nth0/4, numlist/3,
append/2, and append/3 from library(lists); maplist/2, maplist/3, and
maplist/4 from library(apply). No PrologAI pack is imported.

Internal helpers: pm_col_ (extract a column as a list), pm_first_row_idx_
(find the first index of a matching row), pm_first_col_idx_ (find the first
index of a matching column).

END OF PART ARCH-81



END OF PART ARCH-81


PART ARCH-82 - GRAVITY PACK (Layer 95, gv_* prefix)

Work Package 116

Layer: 95
Pack: gravity
Prefix: gv_
Source: packs/gravity/prolog/gravity.pl
Tests: packs/gravity/test/test_gravity.pl

Purpose: directional cell-sliding and gravity operations. Non-Bg cells slide
through background in a chosen direction until reaching a wall (another non-Bg
cell) or the grid boundary. Color-specific variants restrict movement to one
color while treating all other non-Bg cells as immovable walls.

This layer is distinct from:
- The morph pack (Layer 84): mo_dilate and mo_erode expand or shrink regions
  in all four directions simultaneously, not unidirectionally.
- The project pack (Layer 88): pj_shadow_* propagates values into background
  cells but does not compact or gather the source cells.
- The flip pack (Layer 20) and rotate pack (Layer 21): fixed orientation
  transforms that rearrange all cells, not selective sliding.
The gravity pack is the only pack that simulates physical falling or
directional compaction of non-Bg cells.

Predicate groups:

Group 1 - Single-list packing (GV-GV-001 through GV-GV-004):
gv_pack_row_left, gv_pack_row_right, gv_pack_col_up, and gv_pack_col_down
operate on a single list of values (a row or column). They separate non-Bg
from Bg cells using include/3 and reconstruct the list with non-Bg values
compacted to one end and Bg padding filling the other end.

Group 2 - Full-grid directional gravity (GV-GV-005 through GV-GV-008):
gv_fall_left and gv_fall_right apply gv_pack_row_left and gv_pack_row_right
to each row independently using maplist. gv_fall_down and gv_fall_up use
an internal transpose helper (gv_transpose_) to convert the column-wise
operation into a row-wise one, apply packing, then transpose back.

Group 3 - Direction dispatch (GV-GV-009):
gv_fall_dir uses a single if-then-else clause for deterministic dispatch to
the appropriate gv_fall_* predicate, avoiding multi-clause choicepoints.

Group 4 - Color-specific gravity (GV-GV-010 through GV-GV-013):
These predicates use the internal helpers gv_take_seg_, gv_pack_seg_left_,
gv_pack_seg_right_, gv_split_pack_left_, and gv_split_pack_right_ to split
each row (or transposed column) at wall cells (cells that are neither Bg nor
Color) and pack Color cells within each segment independently. This allows
Color cells to slide to one end of a segment without passing through walls.

Group 5 - Color-direction dispatch (GV-GV-014):
gv_fall_color_dir uses a single if-then-else clause for deterministic dispatch
to the appropriate gv_fall_color_* predicate.

Dependencies: none. The gravity pack imports nth0/3, numlist/3, append/2, and
append/3 from library(lists); and include/3 and maplist/2,3 from library(apply).
No PrologAI pack is imported.

Internal helpers: gv_transpose_ (column-as-row transposition), gv_take_seg_
(collect a contiguous Bg/Color segment), gv_pack_seg_left_ (pack segment with
Color at left), gv_pack_seg_right_ (pack segment with Color at right),
gv_split_pack_left_ (recursive row splitter for leftward Color gravity),
gv_split_pack_right_ (recursive row splitter for rightward Color gravity).

END OF PART ARCH-82



PART ARCH-83: COUNT PACK - LAYER 96

Work Package: 117
Pack name: count
Prefix: cn_
Layer: 96
Location: packs/count/

Purpose: Provide predicates for counting cell values, computing frequency
histograms, comparing grids cell-by-cell, and tallying region colors. Serves
tasks that require understanding the distribution of values in a grid or the
relationship between two grids.

Predicate groups:

Group 1 - Value counting (CN-CN-001 through CN-CN-003):
cn_by_value counts occurrences in a flat list. cn_color_count flattens the
grid and delegates to cn_by_value. cn_histogram uses msort to sort all values,
then run-length encoding via cn_count_runs_ and cn_split_pairs_ to produce
parallel Colors and Counts lists.

Group 2 - Frequency extremes (CN-CN-004 through CN-CN-005):
cn_max_color and cn_min_color call cn_histogram then max_list or min_list to
find the extreme count. nth0/3 locates the first index where the extreme
count appears, then nth0/3 retrieves the corresponding color. The cut (!) after
nth0 ensures determinism when counts are tied.

Group 3 - Row and column presence (CN-CN-006 through CN-CN-007):
cn_color_rows uses include/3 with a member/2 test to filter rows. cn_color_cols
enumerates column indices via numlist/3, uses cn_extract_col_ (which applies
nth0/3 to every row via maplist) to build each column, tests membership, and
counts matching indices.

Group 4 - Distinct value counts (CN-CN-008 through CN-CN-009):
cn_row_distinct retrieves the row with nth0, sorts to deduplicate, and counts.
cn_col_distinct extracts the column with cn_extract_col_, sorts, and counts.
Both use sort/2 which removes duplicates by contract in SWI-Prolog.

Group 5 - Grid total (CN-CN-010):
cn_grid_total delegates to the cn_grid_dims_ helper which uses length/2 on the
grid and its first row. Total is Rows * Cols.

Group 6 - Cell comparison (CN-CN-011 through CN-CN-012):
cn_equal_cells uses cn_compare_row_ (which calls cn_compare_cell_ via maplist)
to produce per-cell flags, flattens, and sums via sum_list/2. cn_diff_cells
computes total minus equal.

Group 7 - Region color (CN-CN-013 through CN-CN-014):
cn_region_color pattern-matches the first r(R,C) cell of a region and looks up
Grid[R][C] with two nth0 calls. cn_regions_per_color maps cn_region_color over
all regions to produce a color list, then folds cn_tally_ over that list. The
tally uses select/3 to find and update an existing entry or prepend a new one.

Dependencies: none. The count pack imports member/2, nth0/3, max_list/2,
min_list/2, numlist/3, sum_list/2, and select/3 from library(lists); and
maplist/2, maplist/3, include/3, and foldl/4 from library(apply). No PrologAI
pack is imported.

Internal helpers: cn_grid_dims_ (row and column measurement), cn_count_same_
(run-length leading count), cn_count_runs_ (run-length encoding to pairs),
cn_split_pairs_ (pair list unzip), cn_compare_cell_ (equality flag),
cn_compare_row_ (row-level flag list), cn_tally_ (association-list increment),
cn_extract_col_ (column extraction by index).

END OF PART ARCH-83


PART ARCH-84: STRIPE PACK - LAYER 97

Work Package: 118
Pack name: stripe
Prefix: sr_
Layer: 97
Location: packs/stripe/

Purpose: Provide predicates for detecting rows and columns that are entirely
one value (uniform stripes), listing non-uniform rows and columns, filling
individual or multiple rows and columns with a value, and filling the
intersections of row and column sets.

Predicate groups:

Group 1 - Single-stripe detection (SR-SR-001 through SR-SR-002):
sr_uniform_row and sr_uniform_col each extract the target row or column with
nth0 or sr_col_, unify the head cell as Color, and test that all cells equal
Color via maplist(=(Color), ...). The test fails if the row or column contains
any other value.

Group 2 - Uniform index lists (SR-SR-003 through SR-SR-004):
sr_uniform_rows and sr_uniform_cols enumerate all row or column indices via
numlist/3, then use include/3 with sr_uniform_row or sr_uniform_col as the
filter goal to collect matching indices.

Group 3 - Stripe pair lists (SR-SR-005 through SR-SR-006):
sr_all_stripe_rows and sr_all_stripe_cols delegate to the internal helpers
sr_stripe_row_pairs_ and sr_stripe_col_pairs_. Each helper iterates the index
list and uses if-then-else to conditionally add R-Color or C-Color pairs.
This avoids choicepoints from multiple clause heads.

Group 4 - Mixed index lists (SR-SR-007 through SR-SR-008):
sr_mixed_rows and sr_mixed_cols use include/3 with a negation-as-failure goal
(\+ sr_uniform_row or \+ sr_uniform_col) to collect non-uniform indices.

Group 5 - Single fill (SR-SR-009 through SR-SR-010):
sr_fill_row delegates to sr_fill_row_, which builds a FilledRow of all Color
via length/2 and maplist(=(Color), ...), then uses the internal
sr_replace_nth_ helper to substitute that row in the grid list. sr_fill_col
delegates to sr_fill_col_, which maps sr_replace_nth_ over every row.
sr_replace_nth_ is deterministic because its base case carries a cut.

Group 6 - Multi-fill (SR-SR-011 through SR-SR-012):
sr_fill_rows and sr_fill_cols use if-then-else recursion: when the index list
is empty, return the grid unchanged; otherwise fill one index and recurse.
This eliminates choicepoints from multi-clause dispatch.

Group 7 - Cross product and cross fill (SR-SR-013 through SR-SR-014):
sr_cross_cells calls sr_cross_product_, which maps each row R to a list of
r(R,C) terms (one per column C) and appends the sublists. sr_cross_fill is
a two-step composition: sr_fill_rows produces an intermediate grid with all
listed rows filled, then sr_fill_cols fills all listed columns.

Dependencies: none. The stripe pack imports nth0/3, numlist/3, and append/2
from library(lists); and maplist/2, maplist/3, and include/3 from
library(apply). No PrologAI pack is imported.

Internal helpers: sr_col_ (column extraction), sr_replace_nth_ (deterministic
list element replacement), sr_fill_row_ (row replacement in a grid),
sr_fill_col_ (column replacement in a grid), sr_stripe_row_pairs_ (uniform
row pair collector), sr_stripe_col_pairs_ (uniform column pair collector),
sr_cross_product_ (Cartesian r(R,C) list builder).

END OF PART ARCH-84


PART ARCH-85: DIAGONAL PACK - LAYER 98

Work Package: 119
Pack name: diagonal
Prefix: dg_
Layer: 98
Location: packs/diagonal/

Purpose: Provide predicates for extracting cell-value lists along diagonals
and anti-diagonals of any 2D grid, filling individual diagonals and anti-
diagonals with a color, computing the diagonal and anti-diagonal membership
index of any cell, and testing whether a diagonal or anti-diagonal is uniform.

Definitions: A diagonal is a set of cells sharing a constant C-R offset. An
anti-diagonal is a set sharing a constant R+C sum. The main diagonal has
offset 0. The main anti-diagonal has sum NC-1 (through the top-right corner).

Predicate groups:

Group 1 - Value extraction (DG-DG-001 through DG-DG-004):
dg_main_diag calls dg_diag_cells_(NR, NC, 0) then maps dg_cell_at_ over the
resulting R-C pairs. dg_anti_diag uses Sum = NC-1. dg_nth_diag and
dg_nth_anti_diag use the caller-supplied offset or sum directly. dg_diag_cells_
and dg_anti_diag_cells_ use numlist/3 and include/3 to collect valid R-C pairs
within the grid bounds.

Group 2 - Complete diagonal enumeration (DG-DG-005 through DG-DG-006):
dg_all_diags builds the offset range [-(NR-1) .. NC-1] with numlist/3 and maps
dg_nth_diag over it. dg_all_anti_diags builds the sum range [0 .. NR+NC-2]
and maps dg_nth_anti_diag over it.

Group 3 - Diagonal fill (DG-DG-007 through DG-DG-010):
Each fill predicate collects the target diagonal's R-C pairs, then calls
dg_fill_cells_. dg_fill_cells_ uses if-then-else for deterministic dispatch:
when the cell list is empty it returns the grid unchanged; otherwise it calls
dg_replace_cell_ on the first cell and recurses.

Group 4 - Cell index membership (DG-DG-011 through DG-DG-012):
dg_cell_diag and dg_cell_anti_diag are single-step grid_arithmetic: N is C-R
and N is R+C respectively.

Group 5 - Uniformity tests (DG-DG-013 through DG-DG-014):
dg_uniform_diag and dg_uniform_anti_diag extract the target diagonal with
dg_nth_diag or dg_nth_anti_diag, unify the head element as Color, and test
that all elements equal Color via maplist(=(Color), ...).

Dependencies: none. The diagonal pack imports nth0/3, numlist/3, and append/2
from library(lists); and maplist/2, maplist/3, and include/3 from library(apply).
No PrologAI pack is imported.

Internal helpers: dg_dims_ (row and column count), dg_cell_at_ (value lookup),
dg_replace_nth_list_ (deterministic list element replacement with cut),
dg_replace_cell_ (single-cell grid mutation with cut after nth0),
dg_fill_cells_ (iterative cell fill with if-then-else),
dg_diag_cells_ (valid R-C pairs for diagonal offset N),
dg_anti_diag_cells_ (valid R-C pairs for anti-diagonal sum N).

END OF PART ARCH-85

PART ARCH-86: RECUR PACK (Layer 99, Work Package 120)

Location: packs/recur/prolog/recur.pl
Pack file: packs/recur/pack.pl
Tests: packs/recur/test/test_recur.pl
Module name: recur
Export prefix: rc_

Group 1 - Arithmetic sequence generation and detection (RC-RC-001 through RC-RC-003):
rc_arith generates a list of N terms using numlist/3 for the index list and
maplist/3 with a lambda to compute Start + I * Step. rc_arith_step extracts
the common difference from the first two elements, then verifies all subsequent
pairs using the recursive helper rc_check_step_ (which has a cut on its
single-element base case to avoid a choicepoint). rc_is_arith delegates
entirely to rc_arith_step.

Group 2 - Repetition period detection and generation (RC-RC-004 through RC-RC-006):
rc_repeat creates N identical copies of Unit using length/2 (built-in, not
imported) and maplist/3, then flattens with append/2. rc_period uses between/3
(built-in) to iterate candidate period lengths P, filters by divisibility, extracts
a candidate prefix with append/3, and verifies with rc_repeat. A cut after the
first successful match returns the minimal period. rc_is_periodic delegates to
rc_period.

Group 3 - Sequence continuation (RC-RC-007 through RC-RC-008):
rc_next_arith computes the step with rc_arith_step, finds the last element with
the internal helper rc_last_, then calls rc_arith to generate N more terms.
rc_next_repeat finds the period with rc_period, computes the offset as
length(Seq) mod length(Unit), and maps over 1..N using numlist/3 and maplist/3
with a lambda that computes (Offset + I - 1) mod P and indexes into Unit with nth0.

Group 4 - Extension predicates (RC-RC-009 through RC-RC-010):
rc_extend_arith and rc_extend_repeat call the corresponding next predicate and
append the result to the original sequence with append/3.

Group 5 - Cycle indexing (RC-RC-011):
rc_cycle_nth uses (N-1) mod length(Unit) to compute the 0-based index and
retrieves the element with nth0/3.

Group 6 - Pair-wise zip (RC-RC-012):
rc_zip_with uses two-clause recursion: a base case for empty lists and a recursive
case that calls Goal(A, B, C) with call/3. No choicepoint warning because the
two heads ([] vs [_|_]) are mutually exclusive.

Group 7 - Difference predicates (RC-RC-013 through RC-RC-014):
rc_diff_list has a cut on its single-element base case to prevent a choicepoint.
rc_const_diffs calls rc_diff_list, unifies the head as Step, and tests all
remaining differences with maplist(=:=(Step), ...).

Dependencies: none. The recur pack imports nth0/3, numlist/3, append/2, and
append/3 from library(lists); and maplist/2 and maplist/3 from library(apply).
Built-ins used (not imported): length/2, between/3.
No PrologAI pack is imported.

Internal helpers: rc_check_step_ (verifies constant differences with cut on base
case), rc_last_ (last element of list with cut on base case).

END OF PART ARCH-86


PART ARCH-87: LINE PACK (Layer 100, li_* prefix)

Location: packs/line/prolog/line.pl
Layer: 100
Work Package: 121
Prefix: li_

The line pack occupies Layer 100 of the PrologAI cognitive substrate. It
provides straight-line segment operations for 2D integer-coordinate grids: cell
enumeration on horizontal, vertical, and 45-degree diagonal segments; grid
drawing; alignment and collinearity tests; and endpoint/gap queries.

Exported predicates (14, LI-LI-001 through LI-LI-014):

Group 1 - Segment cell enumeration (LI-LI-001 through LI-LI-003):
li_hline/4, li_vline/4, and li_diag_seg/5 enumerate the R-C cells on a
horizontal, vertical, or 45-degree diagonal segment respectively. li_hline and
li_vline use numlist/3 to generate the span of column or row indices and
maplist/3 with a unification lambda [X, RC]>>(RC = R-X) to build the R-C pairs
deterministically. li_diag_seg delegates to the internal li_diag_walk_ which
uses an if-then-else for determinism: the base case (at the endpoint) is the
then-branch; the recursive step is the else-branch.

Group 2 - Grid drawing (LI-LI-004 through LI-LI-006):
li_draw_h/6, li_draw_v/6, and li_draw_diag/7 call the corresponding
enumeration predicate and then pass the resulting cell list to li_fill_cells_.
li_fill_cells_ mutates the grid one cell at a time using the internal helpers
li_set_cell_ and li_replace_nth_. li_fill_cells_ uses if-then-else for
determinism; li_replace_nth_ uses a cut on its base case (index 0).

Group 3 - Alignment tests (LI-LI-007 through LI-LI-010):
li_same_row/4, li_same_col/4, li_same_diag/4, and li_same_anti/4 are pure
arithmetic tests. li_same_row checks R1 =:= R2; li_same_col checks C1 =:= C2;
li_same_diag checks C1-R1 =:= C2-R2; li_same_anti checks R1+C1 =:= R2+C2.
All are deterministic single-clause predicates.

Group 4 - Collinearity (LI-LI-011):
li_collinear/6 uses an if-then-else chain with four arms: same row, same
column, same diagonal (C-R), and same anti-diagonal (R+C). The if-then-else
chain commits to the first matching condition, leaving no choicepoints.

Group 5 - Endpoints (LI-LI-012):
li_endpoints/3 extracts the first element from the list head and walks to the
last element with the internal helper li_last_. li_last_ accumulates the last
seen element; a cut on the empty-list base case prevents a choicepoint.

Group 6 - Gap query (LI-LI-013):
li_gap/5 uses an if-then-else chain over four alignment types (row, column,
diagonal, anti-diagonal). For horizontal and vertical gaps, it uses numlist/3
and maplist/3 with unification lambdas. For diagonal and anti-diagonal gaps, it
delegates to li_diag_walk_ on the interior endpoints.

Group 7 - Line type classification (LI-LI-014):
li_line_type/5 uses an if-then-else chain with six arms: point, horizontal,
vertical, diagonal, anti_diagonal, other.

Dependencies: none. The line pack imports nth0/3, numlist/3, and append/2 from
library(lists); maplist/2 and maplist/3 from library(apply). Built-ins used
without import: length/2. No PrologAI pack is imported.

Internal helpers: li_dims_ (grid dimensions), li_cell_at_ (cell value lookup),
li_replace_nth_ (list element replacement, cut on base), li_set_cell_ (grid
cell mutation, cut after nth0), li_fill_cells_ (sequential cell fill, if-then-
else), li_diag_step_ (step direction for diagonal walk), li_diag_walk_ (walk
along 45-degree diagonal, if-then-else), li_last_ (last list element, cut on
base).

END OF PART ARCH-87


PART ARCH-88: RECT PACK (Layer 101, rt_* prefix)

Location: packs/rect/prolog/rect.pl
Layer: 101
Work Package: 122
Prefix: rt_

The rect pack occupies Layer 101 of the PrologAI cognitive substrate. It
provides rectangle operations for 2D integer-coordinate grids: cell enumeration
for solid rectangles, frames, and interiors; grid drawing for each region type;
containment tests; bounding box computation; corner extraction; solid/frame
testing; overlap detection; and scaling.

Exported predicates (14, RT-RT-001 through RT-RT-014):

Group 1 - Cell enumeration (RT-RT-001 through RT-RT-003):
rt_cells/5 generates all cells in the solid rectangle. It uses numlist/3 for
both axes, then maplist/4 with a row-level lambda that inner-maps with a
unification lambda [C, RC]>>(RC = R-C) to build R-C pairs without leaving
choicepoints. append/2 flattens the 2D list.

rt_border/5 computes the frame cells. It builds the top row, the bottom row
(if distinct from the top), and the inner left/right column segments (if the
rectangle is at least 3 rows tall). All four lists are concatenated and sorted
with sort/2 (built-in). The if-then-else guards for R2 > R1 and R2-R1 > 1
commit immediately, leaving no choicepoints.

rt_interior/5 uses a single if-then-else: if the rectangle has at least 3 rows
and 3 columns, it calls rt_cells on the inset rectangle; otherwise it unifies
the result with [].

Group 2 - Grid drawing (RT-RT-004 through RT-RT-006):
rt_draw/7, rt_draw_border/7, and rt_draw_interior/7 delegate to the
corresponding cell enumeration predicate and then pass the cell list to the
internal rt_fill_cells_. rt_fill_cells_ uses if-then-else for determinism and
calls rt_set_cell_ for each cell. rt_set_cell_ uses nth0/3 (cut after the
call to prevent backtracking) and rt_replace_nth_ (cut on the base case where
index is 0) to mutate one cell at a time.

Group 3 - Geometric queries (RT-RT-007 through RT-RT-009):
rt_area/5 computes (R2-R1+1)*(C2-C1+1) with arithmetic. rt_contains/6 is
a pure arithmetic test: R1 =< R, R =< R2, C1 =< C, C =< C2. rt_corners/5
unifies the result directly with [R1-C1, R1-C2, R2-C1, R2-C2].

Group 4 - Bounding box (RT-RT-010):
rt_bbox/5 uses two maplist/3 calls with unification lambdas [RC, R]>>(RC = R-_)
and [RC, C]>>(RC = _-C) to extract row and column indices separately. min_list/2
and max_list/2 (from library(lists)) compute the extents.

Group 5 - Color tests (RT-RT-011 through RT-RT-012):
rt_is_solid/6 enumerates rectangle cells with rt_cells, unifies Color with the
value of the first cell via the internal rt_cell_color_ helper (which uses two
nth0 calls), then uses forall/2 (built-in) to verify every cell has the same
value. rt_is_frame/6 is identical but uses rt_border for the cell list.

Group 6 - Overlap and scaling (RT-RT-013 through RT-RT-014):
rt_overlap/8 is a pure arithmetic test: row intervals overlap iff R1a =< R2b
and R2a >= R1b; column intervals overlap iff C1a =< C2b and C2a >= C1b.
rt_scale/7 computes the new bottom-right corner with grid_arithmetic:
R2New = R1 + (R2-R1)*Factor and C2New = C1 + (C2-C1)*Factor.

Dependencies: none. The rect pack imports nth0/3, numlist/3, append/2, append/3,
member/2, min_list/2, and max_list/2 from library(lists); maplist/2, maplist/3,
and maplist/4 from library(apply). Built-ins used without import: sort/2,
forall/2, length/2. No PrologAI pack is imported.

Internal helpers: rt_replace_nth_ (list element replacement, cut on index-0
base), rt_set_cell_ (grid cell mutation, cut after nth0), rt_fill_cells_
(sequential cell fill, if-then-else), rt_cell_color_ (cell value lookup).

END OF PART ARCH-88


PART ARCH-89: CLUSTER PACK (Layer 102, cl_* prefix)

Location: packs/cluster/prolog/cluster.pl
Layer: 102
Work Package: 123
Prefix: cl_

The cluster pack occupies Layer 102 of the PrologAI cognitive substrate. It
provides spatial proximity and grouping operations over sets of R-C cells: three
distance metrics, proximity filtering, nearest and farthest cell queries, centroid
and spread computation, color-based grouping, distance-sorted ordering, closest
and farthest pair detection, and band filtering.

Exported predicates (14, CL-CL-001 through CL-CL-014):

Group 1 - Distance metrics (CL-CL-001 through CL-CL-003):
cl_chebyshev/5, cl_manhattan/5, and cl_euclidean_sq/5 are pure arithmetic
predicates. cl_chebyshev uses max(abs(dR), abs(dC)); cl_manhattan uses
abs(dR) + abs(dC); cl_euclidean_sq uses dR*dR + dC*dC. All three are
deterministic single-clause predicates with no list operations.

Group 2 - Proximity filtering (CL-CL-004):
cl_within/5 uses include/3 from library(apply) with a lambda that computes
the Chebyshev distance to the query point and checks whether it is at most D.
The lambda is [Cell]>>(Cell = CR-CC, Dist is max(...), Dist =< D), which is
deterministic because the body is a conjunction with no disjunction.

Group 3 - Nearest and farthest queries (CL-CL-005 through CL-CL-006):
cl_nearest/4 and cl_farthest/4 both use a fold-style internal helper that
accumulates the best cell seen so far. The helper base case unifies the
accumulated best cell with the result; a cut prevents backtracking. The
recursive case uses if-then-else to update the accumulator deterministically.

Group 4 - Centroid and spread (CL-CL-007 through CL-CL-009):
cl_center/3 extracts rows and columns with maplist/3 using unification lambdas
[Cell, R]>>(Cell = R-_) and [Cell, C]>>(Cell = _-C). sum_list/2 accumulates
the totals; length/2 counts elements; round/1 (via is/2) rounds the averages.

cl_diameter/2 delegates to the internal cl_all_pairs_ to enumerate all
unordered pairs, then uses maplist/3 with a lambda extracting pair components
via [Pair, Dist]>>(Pair = (PR1-PC1)-(PR2-PC2), ...) followed by max_list/2.
The single-cell base case has a cut.

cl_spread/3 uses the same row/column extraction lambdas as cl_center, then
computes bounding box dimensions with min_list/2 and max_list/2.

Group 5 - Color grouping (CL-CL-010):
cl_group_by_color/4 first maps over Cells to retrieve each cell's grid value
using two nested nth0 calls (lambda: [Cell, Color]>>(Cell = CR-CC, nth0(CR,
Grid, Row), nth0(CC, Row, Color))). sort/2 (built-in) gives the distinct
sorted color list. Then maplist/3 applies include/3 for each color with a
lambda that performs the same nth0 lookup and tests equality with Clr.

Group 6 - Sort by distance (CL-CL-011):
cl_sort_by_dist/4 pairs each cell with its Chebyshev distance using maplist/3,
then uses keysort/2 (built-in, stable) to sort by the distance key. maplist/3
with [Pair, Cell]>>(Pair = _-Cell) extracts the cells from the sorted pairs.

Group 7 - Pair extremes (CL-CL-012 through CL-CL-013):
cl_nearest_pair/3 and cl_farthest_pair/3 call cl_all_pairs_ then initialize
with the first pair and fold through the rest with cl_min_pair_ or cl_max_pair_
respectively. The fold helpers use if-then-else and cuts on their base cases.
The pair destructuring uses (PR1-PC1)-(PR2-PC2) to extract both endpoints.

Group 8 - Band filter (CL-CL-014):
cl_cells_in_band/6 uses include/3 with a lambda that tests R1 =< CR, CR =< R2,
C1 =< CC, CC =< C2. The lambda captures R1, R2, C1, C2 from the outer scope.

Internal helpers: cl_nearest_helper_ (fold for nearest cell, if-then-else with
cut on base case), cl_farthest_helper_ (fold for farthest cell), cl_all_pairs_
(all unordered pairs from a list, cuts on base cases), cl_min_pair_ (fold for
minimum-distance pair), cl_max_pair_ (fold for maximum-distance pair).

Dependencies: none. The cluster pack imports nth0/3, member/2, max_list/2,
min_list/2, sum_list/2, append/2, and append/3 from library(lists); maplist/2,
maplist/3, and include/3 from library(apply). Built-ins used without import:
sort/2, keysort/2, length/2. No PrologAI pack is imported.

END OF PART ARCH-89


PART ARCH-90: RAY PACK ARCHITECTURE (Layer 103)

Module: ray
File: packs/ray/prolog/ray.pl
Layer: 103
Prefix: ry_
Predicate count: 14 public, 5 internal helpers

Public predicates:
  ry_in_bounds/3          - bounds test for a single cell
  ry_cells_in_dir/6       - enumerate cells from origin in a direction
  ry_first_hit/7          - first obstacle cell in a direction
  ry_cast_clear/7         - background cells before first obstacle
  ry_distance_to_hit/7    - step count to first obstacle
  ry_distance_to_edge/6   - step count to grid boundary
  ry_is_clear/6           - test that all cells in direction are background
  ry_project/8            - cell N steps from origin in direction
  ry_dir_to_delta/3       - named direction to unit step pair
  ry_reflect_h/4          - reflect direction across horizontal axis
  ry_reflect_v/4          - reflect direction across vertical axis
  ry_los/6                - line-of-sight test between two cells
  ry_los_cells/6          - interior cells on a line segment
  ry_cast_all_4/5         - cast rays in all 4 compass directions

Internal helpers:
  ry_dims_/3              - extract NR and NC from a grid
  ry_cells_in_dir_/7      - recursive ray walker with explicit bounds
  ry_cell_val_/3          - value lookup at R-C cell coordinate
  ry_first_hit_/4         - linear scan for first non-Bg cell
  ry_take_while_bg_/4     - collect background prefix of a cell list
  ry_dist_hit_/5          - step counter to first non-Bg cell
  ry_diag_walk_/7         - recursive diagonal cell enumeration
  ry_cast_one_/8          - single-direction cast with none fallback

Imports from library(lists): nth0/3, numlist/3, member/2
Imports from library(apply): maplist/3
Built-ins used without import: length/2, forall/2

Design patterns:
  - All recursive walkers (ry_cells_in_dir_, ry_first_hit_, ry_take_while_bg_,
    ry_dist_hit_, ry_diag_walk_) use if-then-else for determinism; no two-clause
    recursion that would leave choicepoints.
  - ry_take_while_bg_ has a cut on the base case (empty list) to prevent a
    spurious choicepoint on the final call.
  - ry_dir_to_delta uses a single if-then-else chain so the predicate is
    deterministic when Dir is ground.
  - ry_cast_one_ uses soft-cut (if-then-else with ry_first_hit) so that the
    absence of an obstacle is handled cleanly without explicit failure.
  - ry_los_cells handles three alignment cases (horizontal, vertical, diagonal)
    with nested if-then-else; the Grid argument is accepted but not accessed,
    matching the interface style of other pack predicates that may use Grid.
  - ry_project is a pure arithmetic predicate with an in-bounds post-condition;
    it fails (rather than throwing) when the result is out of bounds.
  - maplist/3 with unification lambdas [C, RC]>>(RC = R-C) is used in
    ry_los_cells to build cell coordinate lists without leaving choicepoints.

Dependencies: none. The ray pack does not import any PrologAI pack.

END OF PART ARCH-90


PART ARCH-91: VEC2 PACK ARCHITECTURE (Layer 104)

Module: vec2
File: packs/vec2/prolog/vec2.pl
Layer: 104
Prefix: vv_
Predicate count: 14 public, 1 internal helper

Public predicates:
  vv_offset/6             - displacement vector between two cells
  vv_add/6               - apply displacement to a point
  vv_scale/5             - scale a vector by an integer factor
  vv_neg/4               - negate a vector
  vv_len_sq/3            - squared Euclidean length
  vv_manhattan/3         - L1 magnitude
  vv_chebyshev/3         - L-infinity magnitude
  vv_rot90_cw/4          - rotate 90 degrees clockwise
  vv_rot90_ccw/4         - rotate 90 degrees counter-clockwise
  vv_rot180/4            - rotate 180 degrees
  vv_dot/5               - dot product
  vv_cross/5             - 2D cross product (z-component)
  vv_parallel/4          - parallelism test
  vv_translate_region/4  - translate a list of R-C cells by a vector

Internal helpers:
  vv_translate_cell_/4   - translate one R-C cell by (DR,DC)

Imports from library(apply): maplist/3
No imports from library(lists).
No built-in predicates imported.

Design notes:
  - All predicates are pure arithmetic; no grid access, no side effects.
  - vv_rot90_cw uses direct unification RDR = DC (no arithmetic) and
    is/2 for RDC is -DR, keeping the predicate concise.
  - vv_rot90_ccw similarly uses is/2 for the negation and direct
    unification for the copy.
  - vv_parallel calls vv_cross and tests the result with =:= 0; this
    makes the parallelism test a one-liner on top of vv_cross.
  - vv_translate_region uses maplist/3 with the helper vv_translate_cell_/4
    which is partially applied as vv_translate_cell_(DR, DC) via the
    module-aware call mechanism.
  - No PrologAI pack is imported.

Dependencies: none. The vec2 pack is fully self-contained.
