PART ARCH-92: SPREAD PACK ARCHITECTURE (Layer 105)

Location: packs/spread/prolog/spread.pl
Module: spread
Layer: 105
Work Package: 126
Prefix: sd_*
Dependencies: library(lists) [member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, append/2, append/3,
              max_list/2, min_list/2], library(apply) [maplist/3, maplist/4,
              include/3]. No PrologAI pack is imported.

Public interface (14 predicates):
  sd_dist_map/5     - single-source BFS distance map
  sd_dist_multi/4   - multi-source BFS distance map (minimum over seeds)
  sd_reachable/5    - all reachable Bg cells from a source
  sd_path_dist/7    - BFS shortest path distance between two cells
  sd_path_exists/6  - reachability test between two cells
  sd_ring/6         - cells at exactly BFS distance D
  sd_zone/6         - cells within BFS distance MaxD
  sd_dist_to_set/6  - minimum distance from source to a target set
  sd_farthest/5     - farthest reachable cell by BFS distance
  sd_expand_once/5  - one BFS level expansion (low-level)
  sd_spread_color/5 - spread a color outward through background cells
  sd_max_dist/5     - maximum BFS distance to any reachable cell
  sd_fill_dist/5    - grid with BFS distances overlaid on Bg cells
  sd_voronoi/4      - Voronoi cell-to-seed assignment by BFS distance

Internal helpers:
  sd_dims_/3        - extract (NR, NC) from grid
  sd_cell_val_/3    - get value at R-C cell
  sd_4candidates_/5 - in-bounds 4-adjacent cells
  sd_bg4unvis_/8    - Bg 4-neighbors not in visited set
  sd_make_bfs1_/3   - build bfs1(Cell,D) queue entry
  sd_bfs_single_/8  - BFS loop for single/multi source distance maps
  sd_color_cells_/3 - find all cells with a given value
  sd_set_grid_cell_/5  - replace a cell value in a grid
  sd_apply_vals_/4  - set a list of cells to a value
  sd_apply_dist_map_/3 - overlay DistMap values onto a grid
  sd_make_bfs2_/4   - build bfs2(Cell,D,Seed) queue entry
  sd_bfs_voronoi_/8 - BFS loop for Voronoi seed assignment

Data structures:
  DistMap  - list of Cell-D pairs (Cell = R-C, D = non-negative integer)
  Assignment - list of Cell-SeedIdx pairs (SeedIdx 1-based integer)
  BFS queue entry (single): bfs1(Cell, D)
  BFS queue entry (voronoi): bfs2(Cell, D, SeedIdx)
  Grid - list of lists of integers (row-major, 0-based indexing)

Design notes:
  BFS uses a FIFO queue implemented as a Prolog list. Neighbors are appended
  to the tail; the head is dequeued each step. Visited cells are tracked as
  a list; membership test is O(n) but sufficient for the grid sizes occurring
  in ARC-AGI-2 evaluation tasks. The Voronoi BFS interleaves all seed frontiers
  in init-queue order; FIFO order guarantees that ties are broken by the seed
  with the lower 1-based index. sd_spread_color seeds the BFS from Color cells
  (non-Bg) without filtering them out, using D > 0 to exclude them from the
  cells to be painted.

Dependencies: none. The spread pack is fully self-contained.

END OF PART ARCH-92


PART ARCH-93: ENCLOSURE PACK (en_* prefix, Layer 106)
Work Package 127

File: packs/enclosure/prolog/enclosure.pl
Module: enclosure
Exported predicates (14):
  en_border_cells/2, en_outer_cells/3, en_inner_cells/3, en_is_inner/4,
  en_is_outer/4, en_fill_inner/4, en_inner_count/3, en_has_inner/2,
  en_inner_components/3, en_outer_components/3, en_fill_hole/6,
  en_boundary_cells/3, en_interior_cells/3, en_is_surrounded/4

Imports:
  library(lists): member/2, memberchk/2, nth0/3, append/2, append/3,
                  subtract/3
  library(apply): maplist/3, include/3

Internal helpers:
  en_dims_/3          - extract row and column count from a grid
  en_cell_val_/3      - retrieve value at a cell
  en_4candidates_/5   - in-bounds 4-adjacent cells of a given cell
  en_all_bg_/3        - all Bg cells in sorted order
  en_all_color_/3     - all Color cells in sorted order
  en_bfs_bg_/7        - BFS traversal through Bg cells (Vis as accumulator)
  en_set_cell_/5      - replace one cell value in a grid
  en_set_cells_/4     - apply a list of cell replacements
  en_comp_bfs_/6      - BFS within a restricted available cell set
  en_all_comps_/4     - partition a cell list into connected components

Algorithm: outer/inner classification
  Border BFS: collect all Bg cells on the grid border as seeds. Run
  en_bfs_bg_ from those seeds, growing through 4-adjacent Bg cells. The
  reached set is the exterior. All other Bg cells (set difference via
  subtract/3) are interior. The BFS is queue-based FIFO using a Prolog
  list; the visited set doubles as the accumulator and is returned as the
  result.

Algorithm: connected components
  en_comp_bfs_: given an available set (Avail) and a starting cell, BFS
  within Avail (neighbors must be in Avail and not yet visited). The
  visited list is the accumulator; the final visited list is the component.
  en_all_comps_: iteratively extract components by taking the first
  unassigned cell, running en_comp_bfs_ to find its component, subtracting
  the component from the remaining cells, and recursing.

Algorithm: boundary vs. interior within a color region
  en_boundary_cells: include all Color cells that are on the grid edge
  (fewer than 4 in-bounds neighbors) or have at least one in-bounds
  neighbor with a different value.
  en_interior_cells: include all Color cells with exactly 4 in-bounds
  neighbors that are all Color.
  Both use include/3 with a YALL lambda that captures Grid, NR, NC, Color
  from the enclosing scope. Free variables in the lambda body are fresh
  for each invocation due to YALL's copy_term semantics.

Data representations:
  Grid - list of lists of integers (row-major, 0-based indexing)
  Cell - R-C pair (row-column, 0-based integer)
  Comps - list of cell lists, each list being one connected component

Dependencies: none. The enclosure pack is fully self-contained.

END OF PART ARCH-93


PART ARCH-94 - HULL PACK ARCHITECTURE

Layer: 107
Work Package: 128
Module file: packs/hull/prolog/hull.pl
Test file: packs/hull/test/test_hull.pl
Pack descriptor: packs/hull/pack.pl
Prefix: hu_

Purpose:
  Convex hull computation and polygon geometry for 2D integer-coordinate
  cell sets. Provides the foundational "smallest enclosing convex region"
  operation and derived predicates: area, perimeter, containment, diameter,
  convexity testing, concavity extraction, and hull filling.

Algorithm: Andrew's Monotone Chain
  Cells are sorted by (C, R) — column ascending, then row ascending —
  which corresponds to sorting by (x, y) in standard Cartesian coordinates
  with y=R increasing downward. The algorithm builds two half-hulls:
  1. Lower half (left-to-right): trim CCW/collinear turns (Z >= 0).
  2. Upper half (right-to-left): same trim condition on reversed sequence.
  After trimming shared endpoints from each half-hull, the two halves are
  concatenated to form the complete hull in clockwise screen order.

Cross product convention:
  hu_cross_(A, B, C) = (C.col - A.col)*(C.row - A.row) - (B.row - A.row)*(C.col - A.col)
  Positive = counterclockwise turn in screen space (R increases downward).
  Trim condition: Z >= 0 (non-clockwise turns are removed from hull).
  Result: hull vertices are in clockwise screen order.

Point-in-hull test:
  For a CW hull, point P is inside or on the hull iff for every directed
  edge (A -> B), the edge cross product Z = (B.col-A.col)*(P.row-A.row) -
  (B.row-A.row)*(P.col-A.col) satisfies Z =< 0. Degenerate cases (0 or 1
  vertex hulls) use exact equality; 2-vertex hulls use collinearity plus
  bounding-box bounds.

Shoelace formula:
  hu_hull_area2 closes the polygon and sums C_i * R_{i+1} - C_{i+1} * R_i
  over all consecutive vertex pairs. The absolute value is twice the area.
  All values are integers (no floating point).

Convexity test:
  A cell set is convex iff the set equals the set of all grid cells inside
  the hull (within the bounding box). Computed by building the hull, then
  enumerating all grid cells in the bounding box, testing each for
  hu_in_hull, and comparing the result to the original cell set.

Exported predicates:
  hu_convex_hull/2      - compute ordered hull vertices
  hu_is_convex/1        - test discrete convexity
  hu_hull_size/2        - count hull vertices
  hu_hull_area2/2       - twice area (integer, shoelace)
  hu_in_hull/3          - point-in-hull membership
  hu_cells_in_hull/3    - all grid cells inside hull
  hu_fill_hull/4        - paint hull interior in a grid
  hu_concavities/4      - find Bg cells in hull but not in shape
  hu_diameter/4         - farthest pair of cells
  hu_aspect/3           - bounding box height and width
  hu_is_rect/1          - test for rectangular hull
  hu_hull_perim2/2      - sum of squared edge lengths
  hu_centroid/3         - integer centroid of hull vertices
  hu_hull_contains/2    - test containment of a cell set

Private helpers:
  hu_sort_xy_/2         - sort cells by (C, R) for monotone chain
  hu_cross_/4           - screen-coordinate cross product
  hu_trim_/3            - remove CCW/collinear points from half-hull
  hu_build_half_/3      - build one monotone chain half-hull
  hu_bbox_/5            - bounding box of a cell list
  hu_edge_test_/3       - single-edge inside test (Z =< 0)
  hu_all_edges_/2       - test all edges of a closed polygon
  hu_dims_/3            - grid dimensions
  hu_set_cell_/5        - replace one cell value
  hu_set_cells_/4       - apply list of cell replacements
  hu_shoelace_/2        - closed polygon shoelace sum
  hu_shoelace_sum_/3    - accumulate shoelace terms
  hu_dist2_/3           - squared Euclidean distance
  hu_dot_/4             - edge-edge dot product
  hu_edge_len2_/3       - squared edge length
  hu_perim2_sum_/3      - accumulate squared edge lengths
  hu_sum_list_/2        - sum a list of integers

Data representations:
  Grid - list of lists of integers (row-major, 0-based indexing)
  Cell - R-C pair (row-column, 0-based integer)
  Hull - list of R-C cells in clockwise screen order

Dependencies: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, append/3, reverse/2,
  min_list/2, max_list/2, last/2. library(apply): maplist/3.
  No PrologAI pack dependencies.

END OF PART ARCH-94


PART ARCH-95 - PATCH PACK ARCHITECTURE

Layer: 108
Pack: patch
Source: packs/patch/prolog/patch.pl
Tests: packs/patch/test/test_patch.pl
Prefix: pa_
Dependencies: none (no pack imports; uses only standard library predicates)

Purpose:

The patch pack provides sub-grid extraction and template matching for
integer-valued grids. A "patch" is any rectangular sub-grid (a list of lists
of integers). The pack enables:

1. Sub-grid extraction: pa_extract retrieves any rectangular region.
2. Template matching: pa_match / pa_match_all / pa_match_count find all
   positions where a small pattern occurs exactly within a larger grid.
3. Wildcard matching: pa_match_bg allows background-colored cells in the
   pattern to match any grid cell (pattern with "don't care" positions).
4. Sliding window enumeration: pa_slides / pa_unique_patches give all
   possible sub-regions of a given size.
5. Statistical analysis: pa_most_common_patch finds the most frequent
   sub-pattern.
6. Patch comparison: pa_diff identifies differing cells between two patches.
7. Geometric operations: pa_flip_h, pa_flip_v, pa_rot90 for 2D transforms.
8. Uniformity test: pa_is_uniform checks if a patch has a single color.

Key design decision: pa_match is non-deterministic and backtracks over all
matching positions. pa_match_all wraps it in findall for a complete list.
This split allows both single-match (early exit) and all-match queries.

Template matching algorithm (pa_match): for each candidate top-left corner
(R0, C0) in range [0, NR-H] x [0, NC-W], extract the H x W sub-grid using
pa_extract and unify it directly with the Patch argument. Prolog structural
unification performs the cell-by-cell comparison in a single step.

Rotation formula (pa_rot90): clockwise 90-degree rotation in screen
coordinates maps Patch(R, C) to Rotated(C, H-1-R). Output dimensions are
W x H for an H x W input. Verified with 2x3 and 2x2 examples.

All predicates are deterministic except pa_match (which is the intended
non-deterministic entry point for template matching with backtracking).

PART ARCH-95 ends here.

END OF PART ARCH-95

PART ARCH-99 - OFFSET PACK ARCHITECTURE (Layer 112)

Work Package 133: offset pack.
Layer: 112 (Grid Shifting and Circular Rolling).
Prefix: od_*.
File: packs/offset/prolog/offset.pl.
Tests: packs/offset/test/test_offset.pl (42 tests).
Pack descriptor: packs/offset/pack.pl.

Dependencies:
  library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, append/3.
  library(apply): maplist/3.
  No PrologAI pack dependencies.

Exported predicates (14):
  od_shift_row/4, od_shift_row_left/4, od_roll_row/3,
  od_shift_right/4, od_shift_left/4, od_shift_down/4, od_shift_up/4,
  od_shift_dir/5, od_roll_right/3, od_roll_left/3,
  od_roll_down/3, od_roll_up/3, od_shift_color/6, od_infer_shift/5.

Internal predicates:
  od_roll_left_row_/3: circular left shift of a single row. Used by od_roll_left.
  od_apply_shift_/5: apply a signed (DR,DC) shift with if-then-else branching.
    Used by od_infer_shift.

Design decisions:
  od_shift_row uses length/2 + append/3 to split the row at position W-N, then
  findall(Bg, between(1,N,_), ...) to build exactly N background cells.
  N=0 is handled correctly by between(1,0,_) failing -> BgCells=[], append identity.
  od_shift_dir uses a single clause with if-then-else to avoid choicepoints from
  multi-clause dispatch.
  od_infer_shift uses a brute-force search over all integer displacements with a
  cut after the first match. This is O(H*W) in the worst case but correct.
  od_shift_color uses a nested findall with in-bounds check and if-then-else to
  determine each output cell without building an explicit mutable structure.

PART ARCH-100: INTERLEAVE PACK (Layer 113)

Work Package 134. Pack: interleave. Layer 113. Prefix: il_.
File: packs/interleave/prolog/interleave.pl.
Tests: packs/interleave/test/test_interleave.pl.

Purpose: row/column interleaving, weaving, stride selection, and block
partitioning for 2D grids. All operations are pure list transformations
with no side effects.

Predicate architecture:

il_rows/3: base-recursive. Empty base case with cut. Recursive case
  prepends both a GridA row and a GridB row in one step.

il_cols/3: delegates to il_zip_row_ via maplist/4. il_zip_row_ is
  base-recursive with the same pattern as il_rows_.

il_derows/3: delegates to il_derows_/4 with index counter. Two clauses
  differentiated by 0 is I mod 2 with cut. Accumulates Even and Odd
  by prepending to the appropriate list.

il_decols/3: delegates to il_decols_row_ via maplist/4 (collecting even and
  odd columns for each row). il_decols_row_ delegates to il_decols_list_/4,
  which uses the same two-clause index pattern as il_derows_.

il_weave_rows/3: three clauses with cuts for empty and singleton. Recursive
  case builds a BgRow using findall+between and inserts it after Row.

il_weave_cols/3: delegates to il_weave_row_ via maplist/3. il_weave_row_
  has three clauses (empty, singleton, recursive) with cuts.

il_unweave_rows/2: one-liner that calls il_derows and discards Odd.
il_unweave_cols/2: one-liner that calls il_decols and discards Odd.

il_stride_rows/4: findall over between(Start0, H1, I) filtered by
  0 is (I - Start0) mod Step. nth0/3 retrieves each row.

il_stride_cols/4: if-then-else to handle empty grid without choicepoint.
  Computes ColIdxs via findall+between+mod, then applies il_pick_cols_ via
  maplist/3. il_pick_cols_ maps il_nth0_ over each index in a row.

il_select_rows/3: maplist(il_nth0_(Grid), Indices, SubGrid).
il_select_cols/3: maplist(il_pick_cols_(Indices), Grid, SubGrid).

il_rows_n/2: empty base with cut. General case uses findall with nested
  between (row index) and member (grid) for round-robin row collection.

il_block_rows/3: base case for empty grid with cut. Recursive case uses
  if-then-else to distinguish full blocks (length >= N) from a partial
  last block. length/2 + append/3 extracts each block.

Library imports:
  library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, append/2, append/3.
  library(apply): maplist/3, maplist/4.

Tutorial chapter: docs/tutorial/Ch95_Interleave.txt.
SPARC volumes updated: Spec v99, Pseudo v92, Arch v93, Refinement v147,
  Completion v150.

END OF PART ARCH-100


PART ARCH-101: PANEL PACK (Layer 114)

Work Package 135. Pack: panel. Layer 114. Prefix: pn_.
File: packs/panel/prolog/panel.pl.
Tests: packs/panel/test/test_panel.pl.

Purpose: detecting all-background divider rows/columns, splitting at
dividers, removing dividers, quadrant decomposition, and column slicing.
All operations are pure list transformations with no side effects.

Predicate architecture:

pn_is_divider_row/3: nth0/3 retrieves the row; forall/2 checks all
  elements with == for structural equality. forall is a built-in.

pn_is_divider_col/3: forall over member(Row, Grid) with nth0(C, Row, V)
  and V == Bg check.

pn_divider_rows/3: findall over between + pn_is_divider_row.
pn_divider_cols/3: gets width from first row with if-then-else for empty
  grid; findall over between + pn_is_divider_col.

pn_split_rows/3: delegates to pn_split_rows_/5. Two clauses with cut on
  the base case (empty divider list) to avoid choicepoints. Recursive case
  extracts rows [Start, Div) via pn_extract_rows_, then advances Start to
  Div+1 for the next band.

pn_extract_rows_/4: if-then-else to handle empty range (Start > End1).
  Non-empty range uses findall + between + nth0.

pn_split_cols/3: analogous to pn_split_rows but applies pn_slice_row_
  via maplist/3 to each row. Two clauses with cut on base case.

pn_slice_row_/4: length/2 creates a Skip list of C0 variables; append/3
  splits Row into Skip+Suffix; length/2 creates a Sub list of Len=C1-C0
  variables; append/3 unifies Sub with the first Len elements of Suffix.

pn_auto_split_rows/3: one-liner using pn_divider_rows then pn_split_rows.
pn_auto_split_cols/3: one-liner using pn_divider_cols then pn_split_cols.

pn_strip_rows/3: pn_divider_rows finds Divs; findall over between +
  \+ memberchk(I, Divs) + nth0 collects non-divider rows.

pn_strip_cols/3: pn_divider_cols finds Divs; findall over between +
  \+ memberchk builds the Kept index list; maplist(pn_select_cols_) extracts
  kept columns from each row. pn_select_cols_ uses maplist(pn_nth0_) over Idxs.

pn_quadrants/5: computes MidR = H//2, MidC = W//2; calls pn_rect_ four
  times with the four (R0,C0,R1,C1) quadrant boundaries.

pn_rect_/6: findall over between(R0,R1a,R) + nth0 + pn_slice_row_.

pn_n_col_parts/3: findall over between(0, N1, K) + arithmetic for C0/C1 +
  maplist(pn_slice_row_) to extract each strip from all rows.

pn_col_slices/3: pn_cumsum_ computes running totals; pn_col_slices_ is
  two-clause recursive with cut on the empty base case.

pn_has_dividers/2: calls pn_divider_rows; if non-empty, succeeds (true);
  else calls pn_divider_cols and checks non-empty. Uses if-then-else.

Library imports:
  library(lists): memberchk/2, nth0/3, append/2, append/3.
  library(apply): maplist/3.
  forall/2 is a built-in and is not imported.

Tutorial chapter: docs/tutorial/Ch96_Panel.txt.
SPARC volumes updated: Spec v100, Pseudo v93, Arch v94, Refinement v148,
  Completion v151.

END OF PART ARCH-101


PART ARCH-102: SCAN PACK (WP 136, Layer 115)

Work Package: 136
Layer: 115
Module prefix: sn_
Pack location: packs/scan/

Purpose: General-purpose grid cell enumeration and manipulation. Orthogonal
to existing spatial packs; provides the building blocks for constructing
ARC-AGI-2 rule predicates that need to inspect, filter, or transform specific
cells across a grid.

Files:
  packs/scan/pack.pl               - pack descriptor (name, version, requires)
  packs/scan/prolog/scan.pl        - module scan, 14 sn_* predicates
  packs/scan/test/test_scan.pl     - 42 PLUnit acceptance tests

Predicates:
  sn_row_major/2    - R-C-V triples in row-major order
  sn_col_major/2    - R-C-V triples in column-major order
  sn_cells_of/3     - R-C pairs for all cells matching a value
  sn_set_cell/5     - new grid with one cell replaced
  sn_map_cells/3    - apply Goal(R,C,OldV,NewV) to every cell
  sn_filter_cells/3 - R-C-V triples satisfying a predicate
  sn_update_cells/3 - batch R-C-V cell updates
  sn_zigzag/2       - boustrophedon traversal
  sn_spiral_in/2    - clockwise spiral from outer ring inward
  sn_border_traversal/2 - outer border cells clockwise
  sn_diag_traversal_ne/2 - NE diagonals (R+C constant)
  sn_diag_traversal_se/2 - SE diagonals (C-R constant)
  sn_grid_from_cells/5   - build grid from sparse cell list
  sn_index_of/4     - first occurrence of a value (row-major)

Implementation notes:
  sn_row_major, sn_col_major, sn_cells_of, sn_filter_cells, sn_diag_traversal_ne,
  sn_diag_traversal_se: single findall, fully deterministic.
  sn_set_cell, sn_map_cells, sn_update_cells, sn_grid_from_cells: nested findall.
  sn_zigzag: single findall with if-then-else on row parity.
  sn_spiral_in: recursive sn_spiral_/6 with nested if-then-else termination.
  sn_border_traversal: if-then-else on H > 1 and W > 1 guards.
  sn_index_of: between/3 enumeration with cut on first match.

Library imports:
  library(lists): memberchk/2, nth0/3, append/3, reverse/2.
  All other predicates used (between/3, findall/3, call/N, length/2) are built-ins.

PART ARCH-103: BOUND PACK (WP 137, Layer 116)

Work Package: 137
Layer: 116
Module prefix: bd_
Pack location: packs/bound/

Purpose: Bounding box extraction and manipulation. Orthogonal to existing spatial
packs; provides building blocks for ARC-AGI-2 rules that need to locate objects
by their tight extent, place sub-grids at computed positions, or test rectangular
region relationships.

Files:
  packs/bound/pack.pl              - pack descriptor (name, version, requires)
  packs/bound/prolog/bound.pl      - module bound, 14 bd_* predicates
  packs/bound/test/test_bound.pl   - 42 PLUnit acceptance tests

Predicates:
  bd_bbox/6         - tight inclusive bounding box of a color
  bd_bbox_h/3       - height of an inclusive bounding box
  bd_bbox_w/3       - width of an inclusive bounding box
  bd_crop_bbox/6    - crop grid to an inclusive rectangle
  bd_crop_color/3   - crop to tight bounding box of a color
  bd_trim/3         - remove all-Bg border rows and columns
  bd_pad/4          - add N Bg cells on all four sides
  bd_place/6        - place a sub-grid at a canvas position
  bd_center/4       - integer center of a color's bounding box
  bd_bbox_contains/6 - test if a cell lies within a bounding box
  bd_bbox_overlap/8  - test if two bounding boxes overlap
  bd_bbox_union/12   - smallest box enclosing two boxes
  bd_expand/9        - expand a bounding box outward by N
  bd_fill_bbox/7     - fill a rectangular region with a color

Implementation notes:
  bd_bbox: findall over all cell positions; min_list/max_list on collected indices.
  bd_crop_bbox: findall over row range with bd_slice_row_ for inclusive column slices.
  bd_trim: findall of non-Bg cells; if-then-else for empty result.
  bd_pad: findall for background rows; maplist(bd_pad_row_) for row padding.
  bd_place: nested findall with if-then-else on Patch row/column bounds.
  bd_fill_bbox: nested findall with if-then-else on bounding box bounds.
  Arithmetic predicates (bd_bbox_h, bd_bbox_w, bd_center, bd_expand,
  bd_bbox_union): pure arithmetic, fully deterministic.
  bd_bbox_contains, bd_bbox_overlap: constraint tests, may fail.

Library imports:
  library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, min_list/2, max_list/2, append/2, append/3.
  library(apply): maplist/3.

Tutorial chapter: docs/tutorial/Ch98_Bound.txt.

PART ARCH-104: CELLSET PACK

Work Package: 138
Layer: 117
Module prefix: cs_
Pack location: packs/cellset/

Purpose: Sparse cell set operations over R-C position lists. Orthogonal to
existing spatial packs; provides a set-theoretic layer for ARC-AGI-2 rules that
need to treat objects as sorted position lists rather than dense grids.

Files:
  packs/cellset/pack.pl              - pack descriptor (name, version, requires)
  packs/cellset/prolog/cellset.pl    - module cellset, 14 cs_* predicates
  packs/cellset/test/test_cellset.pl - 42 PLUnit acceptance tests

Predicates:
  cs_from_grid/3     - extract sorted R-C positions of a color from a grid
  cs_to_grid/6       - paint a cell set onto an HxW canvas
  cs_union/3         - sorted set union
  cs_intersect/3     - sorted set intersection
  cs_subtract/3      - set difference
  cs_translate/4     - shift all cells by (DR, DC)
  cs_bbox/5          - bounding box of a non-empty cell set
  cs_normalize/4     - translate so top-left is at (0,0); return offsets
  cs_size/2          - count of cells in the set
  cs_contains/3      - deterministic membership test
  cs_adjacent_bg/2   - sorted 4-connected background neighbors
  cs_same_shape/2    - shape equality after normalization
  cs_rotate_90/3     - 90-degree CW rotation within a grid of H rows
  cs_mirror_h/3      - horizontal mirror within a grid of W columns

Implementation notes:
  cs_from_grid: findall over grid, sort/2 for canonical order.
  cs_to_grid: nested findall with memberchk to select Color or Bg per cell.
  cs_union: append + sort removes duplicates.
  cs_intersect: findall of members of A in B, then sort.
  cs_subtract: delegates to subtract/3 from library(lists).
  cs_translate: maplist with cs_add_ helper; preserves sort order.
  cs_bbox: findall of row and column indices; min_list/max_list.
  cs_normalize: two clauses - empty list returns ([], 0, 0); non-empty uses
    cs_bbox + cs_translate.
  cs_adjacent_bg: findall of 4 offsets per cell, \+memberchk filter, sort.
  cs_same_shape: if-then-else on empty; otherwise normalize both and ==/2.
  cs_rotate_90: maplist with cs_rot90_ (new_R=C, new_C=H1-R), then sort.
  cs_mirror_h: maplist with cs_mirh_ (new_C=W1-C), then sort.

Library imports:
  library(lists): member/2, memberchk/2, nth0/3, append/2, subtract/3,
    min_list/2, max_list/2.
  library(apply): maplist/3.

PART ARCH-105: LOCATE PACK

Work Package: 139
Layer: 118
Module prefix: lc_
Pack location: packs/locate/

Purpose: Pattern location within grids. Orthogonal to scan and cellset packs;
provides subgrid template matching and row/column sequence search for ARC-AGI-2
rules that need to find where sub-patterns occur, which rows/columns match a
given sequence, and where unique markers are positioned.

Files:
  packs/locate/pack.pl              - pack descriptor (name, version, requires)
  packs/locate/prolog/locate.pl     - module locate, 14 lc_* predicates
  packs/locate/test/test_locate.pl  - 42 PLUnit acceptance tests

Predicates:
  lc_subgrid_at/4      - test if Sub appears at a specific position in Grid
  lc_find_sub/4        - first position where Sub matches (deterministic)
  lc_all_sub/3         - all positions where Sub matches
  lc_subgrid_count/3   - count of Sub occurrences in Grid
  lc_row_pattern/3     - first row index matching a row pattern
  lc_all_row_pattern/3 - all row indices matching a row pattern
  lc_col_pattern/3     - first column index matching a column pattern
  lc_all_col_pattern/3 - all column indices matching a column pattern
  lc_row_prefix/4      - decompose a grid row as prefix ++ rest
  lc_row_suffix/3      - test if a grid row ends with a given suffix
  lc_anchor/4          - unique-occurrence cell: exactly one cell equals V
  lc_row_count/3       - count of V per row as a list
  lc_row_contains/3    - sorted rows that contain V
  lc_col_contains/3    - sorted columns that contain V

Implementation notes:
  lc_subgrid_at: forall/2 over Sub positions; each tests a Grid offset cell.
  lc_find_sub: between/3 enumeration + lc_subgrid_at + cut.
  lc_all_sub: findall over candidates filtered by lc_subgrid_at.
  lc_row_pattern: nth0 with Pattern for direct unification + cut.
  lc_col_pattern: inner findall extracts column as list; unifies with Pattern; cut.
  lc_all_col_pattern: outer findall collects columns where inner findall unifies.
  lc_row_prefix: append(Prefix, Rest, Row) via nth0.
  lc_row_suffix: append(_, Suffix, Row) + cut for deterministic test.
  lc_anchor: findall of all V positions; single-element list pattern.
  lc_row_count: maplist with lc_count_in_row_ (findall + member + length).
  lc_row_contains: findall + member + sort.
  lc_col_contains: findall + nth0 + sort.

Library imports:

PART ARCH-106: EXTENDED CELL SELECTION BY VALUE COMPARISON (xsel PACK)

Work Package 140. Layer 119. Module: xsel. Prefix: xs_*.
Location: packs/xsel/prolog/xsel.pl.
Tests: packs/xsel/test/test_xsel.pl (42 tests).

Layer role: Extended cell selection by numerical value comparison on 2D grids.
Complements arith (cell arithmetic), histogram (frequency counts), and count
(equality counts) by providing order-based queries across the numerical range.

Predicate inventory (14):
  xs_cells_lt, xs_cells_gt, xs_cells_le, xs_cells_ge: threshold cell selectors.
  xs_cells_between: closed-interval cell selector.
  xs_cells_ne: inequality cell selector.
  xs_max_cells, xs_min_cells: extremum cell locators.
  xs_threshold: binary threshold mapping producing a new grid.
  xs_replace_lt, xs_replace_gt: conditional value replacement in a grid.
  xs_rank_vals: sorted unique value list (ordinal rank ladder).
  xs_val_rank: 0-based rank of a specific value in the grid.
  xs_rank_grid: replace every cell with its ordinal rank.

Key implementation notes:
  xs_cells_lt/gt/le/ge/between/ne: findall with arithmetic guard + sort/2.
  xs_max_cells/xs_min_cells: two-pass - first collect all values and compute
    extremum via max_list/min_list; second findall collects matching positions.
  xs_threshold/xs_replace_lt/xs_replace_gt: nested maplist (row then cell)
    with if-then-else inside private helper predicates.
  xs_rank_vals: findall via nested member/2 + sort/2 (deduplication is free).
  xs_val_rank: xs_rank_vals + nth0 + cut to commit to unique match.
  xs_rank_grid: xs_rank_vals once, then nested maplist with nth0 + cut per cell.

Library imports:
  library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, max_list/2, min_list/2.
  library(apply): maplist/3.

Tutorial chapter: docs/tutorial/Ch101_Xsel.txt.

  Completion v156.

PART ARCH-107: CELLULAR AUTOMATON NEIGHBORHOOD AGGREGATION (autom PACK)

Work Package 141. Layer 120. Module: autom. Prefix: at_*.
Location: packs/autom/prolog/autom.pl.
Tests: packs/autom/test/test_autom.pl (42 tests).

Layer role: Grid-wide neighborhood aggregation. Produces transformed grids
where each cell's value is determined by aggregating its neighborhood.
Complements neighbor pack (per-cell queries) and window pack (per-cell counts).

Predicate inventory (14):
  at_count_nbrs_4, at_count_nbrs_8: count grids for a specific target value.
  at_count_same_4, at_count_same_8: count grids for same-valued neighbors.
  at_any_nbr_4, at_any_nbr_8: boolean grids for any-neighbor existence.
  at_all_nbrs_4, at_all_nbrs_8: boolean grids for all-neighbor condition.
  at_isolated_4, at_isolated_8: lists of isolated cells of a given value.
  at_birth_4, at_birth_8: apply a birth rule to dead cells.
  at_majority_4: each cell takes the majority value among itself and 4-neighbors.
  at_step_gol: one step of Conway's Game of Life (B3/S23).

Key implementation notes:
  at_offs4_/at_offs8_: private predicates that supply direction offset lists;
    avoids repeating literal offset lists in every predicate.
  at_count_nbrs_4/8: triple-nested findall (outer=rows, middle=cells, inner=nbrs).
  at_any_nbr_4/8: uses at_has_nbr_4_/at_has_nbr_8_ private helpers with cut on
    first V-neighbor found; if-then-else maps to 1/0.
  at_all_nbrs_4/8: uses forall/2 over in-bounds neighbor positions; vacuously
    true for cells with no in-bounds neighbors (e.g., single-cell grid).
  at_isolated_4/8: findall with \+ at_has_nbr_ for negation-as-failure test.
  at_birth_4/8: triple-nested findall; (V == Dead, N =:= Count -> Live ; V).
  at_majority_4: at_mode_ computes majority with findall+max_list+tie-to-Bg.
  at_step_gol: triple-nested findall + at_gol_next_ (3 clauses for B3/S23).

Library imports:
  library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, max_list/2.

Tutorial chapter: docs/tutorial/Ch102_Autom.txt.
SPARC volumes updated: Spec v106, Pseudo v99, Arch v100, Refinement v154,
  Completion v157.

END OF PART ARCH-107


PART ARCH-108: CROSS PACK ARCHITECTURE

Work Package 142. Layer 121. Module: cross. Prefix: cx_*.
File: packs/cross/prolog/cross.pl.
Tests: packs/cross/test/test_cross.pl.

Position in dependency order: Layer 121 builds on no other packs.
cross.pl is a standalone analytics module; it does not depend on any other
PrologAI pack.

Design decisions:
  cx_row/cx_col: row extraction uses nth0/3 directly; column extraction uses
    member(Row,Grid) + nth0(C,Row,V) inside findall, iterating rows in order.
  cx_diag/cx_antidiag: iterate row index R from 0..H-1; column index is R
    (main diagonal) or W-1-R (anti-diagonal); guard C>=0 for non-square grids
    where H>W ensures findall produces the correct shorter list.
  cx_row_sum/cx_col_sum: delegate to sum_list/2 from library(lists); no manual
    accumulation needed.
  cx_row_count/cx_col_count: findall+member over the extracted list; length/2
    gives the count. Member/2 uses structural equality so works with any term.
  cx_rows_with/cx_cols_with: between/3 enumerates indices; sort/2 deduplicates
    because a row/column with multiple V occurrences would generate multiple
    copies of the same index in the findall result.
  cx_row_uniq/cx_col_uniq: sort/2 on the extracted list gives sorted unique set.
  cx_row_mode/cx_col_mode: delegate to cx_mode_/3 which reuses the
    findall+max_list+unique-winner-or-Bg pattern established in the autom pack.

Library imports:
  library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, sum_list/2, max_list/2.

Tutorial chapter: docs/tutorial/Ch103_Cross.txt.
SPARC volumes updated: Spec v107, Pseudo v100, Arch v101, Refinement v155,
  Completion v158.

END OF PART ARCH-108


PART ARCH-109: MASK PACK ARCHITECTURE

Work Package 143. Layer 122. Module: mask. Prefix: mk_*.
File: packs/mask/prolog/mask.pl.
Tests: packs/mask/test/test_mask.pl.

Position in dependency order: Layer 122 builds on no other packs.
mask.pl is a standalone module; it does not depend on any other
PrologAI pack.

Design decisions:
  mk_from_val/mk_from_bg: use nested maplist/3 with two-clause per-cell
    helpers. The cut-on-match pattern (match->1, !, other->0) ensures that
    structural equality (==) is used, not arithmetic equality.
  mk_invert: also uses maplist/3 with a two-clause helper. Non-1 values
    (including 0) are inverted to 1, so mk_invert is a bitwise complement
    for standard 0/1 masks.
  mk_and/mk_or: nested maplist/4 for element-wise binary operations. The
    cut-based two-clause helpers avoid redundant arithmetic.
  mk_xor: uses C is (A+B) mod 2 so it works correctly for integer inputs
    beyond 0 and 1, though the standard use is with 0/1 masks.
  mk_apply/mk_fill: nested maplist/4; the two-clause helpers use the mask
    bit as the discriminator. mk_apply and mk_fill are strict duals: apply
    keeps Grid values at 1-positions (replaces 0-positions with Bg), while
    fill sets Grid values at 1-positions to V (keeps 0-positions unchanged).
  mk_overlay: nested maplist/5 for four-list parallel iteration (GridA,
    GridB, Mask -> Grid2 per row; three values per cell -> output cell).
  mk_where: findall + nth0/3 + sort/2. between/3 over row and column indices
    ensures R-C pairs are generated in row-major order, so sort is
    redundant in practice but provides the canonical sorted guarantee.
  mk_count: findall + member/2 is simpler than findall + nth0/3 for this
    use case because we only need to count 1-valued cells, not record their
    positions.
  mk_any: member/2 with cut-on-first-1; short-circuits on the first match.
  mk_all: forall/2 (built-in) with B =:= 1; vacuously true for an
    empty mask.
  mk_extract: findall collecting Grid values at Mask=1 positions using
    both Grid-nth0 and Mask-nth0; sort/2 deduplicates.

Library imports:
  library(apply): maplist/3, maplist/4, maplist/5.
  library(lists): member/2, nth0/3.
  forall/2 is a built-in; not imported.

Tutorial chapter: docs/tutorial/Ch104_Mask.txt.
SPARC volumes updated: Spec v108, Pseudo v101, Arch v102, Refinement v156,
  Completion v159.

END OF PART ARCH-109


PART ARCH-110: TABLE PACK ARCHITECTURE

Work Package 144. Layer 123. Module: table. Prefix: tb_*.
File: packs/table/prolog/table.pl.
Tests: packs/table/test/test_table.pl.

Position in dependency order: Layer 123. No dependencies on other packs.

Design decisions:
  tb_transpose: uses findall over column indices 0..W-1; each column is
    extracted with member(Row,Grid)+nth0(C,Row,V). Requires W>=1; W=0 gives [].
  tb_sort_rows: builds key-value pairs V-Row via findall, sorts with keysort/2
    (built-in stable sort), then unwraps. keysort preserves row identity.
  tb_filter_rows: simple findall with structural nth0 equality (== via unify).
  tb_group_by: two-pass: first collect + sort unique keys, then per-key findall.
    Ordered by sorted column C value, not by first appearance.
  tb_count_by: delegates to tb_group_by then maps length over groups.
  tb_unique_rows: recursive helper with accumulator (Seen list); \+ member/2
    for O(n^2) duplicate detection. Correct for ARC-AGI-2 sized grids (<=30x30).
  tb_select_cols: inner findall iterates ColIdxs in the given order; column
    reordering is achieved by passing ColIdxs in a non-monotone order.
  tb_drop_col: between/3 + Ci \= C; picks all column indices except C.
    Integers compare with \= correctly when C is ground.
  tb_add_col: nth0/3 pairs Grid row I with NewCol element I; append/3 extends.
  tb_insert_row: two-clause recursion; base case R=0 prepends; recursive case
    decrements R and recurses on the tail. Terminates for all R in 0..H.
  tb_delete_row: findall with I \= R; simpler than recursion here.
  tb_swap_rows: fetches both rows with nth0 before rebuilding to avoid
    repeated nth0 calls inside the per-row if-then-else.
  tb_col_max_row/tb_col_min_row: two-step: collect all column C values,
    find extremum, then nth0+nth0+cut to locate first row. The cut ensures
    only the first tied row is returned.

Bug fixed during development: tb_filter_rows was initially declared as /3
in the module export list but is defined with 4 arguments (+Grid, +C, +V, -Filtered).
Fixed to tb_filter_rows/4.

Library imports:
  library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, append/3, max_list/2, min_list/2.
  keysort/2 is a built-in; not imported.

Tutorial chapter: docs/tutorial/Ch105_Table.txt.
SPARC volumes updated: Spec v109, Pseudo v102, Arch v103, Refinement v157,
  Completion v160.

END OF PART ARCH-110

PART ARCH-115: EDGE DETECTION AND BOUNDARY ANALYSIS PACK (WP 149)

Work Package: 149
Layer: 128
Module: edge
File: packs/edge/prolog/edge.pl
Test: packs/edge/test/test_edge.pl
Prefix: ed_*
Exports: 14 predicates

Design patterns:
- ed_h_edges and ed_v_edges use nested findall with between/3 for
  dimension iteration and nth0/3 for cell access. H-1 and W-1
  bounds are computed before the findall to avoid singleton warnings.
- ed_h_edge and ed_v_edge use if-then-else to produce Bool=1 or 0.
- ed_all_edges uses findall to add h-/v- direction tags to edge lists
  then appends and sorts.
- ed_boundary_cells uses a disjunctive findall body; for each matching
  cell the body succeeds if any of the four 4-neighbors has a different
  value. Left-column neighbor uses C0 is C-1 to avoid unevaluated C-1.
- ed_outer_boundary uses a simple disjunctive condition on row/column
  indices to collect all outer-border positions.
- ed_inner_cells delegates to ed_boundary_cells and uses negation-as-
  failure (\+ member) to exclude boundary cells from the result.
- ed_is_smooth delegates to ed_edge_count and checks for zero.
- ed_label_edges uses an outer findall over rows and an inner findall
  over columns; the private helper ed_has_diff_nbr_/6 encapsulates the
  four-direction if-then-else check.
- ed_has_edge/4 uses ed_has_diff_nbr_/6 directly.
- ed_corners uses a findall over all 2x2 top-left positions and
  negation-as-failure to select blocks where not all four cells are equal.
- Private helper ed_has_diff_nbr_(Grid,R,C,V,H1,W1) checks the four
  4-connected directions with bounds guards; uses nested if-then-else
  chains for short-circuit evaluation.

Dependencies: library(lists) for member/2, nth0/3. Built-ins: length/2,
  between/3, findall/3, sort/2, msort/2 (tests only).

Position in cognitive stack: Layer 128, after block (Layer 127) and
  before the next perceptual analysis layer.

Tutorial chapter: docs/tutorial/Ch110_Edge.txt.
SPARC volumes updated: Spec v114, Pseudo v107, Arch v108, Refinement v162,
  Completion v165.

PART ARCH-116: CELL DISTANCE AND PROXIMITY COMPUTATION PACK (WP 150)

Work Package: 150
Layer: 129
Module: distance
File: packs/distance/prolog/distance.pl
Test: packs/distance/test/test_distance.pl
Prefix: dt_*
Exports: 14 predicates

Design patterns:
- dt_manhattan, dt_chebyshev, dt_euclidean_sq are pure arithmetic
  predicates with no data structure traversal.
- dt_nearest and dt_farthest use findall to collect all D-R-C triples
  for cells matching Val, then delegate to private min_list_key_ or
  max_list_key_ helpers that implement accumulator-based min/max selection.
  Using @< / @> term ordering ensures row-major tie-breaking without
  an extra key extraction step.
- dt_all_at uses a findall with an equality guard on the computed
  Manhattan distance, followed by sort/2.
- dt_within_manhattan and dt_within_chebyshev use findall with an =<
  guard on the computed distance.
- dt_map_manhattan and dt_map_chebyshev pre-collect all Val-cell positions
  once (outer findall), then for each cell compute all distances to those
  positions and take the minimum using min_list/2 from library(lists).
  An if-then-else handles the absent-Val case by returning -1.
- dt_ring_manhattan is equivalent to dt_within_manhattan but with an
  equality guard rather than an inequality.
- dt_centroid collects all Val-cell positions, then uses two findall calls
  to separate row and column index lists, sums each with the private
  sumlist_/2 accumulator helper, and computes the integer floor centroid.
- dt_diameter_manhattan and dt_diameter_chebyshev enumerate all unordered
  pairs (A @< B guard avoids duplicates), compute the distance for each
  pair, then select the maximum using max_list_key_.
- Private helpers: min_list_key_/2 and max_list_key_/2 implement
  single-pass accumulator scans over D-... term lists using @< / @>
  term ordering. sumlist_/2 is a two-clause recursive accumulator.

Dependencies: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, min_list/2, max_list/2.
  library(apply): maplist/3. Built-ins: length/2, between/3, findall/3.

Position in cognitive stack: Layer 129, after edge (Layer 128) and
  before the next spatial analysis layer.

Tutorial chapter: docs/tutorial/Ch111_Distance.txt.
SPARC volumes updated: Spec v115, Pseudo v108, Arch v109, Refinement v163,
  Completion v166.

PART ARCH-117: GRID TOPOLOGY AND CONNECTED COMPONENT ANALYSIS PACK (WP 151)

Work Package: 151
Layer: 130
Module: topology
File: packs/topology/prolog/topology.pl
Test: packs/topology/test/test_topology.pl
Prefix: tp_*
Exports: 14 predicates

Design patterns:
- Core BFS: tp_grow_(Grid, Val, Queue, Visited, Result) uses memberchk/2
  for O(n) visited-set lookup. On each step: if head is in visited, skip;
  otherwise find all in-bounds Val-valued 4-neighbors via the tp_val_nbr_/7
  helper, append them to the queue, and recurse.
- tp_val_nbr_/7 uses a disjunctive clause body with explicit bounds checks
  and nth0/3 value checks to generate at most four neighbors per cell.
- tp_all_components: pre-collects and sorts all Val cells once, then
  calls tp_split_cells_ which uses subtract/3 from library(lists) to
  remove each found component from the remaining cell set.
- tp_split_cells_ head pattern: AllCells = [Seed|_] unification in the
  body (not the head) is required because Prolog clause heads cannot
  contain = terms. Base case handles empty list.
- tp_enclosed: seeds the BFS from all border cells with value Bg; the
  Val parameter is accepted but not used by the BFS (the BFS only steps
  through Bg cells). Enclosed cells are Bg cells not reached.
- tp_border_components: uses once/1 to find just one border-touching
  cell per component, preventing duplicate components in the findall
  result when multiple cells touch the border.
- tp_label_components: builds a flat R-C-Label list via tp_build_label_map_
  then uses member/2 with three bound args for lookup; non-Val cells
  default to 0 via if-then-else.
- tp_grow_plain_: variant of tp_grow_ that does not need Grid/Val but
  instead checks membership in an Allowed list of R-C pairs; used by
  tp_split_cells_plain_ for hole counting.

Dependencies: library(lists): member/2, memberchk/2, nth0/3, max_list/2,
  append/3, subtract/3. Built-ins: length/2, between/3, findall/3, sort/2.

Position in cognitive stack: Layer 130, after distance (Layer 129).

Tutorial chapter: docs/tutorial/Ch112_Topology.txt.

PART ARCH-118: ROW AND COLUMN PROJECTION AND PROFILE ANALYSIS PACK

Module: packs/projection/prolog/projection.pl
Pack descriptor: packs/projection/pack.pl
Test: packs/projection/test/test_projection.pl
Prefix: pj_*
Exports: 14 predicates

Design patterns:
- pj_row_sums and pj_row_maxes delegate directly to maplist(sum_list/max_list,
  Grid, Result), making them one-liners.
- All column operations share a private helper pj_col_(Grid, C, Col) which
  uses findall(V, (member(Row,Grid), nth0(C,Row,V)), Col) to extract the
  C-th column as a list.
- pj_row_counts and pj_col_counts use include(=(Val), List, Occ) followed by
  length/2 to count occurrences; =(Val) is a partial application of unification
  that acts as an equality test for ground integers.
- pj_shadow_h collects all column indices where Val appears anywhere in that
  column, then deduplicates with sort/2. pj_shadow_v is the row analogue.
- Run-length profiling uses pj_longest_run_/3 which delegates to
  pj_run_acc_/5: a tail-recursive accumulator that tracks current run length
  (Cur) and maximum seen so far (Max). On match: Cur1 is Cur+1, Max1 is
  max(Cur1,Max). On mismatch: reset Cur to 0, Max1 is max(Cur,Max). Final N
  is the Max at end of list.
- Modal value uses pj_mode_/2: sort for unique values, findall N-V pairs,
  then pj_max_pair_/2 recurse: prefer higher count; on count tie, prefer
  smaller value (V < BV guard). This gives smallest-value tie-breaking.
- Column width computed once via (Grid=[Fr|_] -> length(Fr,W) ; W=0) before
  the findall over between(0,W1,C); avoids repeated computation.

Dependencies: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, max_list/2, sum_list/2.
  library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3, include/3.
  Built-ins: length/2, between/3, findall/3, sort/2.

Position in cognitive stack: Layer 131, after topology (Layer 130).

Tutorial chapter: docs/tutorial/Ch113_Projection.txt.

PART ARCH-119: ROW AND COLUMN GRADIENT AND PROGRESSION ANALYSIS PACK

Module: packs/gradient/prolog/gradient.pl
Pack descriptor: packs/gradient/pack.pl
Test: packs/gradient/test/test_gradient.pl
Prefix: gr_*
Exports: 14 predicates

Design patterns:
- All row predicates use maplist/3 where the operation is a simple mapping
  (gr_h_diffs uses maplist(gr_adj_diffs_, Grid, DiffGrid); gr_h_mono uses
  maplist(gr_mono_, Grid, Flags); gr_h_cum uses maplist(gr_cumsum_, Grid,
  CumGrid); gr_h_second uses maplist(gr_second_diffs_, Grid, D2Grid)).
- All column predicates share the private helper gr_col_(Grid, C, Col) which
  uses findall(V, (member(Row,Grid), nth0(C,Row,V)), Col) to extract each
  column. Column width is computed once before findall via
  (Grid=[Fr|_] -> length(Fr,W) ; W=0).
- gr_adj_diffs_/2 is the core difference primitive: three clauses for [],
  [_], and [A,B|T]. The [A,B|T] clause recurses with [B|T] giving
  correct overlap. Used directly for gr_h_diffs and twice (via
  gr_second_diffs_) for gr_h_second.
- gr_v_diffs_ uses gr_pair_diffs_ to compute element-wise differences
  between adjacent row pairs, recursing with [R2|Rows] overlap.
- gr_v_second delegates to gr_v_diffs twice: gr_v_diffs(Grid, D1),
  gr_v_diffs(D1, D2Grid).
- gr_mono_ uses if-then-else over gr_is_nondec_/gr_is_noninc_ to classify
  in order: non-decreasing first (so constant sequences return 1).
- gr_v_cum_acc_ uses if-then-else on Prev=[] for the first row, then
  gr_row_add_ for subsequent rows. This avoids importing maplist/4.
- gr_cumsum_acc_ is a standard tail-recursive accumulator with Acc=0
  initial value.

Dependencies: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, max_list/2, min_list/2,
  last/2. library(apply): maplist/3.
  Built-ins: length/2, between/3, findall/3.

PART ARCH-120: 2D GRID EXTREMA, LOCAL PEAKS, AND THRESHOLD FILTERING PACK

Module: packs/extrema/prolog/extrema.pl
Pack descriptor: packs/extrema/pack.pl
Test: packs/extrema/test/test_extrema.pl
Prefix: ex_*
Exports: 14 predicates

Design patterns:
- ex_max_val and ex_min_val delegate to ex_flat_vals_ which collects all cell
  values via findall(V, (member(Row,Grid), member(V,Row)), Vals), then use
  max_list/min_list.
- ex_max_cells and ex_min_cells call ex_max_val/ex_min_val first, then use a
  findall over between for positional enumeration with nth0 value matching.
- ex_row_argmax/argmin use findall to collect sum-index pairs (sum_list per row),
  then ex_argmax_idx_/ex_argmin_idx_ which are recursive accumulators that
  compare only on strict > or < to preserve first-occurrence tie-breaking.
- ex_col_argmax/argmin use ex_col_sum_ (findall + sum_list per column) to
  produce sum-index pairs for the same accumulator.
- ex_local_max4 and ex_local_min4 use ex_all_nbr4_lt_/ex_all_nbr4_gt_ which
  compute the four neighbors explicitly (RU=R-1, RD=R+1, CL=C-1, CR=C+1),
  then call ex_check_nbr_lt_/gt_ which tests bounds and value with if-then-else;
  out-of-bounds neighbors silently succeed, making border cells eligible if they
  exceed all in-bounds neighbors they have.
- ex_above, ex_below, ex_nonzero follow the same findall + bounds + nth0 + arithmetic
  test pattern.
- ex_range: combines ex_flat_vals_ with max_list, min_list, and is/2 subtraction.

Dependencies: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, max_list/2, min_list/2,
  sum_list/2. Built-ins: length/2, between/3, findall/3.

PART ARCH-121: NAGGR PACK - LAYER 134

Position in cognitive stack:
Layer 134 sits immediately above the extrema pack (Layer 133, ex_*) and
below subsequent grid intelligence layers.  It extends the neighborhood
reasoning capacity of the platform by providing value-based aggregation
over 4- and 8-connected neighborhoods, complementing the count-based
automaton pack (Layer 120, at_*).

Design patterns used:
  Nested findall grid construction: the outer findall collects one row list
    per row index R; the inner findall collects one aggregate value per
    column index C within that row.
  In-bounds neighbor enumeration: the private helpers na_nbr4_vals_ and
    na_nbr8_vals_ use findall over member(DR-DC, offsets) with explicit
    bounds guards (NR >= 0, NR < H, NC >= 0, NC < W) to collect only
    in-bounds neighbor values.
  Empty-neighborhood sentinel: predicates that cannot produce a meaningful
    result for an empty value list (max, min, mean, range) return 0 via
    an if-then-else guard on Vals=[].

PART ARCH-122: MEDIAN PACK - LAYER 135

Work package: WP 156.
Layer number: 135.
Module name: median.
Source file: packs/median/prolog/median.pl.
Test file: packs/median/test/test_median.pl.
Predicate prefix: md_*.

Position in cognitive stack:
Layer 135 sits immediately above the naggr pack (Layer 134, na_*).  Together
they form a neighborhood statistics cluster: naggr provides sum/max/min/mean/
range/spread/diff over 4/8-connected neighborhoods; median provides the median
and median filter for those same neighborhoods.

Design patterns used:
  Lower/floor median via msort: msort/2 (built-in) preserves duplicates,
    ensuring the median is computed over all values including repetitions.
    sort/2 would remove duplicates and produce incorrect medians.
  Median index formula: for a sorted list of length N, the lower median is
    at 0-based index (N-1)//2.  This is the unique element for odd N and the
    lower of the two middle elements for even N.
  Nested findall for median filter: md_filter4 and md_filter8 use triple-nested
    findall: outer for rows, middle for cells, innermost for neighbor collection.
    The call to md_median incorporates another msort internally.
  Above/below selection: md_above, md_below, md_row_above, md_row_below,
    md_col_above, md_col_below all compute the relevant median first, then use
    findall with a strict arithmetic comparison to collect qualifying positions.

Exports: md_median/2, md_row/3, md_col/3, md_row_medians/2, md_col_medians/2,
  md_grid/2, md_filter4/2, md_filter8/2, md_above/2, md_below/2,
  md_row_above/3, md_row_below/3, md_col_above/3, md_col_below/3.

Library dependencies: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3.
Built-ins used: msort/2, length/2, between/3, findall/3.

Tutorial chapter: docs/tutorial/Ch117_Median.txt.
SPARC volumes updated: Spec v121, Pseudo v114, Arch v115, Refinement v169,
  Completion v172.

ARCH-123: Neighborhood Mode Filter Pack (nmode, Layer 136)

Pack name: nmode
Prefix: nm_*

Location: packs/nmode/
Files:
  pack.pl              - pack manifest
  prolog/nmode.pl      - 14 nm_* predicates + private helpers
  test/test_nmode.pl   - 42 PLUnit tests

Dependencies:
  library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, max_list/2
  Built-ins: msort/2, sort/2, length/2, between/3, findall/3

Private helpers:
  nm_nbr4_vals_/6  - collect in-bounds 4-neighbor values for one cell
  nm_nbr8_vals_/6  - collect in-bounds 8-neighbor values for one cell
  nm_freq_pairs_/2 - convert msort-sorted list to Value-Count pairs
  nm_count_prefix_/4 - count leading equal elements in a sorted list
  nm_pair_vals_/2  - extract count values from Key-Count pairs

Design notes:

  case from matching the final catch-all clause, ensuring nm_mode is
  deterministic and does not produce duplicate solutions inside findall.

  nm_uniform4/8 uses sort(NbrVals, [_]) as a one-step uniformity test:
  succeeds iff all neighbor values are identical (sort produces a singleton).

  nm_outlier4/8 computes the mode of the NEIGHBORS ONLY (cell excluded),
  then checks if the cell's own value differs. This detects cells that are
  anomalous relative to their surroundings.

ARCH-124: Dense Ranking Pack (rank, Layer 137)

Pack name: rank
Prefix: rk_*
Layer: 137
Location: packs/rank/
Files:
  pack.pl              - pack manifest
  prolog/rank.pl       - 14 rk_* predicates + private helpers
  test/test_rank.pl    - 42 PLUnit tests

Dependencies:
  library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3
  Built-ins: sort/2, msort/2, length/2, between/3, findall/3

Private helpers:
  rk_pos1_/3          - 1-based position in a sorted unique list
  rk_pos1_acc_/4      - tail-recursive accumulator for rk_pos1_
  rk_zip_/3           - zip two lists into V-I pairs
  rk_last_n_/3        - last N elements of a list
  rk_first_n_/3       - first N elements of a list
  rk_take_/3          - take at most N elements from front
  rk_drop_/3          - drop N elements from front

Design notes:
  rk_argsort_asc uses msort (stable sort) so equal values keep their
  original left-to-right positions in the indices.

  rk_argsort_desc negates each value before msort: negate(-V) then sort
  ascending gives descending order of V. Equal original values (same -V)
  also remain in original left-to-right order (msort stability).

  rk_col_dense uses a per-cell nested findall approach: for each (R,C),
  it re-computes the column values and ranks Cell (R,C) within them.
  This is O(H*W*H) but is simple and correct for small grids.

  rk_top_n and rk_bottom_n operate on DISTINCT values (not cell counts).
  If the top 2 distinct values each appear multiple times, all cells
  with those values are included.

ARCH-124 END

ARCH-126: cooccur pack (Layer 139, co_* prefix)

Location: packs/cooccur/prolog/cooccur.pl
Module: cooccur
Layer: 139
Prefix: co_

Purpose: Value co-occurrence and adjacency analysis for 2D integer grids.

Provides ordered horizontal, vertical, and diagonal adjacent value pair
enumeration; directed pair counting; undirected 4-adjacent pair counting;
universal and empty adjacency testing; isolated cell detection; border-value
enumeration; shared border testing; horizontal transition frequency tables;
and most-frequently-adjacent value lookup.

Dependencies: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, last/2, append/3.
              library(apply): include/3.
Built-ins: sort/2, msort/2, length/2, between/3, findall/3.

Public predicates (14):
  co_h_pairs/2, co_v_pairs/2, co_d_pairs_dr/2, co_d_pairs_dl/2,
  co_count_h/4, co_count_v/4, co_count_adj4/4,
  co_always_adj4/3, co_never_adj4/3,
  co_isolated4/3, co_border_vals/3, co_shared_border/3,
  co_row_transitions/2, co_most_common_adj4/3

Private helpers:
  co_row_adj_/3: backtracks over consecutive element pairs.
  co_col_adj_/4: backtracks over column-C values in adjacent row pairs.
  co_has_nonadj4_/3: finds V1 cell lacking V2 4-neighbor.

Design notes:
  co_v_pairs enumerates in column-major order (all rows for column 0 first).
  co_count_adj4 uses directed pair counts from h+v pairs:
    symmetric (V1==V2) counts V1-V1 directed pairs; asymmetric adds both
    directions. This gives undirected edge counts.
  co_shared_border uses deterministic cut after finding the first match.
  co_most_common_adj4 breaks ties by returning the largest value (last in
    msort of N-X pairs).

Test file: packs/cooccur/test/test_cooccur.pl (42 tests, all pass).
