ARCH-129: INDEX PACK - COORDINATE-VALUED GRID GENERATION (Layer 142)

Location: packs/index/prolog/index.pl
Prefix: ix_
Layer: 142
Work Package: 163

Purpose: The index pack fills a gap that no other pack addresses: generating
2D grids whose cell values are pure coordinate functions. These grids serve as
operands for arithmetic and masking operations rather than as grids to be
analyzed.

Coordinate grids generated:
  ix_row_grid: cell = R (identifies rows)
  ix_col_grid: cell = C (identifies columns)
  ix_sum_grid: cell = R+C (diagonal band index)
  ix_diff_grid: cell = R-C (anti-diagonal index, signed)
  ix_prod_grid: cell = R*C (product index)

Distance fields (from a reference point):
  ix_manhattan_grid: city-block distance
  ix_chebyshev_grid: chessboard-king distance; concentric rings

Modular stripe patterns:
  ix_mod_grid: (R+C) mod N; diagonal stripes
  ix_row_mod_grid: R mod N; horizontal stripes
  ix_col_mod_grid: C mod N; vertical stripes

Index-based selection and grid_arithmetic:
  ix_mask_rows: zero out rows not in an index list
  ix_mask_cols: zero out columns not in an index list
  ix_apply: elementwise binary Op between an index grid and a value grid
  ix_from: signed linear offsets from a reference point

Design note: All predicates use findall and between for grid construction.
No external packs are required. library(lists) provides member/2 and nth0/3.
All of length/2, between/3, and findall/3 are SWI-Prolog built-ins.

Relationship to other packs:
  arith: ar_cell_add etc. do elementwise arithmetic between two value grids.
    ix_apply extends this by using a coordinate grid as one operand.
  gridops: go_add/go_sub do elementwise arithmetic between value grids.
    index complements these by generating the coordinate operand.
  interleave: il_stride selects every Nth row; ix_mask_rows selects
    arbitrary rows by index list (not by stride).

END OF ARCH-129


ARCH-130: FOLD PACK

Location: packs/fold/prolog/fold.pl. Module: fold. Prefix: fd_*.
Layer 143 of the cognitive stack. Work Package 164.

The fold pack provides 14 predicates for grid folding, unfolding, and fold-symmetry
detection. It operates on grids represented as lists of rows (list of lists).

Splitting predicates:
    fd_split_h/4 uses list prefix via length/2 and append/3 to cut the row list
    at position R+1. fd_split_v/4 delegates to fd_split_row_/4 via maplist/4;
    each row is split by a length/2 prefix and append/3.

Overlay:
    fd_overlay/4 maps fd_overlay_row_/4 over paired rows. fd_overlay_row_/4 maps
    fd_overlay_cell_/4 over paired cells. The cell predicate is a two-clause
    definition: the first clause fires when the A-cell is not the background value
    (cut prevents fallback); the second clause fires when A-cell is background and
    B-cell is returned.

Folding:
    fd_fold_h/4 combines fd_split_h and a findall loop that maps each row index I
    in the top half to its mirror index K = R-I in the bottom half, then overlays.
    fd_fold_v/4 uses fd_split_v and maplist(fd_fold_row_v_) to process each row
    independently via a findall over column indices.

Unfolding:
    fd_unfold_h/2 uses reverse/2 and append/3 to stack a half-grid above its
    upside-down copy. fd_unfold_v/2 uses maplist(fd_mirror_row_) where each row
    is joined with its reverse.

Symmetry:
    fd_sym_h/2 and fd_sym_v/2 use forall/2 with the between-rows mirror formula
    (2R+1-I and 2C+1-J respectively). This formula is consistent with fd_fold_h
    and fd_fold_v: the fold crease sits between rows/cols R and R+1.
    fd_find_fold_h/2 and fd_find_fold_v/2 use between/3 with cut to return the
    first qualifying crease index.

Marker detection:
    fd_mark_row/3 uses between/3, nth0/3, and forall/member to find the first
    all-V row. fd_mark_col/3 uses between/3 and forall/member/nth0 to find the
    first all-V column.

Composition:
    fd_fold_both/5 sequences fd_fold_h and fd_fold_v, reducing a 2D grid to its
    top-left quadrant after two orthogonal folds.

Dependencies: library(lists) for member/2, nth0/3, append/2, append/3, reverse/2.
              library(apply) for maplist/3, maplist/4.
Built-ins used: between/3, forall/2, findall/3, length/2.

END OF ARCH-130


ARCH-131: ROTATION PACK

Location: packs/rotation/prolog/rotation.pl. Module: rotation. Prefix: ro_*.
Layer 144 of the cognitive stack. Work Package 165.

The rotation pack provides 14 predicates for 90/180/270 clockwise grid rotation,
rotational symmetry detection, cell coordinate rotation, overlay-based spin
operations, and rotation matching.

Core rotation:
    ro_rot90/2 uses nested findall loops to build each output row as column C of
    the input Grid read bottom-to-top (index H1-R). The output is W rows by H cols.
    ro_rot180/2 uses maplist(reverse) then reverse to flip each row and reverse row
    order; this is equivalent to the algebraic (R,C) -> (H-1-R, W-1-C) mapping.
    ro_rot270/2 uses nested findall to read column W1-C top-to-bottom for each
    output row C. The output is W rows by H cols (same as ro_rot90).
    ro_rot_n/3 dispatches via pattern-matched clauses with cuts to prevent
    choicepoints when N is ground.

Symmetry:
    ro_is_rot2 and ro_is_rot4 compute the relevant rotation and test structural
    equality (==). ro_sym_order uses two cuts to cascade: order 4 checked first
    (strongest), order 2 next, order 1 as fallback.
    ro_canonical uses msort on the 4-element rotation list; SWI-Prolog standard
    term ordering on lists is lexicographic, so the smallest-keyed rotation wins.

Cell rotation:
    ro_rotate_cells/5 uses findall with member/2 and a private ro_apply_cell_/7
    helper. Each clause of ro_apply_cell_ encodes one of the four formulas.
    For N=3 (270 CW), the formula is NR = W1-C, NC = R (old row becomes new col).

Overlay:
    ro_overlay_bg_, ro_overlay_rows_, and ro_overlay_grids_ are private helpers
    that implement the same background-priority overlay semantics as fd_overlay in
    the fold pack, but implemented locally to avoid cross-module dependencies.
    ro_spin2 overlays Grid with its 180-degree rotation.
    ro_spin4 chains four overlays in order: Grid, G90, G180, G270.

Matching:
    ro_match_rotation uses between/3 with a cut to find the first matching
    rotation index. ro_equiv_rotation wraps it without exposing the index.

Dependencies: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, reverse/2.
              library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3.
Built-ins used: between/3, length/2, findall/3, msort/2.

END OF ARCH-131

ARCH-132: WARP PACK (Layer 145, wr_* prefix)

Work Package 166. File: packs/warp/prolog/warp.pl. Module: warp.

Design notes:
The warp pack occupies Layer 145 and provides shear, cyclic shift, and non-uniform
grid warping. It depends on no other PrologAI packs; all needed helpers are private.

The central private helper is wr_shift_linear_(Row, N, Bg, Out) which shifts a list
rightward by N using a formula Out[C] = Row[C-N] (with Bg fill for out-of-bounds).
This single helper serves wr_shift_row, wr_shear_h, wr_unshear_h, and wr_skew_offsets.

Cyclic shifts use (C-N) mod W and (R-N) mod H. SWI-Prolog's mod/2 operator handles
negative N correctly via floored division, so no special-case is needed.

wr_shear_v and wr_cyclic_shear_v are implemented directly with nested findall over
(R, J) pairs rather than column extraction, for uniformity with the row-based approach.

wr_transpose_anti is implemented with a single nested findall. For square grids it
is an involution (applying it twice returns the original); for non-square grids the
output dimensions are W x H (transposed from H x W).

wr_find_shear_h and wr_find_shear_v search a bounded range -(W-1)..(W-1) or
-(H-1)..(H-1) by using between/3 with offset and cut after the first match.

Exported predicates (14): wr_shift_row/5, wr_shift_col/5, wr_shear_h/4, wr_shear_v/4,
wr_unshear_h/4, wr_unshear_v/4, wr_cyclic_h/3, wr_cyclic_v/3, wr_cyclic_shear_h/3,
wr_cyclic_shear_v/3, wr_skew_offsets/4, wr_transpose_anti/2, wr_find_shear_h/4,
wr_find_shear_v/4.

Dependencies: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, append/2, reverse/2.
              library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3.
Built-ins used: between/3, length/2, findall/3.

END OF ARCH-132

ARCH-133: BORDER PACK (Layer 146, br_* prefix)

Work Package 167. File: packs/border/prolog/border.pl. Module: border.

Design notes:
The border pack occupies Layer 146 and provides concentric ring analysis for 2D grids.
It depends on no other PrologAI packs; all needed helpers are private.

The central concept is the ring depth formula: br_ring_depth_(H, W, R, C, D) computes
D = min(R, H-1-R, C, W-1-C). Ring 0 is the outermost border; ring N is N steps inward.
The maximum ring index is (min(H,W)-1)//2. This formula is shared by br_ring_cells,
br_depth_map, br_fill_ring, and br_is_nested via between/forall.

br_ring_cells, br_depth_map, and br_fill_ring use nested findall with explicit evaluation
of H1 is H-1 and W1 is W-1 before calling between/3. SWI-Prolog between/3 requires
integer bounds; the compound term H-1 is not an integer and must be evaluated first.

br_add_border uses findall with member/2 and append/3 directly, rather than maplist
with partial application, to avoid arity confusion when prepending and appending V.

br_strip_border uses between(1, H2, R) with H2 is H-2 already evaluated, and similarly
between(1, W2, C) with W2 is W-2. This is the same pattern as the row/column extraction
in other packs.

br_inner_n is implemented with structural recursion: N=0 is the identity (cut), and
N>0 strips one ring then recurses with N-1. This avoids any need for accumulator state.

br_ring_colors_ uses three clauses: base case (N > MaxN returns []), success case
(ring N is uniform, collect its color and recurse), and fail case (ring N is not
uniform, return [] to stop collecting). The cut in the success clause prevents the
fail clause from firing when br_ring_color succeeds.

br_is_nested uses forall/2 with between/3: this is semantically equivalent to a
universal quantification over all ring indices and reads cleanly.

Exported predicates (14): br_ring_cells/3, br_ring_vals/3, br_ring_color/3,
br_is_uniform_ring/2, br_add_border/3, br_strip_border/2, br_inner_n/3,
br_outer_color/2, br_is_uniform_outer/1, br_ring_colors/2, br_max_ring/2,
br_is_nested/1, br_depth_map/2, br_fill_ring/4.

Dependencies: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, append/2, append/3.
              library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3.
Built-ins used: between/3, length/2, findall/3, forall/2, sort/2.

END OF ARCH-133


ARCH-134: SPLICE PACK DESIGN NOTES (Layer 147)

Module: splice. Prefix: sp_*. Layer: 147.
File: packs/splice/prolog/splice.pl.
Exports: 14 predicates (sp_insert_row/4, sp_delete_row/3, sp_insert_col/4,
  sp_delete_col/3, sp_swap_rows/4, sp_swap_cols/4, sp_reverse_rows/2,
  sp_reverse_cols/2, sp_rotate_rows/3, sp_rotate_cols/3, sp_replicate_row/4,
  sp_replicate_col/4, sp_select_rows/3, sp_select_cols/3).

Design rationale:

Row and column structural editing is a distinct capability from cell-level
value modification. Predicates such as sn_set_cell (scan pack) and bd_fill_bbox
(bound pack) change values at fixed positions; they cannot change the number of
rows or columns. The splice pack fills this gap by providing operations that
reshape the grid's structure.

Row operations (sp_insert_row, sp_delete_row, sp_swap_rows, sp_reverse_rows,
sp_rotate_rows, sp_replicate_row, sp_select_rows) work directly on the top-level
list of rows. Column operations (sp_insert_col, sp_delete_col, sp_swap_cols,
sp_reverse_cols, sp_rotate_cols, sp_replicate_col, sp_select_cols) are
implemented by applying a private row-level helper to every row via maplist.

Split-and-reassemble pattern:
All insertion and deletion predicates use length(Prefix, K) to create a list of
exactly K free variables, then append(Prefix, Suffix, List) to unify Prefix with
the first K elements of List and Suffix with the rest. This pattern avoids explicit
index arithmetic and works in both deterministic and generative modes.

Maplist arity:
Private helpers called via maplist take the fixed arguments (C, N, or Indices) as
leading parameters using partial application. For a 4-arg helper helper_(A, B, X, Y),
maplist(helper_(A, B), ListX, ListY) calls helper_(A, B, Elem, Out) for each pair,
which is a valid call at arity 4. This is verified for sp_insert_col_row_/4,
sp_delete_col_row_/3, sp_swap_in_row_/4, sp_rotate_row_cols_/3,
sp_replicate_col_in_row_/4, and sp_select_col_from_row_/3.

Cyclic rotation:
sp_rotate_rows and sp_rotate_cols both reduce K modulo the grid dimension before
splitting, so K values of 0, H (or W), 2H (or 2W), etc. all produce identity.
Negative K is not supported; callers should add H before calling if needed.

Replication with N=0:
sp_replicate_row(Grid, R, 0, Out) deletes row R; sp_replicate_col(Grid, C, 0, Out)
deletes column C. This makes replication a superset of deletion for rows and columns.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, append/2, append/3, reverse/2.
Library imports: library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3.
Built-ins: length/2, findall/3, between/3.

END OF ARCH-134


ARCH-135: OBJOP PACK DESIGN NOTES (Layer 148)

Module: objop. Prefix: oo_*. Layer: 148.
File: packs/objop/prolog/objop.pl.
Exports: 14 predicates (oo_cells_of/3, oo_bbox/5, oo_count/3, oo_size/4,
  oo_center/4, oo_erase/4, oo_repaint/4, oo_swap/4, oo_move/6, oo_copy/5,
  oo_rotate90/4, oo_rotate180/4, oo_mirror_h/4, oo_mirror_v/4).

Design rationale:

The cellset pack (Layer 117) handles object manipulation at the level of sparse
R-C position lists. The caller must convert from grid to cells, transform, and
convert back. The objop pack provides the same logical operations at the grid
level: each predicate accepts a full grid and a target color V, identifies all V
cells automatically, performs the transformation, and returns the modified grid.
This matches the common ARC-AGI-2 workflow of "find the red object and rotate it."

The central private helper oo_set_cells_(Grid, Cells, Val, Out) does a full grid
scan: for each cell (R,C), it checks memberchk(R-C, Cells) and writes Val if true,
or the original value if false. This is O(H*W*|Cells|) but acceptable for grids up
to 30x30 and objects up to 50 cells.

Rotation convention:
oo_rotate90 uses 90 degrees CW rotation where the top-left corner of the bounding
box is the pivot point. For a bounding box of height H, the formula in normalized
coordinates is (r, c) → (c, H-1-r). In absolute coordinates: NewR = R0+c, NewC =
C0+(H-1)-r where r=R-R0 and c=C-C0. This means:
- Top-left (0,0) → (0, H-1): top-left goes to top-right of the H-wide output row.
- Bottom-left (H-1,0) → (0,0): bottom-left goes to new top-left.
- Bottom-right (H-1,W-1) → (W-1,0): bottom-right goes to bottom-left.

After rotation, the new bounding box has height = old W and width = old H. The new
top-left is still (R0, C0). No clipping occurs since the formula stays within the
original bbox span (assuming a square bbox), but non-square bboxes may produce
cells outside the original bbox column range.

Mirror conventions:
oo_mirror_h flips cells left-right within the bounding box. All rows are unchanged
(NewR = R); only columns are swapped: NewC = C0+(W-1)-c where c=C-C0.
oo_mirror_v flips cells top-bottom within the bounding box. All columns unchanged;
rows are swapped: NewR = R0+(H-1)-r.

The swap predicate oo_swap assumes V1 and V2 are non-overlapping colors. When they
do overlap, the first pass (V1→V2) would write V2 over the overlap cells; the second
pass would then write V1 over the original V2 positions, which includes the overlap.
The result depends on the overlap geometry and is undefined.

Clipping in oo_move and oo_copy:
Both predicates filter new positions with between(0, H1, NewR) and
between(0, W1, NewC) where H1 = H-1 and W1 = W-1. Cells translated outside the
grid are silently dropped. This is the least-surprise behavior for most ARC-AGI
tasks where objects can slide to but not beyond the grid edge.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, memberchk/2, nth0/3, min_list/2,
max_list/2.
Built-ins: findall/3, sort/2, length/2, between/3.

END OF ARCH-135


ARCH-136: PAIR PACK DESIGN NOTES (Layer 149)

Module: pair. Prefix: pr_*. Layer: 149.
File: packs/pair/prolog/pair.pl.
Exports: 14 predicates (pr_obj_shape/2, pr_obj_color/2, pr_obj_size/2,
  pr_shape_eq/2, pr_color_eq/2, pr_size_eq/2, pr_group_color/2,
  pr_group_size/2, pr_group_shape/2, pr_unique_color/2, pr_unique_size/2,
  pr_match_color/3, pr_match_size/3, pr_match_shape/3).

Design rationale:

ARC-AGI-2 tasks frequently require pairing objects across two scenes: given input
objects A, B, C and output objects X, Y, Z, determine which input corresponds to
which output. The most common pairing keys are color, size (cell count), and
D4-canonical shape. The pair pack centralizes all three key types into a uniform
API so that higher-level ARC solvers do not need to re-implement the D4 computation
or the grouping logic for each task.

Objects are represented as obj(Color, Cells) terms where Cells is a sorted list of
r(R,C) terms. This representation was established by the scene pack (Layer 37) and
is used consistently throughout the ARC-AGI-2 pack stack. The pair pack does not
define the object representation; it only defines operations on it.

D4 canonical shape:
The 8 D4 symmetry operations form the dihedral group of order 8, which is the
symmetry group of a square. For ARC-AGI-2 tasks, two objects that are related by
any D4 transformation should be considered shape-equivalent. The canonical shape
is the lexicographic minimum across all 8 transforms, computed as follows:

1. Normalize the cell list to the origin (min row = 0, min col = 0).
2. Compute H1 = max row index, W1 = max col index of the normalized cells.
3. Apply each of the 8 ops: id, r90, r180, r270, fh, fv, fd1, fd2.
4. After each op, normalize the result to origin and sort.
5. Take the lex-min across all 8 sorted normalized lists.

The private predicate pr_cell_d4_(Op, H1, W1, r(R,C), r(NR,NC)) applies a single
D4 operation to a single cell. H1 and W1 are computed once per object from the
normalized bounding box and reused across all 8 transforms and all cells.

The private predicate pr_min_term_(A, B, Min) returns the lex-min of two Prolog
terms using the @< operator. It is used with foldl over the 8 transform results to
find the canonical shape.

Grouping architecture:
The three grouping predicates (pr_group_color, pr_group_size, pr_group_shape) all
follow the same two-phase pattern:
  Phase 1: collect all distinct key values with findall + sort.
  Phase 2: for each key, collect all objects having that key with findall.
This produces a sorted list of Key-[Obj,...] pairs. The sort in Phase 1 ensures
deterministic ordering. The sublists preserve the original order of Objs because
findall preserves the order of solutions.

Unique predicates:
pr_unique_color and pr_unique_size use the grouping predicates then search for a
group whose object list has exactly one element (a singleton). The built-in pattern
member(_-[Obj], Groups) unifies only when the list has exactly one element. If zero
or more than one singleton group exists, member fails and the predicate fails. This
is the correct behavior for ARC tasks where a "unique" object is meaningful only
when exactly one such object exists.

Match predicates:
The three match predicates (pr_match_color, pr_match_size, pr_match_shape) compute
the full cross-product of Objs1 and Objs2 filtered by equal key. The result is a
list of Key-Obj1-Obj2 triples. Multiple pairs per key are allowed; the caller is
responsible for selecting a one-to-one assignment if needed. The triples are
returned in the order Prolog explores the cross-product (outer loop on Objs1, inner
loop on Objs2).

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, min_list/2, max_list/2.
Built-ins: findall/3, sort/2, length/2.

END OF ARCH-136


ARCH-137: ARRANGE PACK DESIGN NOTES (Layer 150)

Pack: arrange
Prefix: ag_
Layer: 150
Location: packs/arrange/prolog/arrange.pl
Tests: packs/arrange/test/test_arrange.pl

Purpose:
The arrange pack provides arrangement-level reasoning over lists of obj(Color, Cells)
terms. Where the pair pack (Layer 149) asks "are these two objects the same shape?",
the arrange pack asks "where are these objects positioned relative to each other, and
what is their spatial arrangement?". This pack enables sorting objects by position,
detecting evenly-spaced grids of objects, computing the collective bounding box of a
group, and finding the nearest neighbor.

Design principles:

1. Centroid as the position representative: All positional predicates use the integer
   (floor-average) centroid of the cell list as the object's representative point.
   This is invariant to color and reflects the geometric center of the shape.

2. Stable sorting: ag_sort_by_row and ag_sort_by_col use keysort/2, which is stable.
   Objects with equal centroid positions preserve their original relative order. This
   is important for deterministic behavior when objects share a row or column.

3. Gap analysis via sort + consecutive difference: ag_row_gaps and ag_col_gaps use
   sort/2 to deduplicate and order centroid coordinates, then ag_consec_gaps_ to
   compute the differences. Deduplication before gap computation means that two objects
   at the same centroid row contribute only one position to the gap list.

4. The ag_consec_gaps_ private helper: Three clauses cover [], [_] (with cut), and
   [A,B|T]. The cut on the singleton clause prevents choicepoint warnings when the
   recursive case eventually reduces to a one-element list.

5. Manhattan distance for nearest neighbor: ag_nearest uses Manhattan (L1) distance
   between centroids. This is consistent with the spatial pack's sp_distance_manhattan
   predicate and is the natural distance for grid-based scenes.

Predicate count: 14 public predicates (ag_centroid/2, ag_offset/3, ag_row_order/2,
ag_col_order/2, ag_row_aligned/2, ag_col_aligned/2, ag_sort_by_row/2, ag_sort_by_col/2,
ag_row_gaps/2, ag_col_gaps/2, ag_equal_row_gaps/1, ag_equal_col_gaps/1,
ag_group_bbox/5, ag_nearest/3).

Private helpers: ag_consec_gaps_/2, ag_all_equal_/1.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, min_list/2, max_list/2, sum_list/2.
Built-ins: findall/3, sort/2, keysort/2, length/2.

Tests: 42 PLUnit tests (3 per predicate). All pass with no warnings.

END OF ARCH-137


ARCH-138: XFORM PACK DESIGN NOTES (Layer 151)

Pack: xform
Prefix: xf_
Layer: 151
Location: packs/xform/prolog/xform.pl
Tests: packs/xform/test/test_xform.pl

Purpose:
The xform pack provides object-level transformation and transformation-inference tools.
Existing packs handle scenes (scene), object properties and grouping (pair), and object
positions (arrange). The xform pack handles the question "what happened to this object?"
by providing tools to both apply transformations (recolor, translate, D4 ops) and to
discover what transformation connects two versions of an object.

Design:

Applied transformations: xf_recolor, xf_translate, xf_normalize, xf_d4.
These take an obj term and return a new obj term. xf_d4 normalizes the input, applies
the D4 operation (producing another normalized result since all 8 D4 ops are
origin-preserving on normalized inputs), then translates back to the original top-left
corner. xf_normalize is the foundation for all shape-invariant comparisons.

xf_same_cells: Implemented as a one-clause predicate with Cells as a shared variable
between both arguments. This forces exact cell-set identity via Prolog unification.

xf_cell_offset: Normalizes both inputs and requires the normalized cell sets to unify.
The offset is computed from the top-left corner differences. Fails naturally for objects
with different shapes.

xf_is_recolor: Similar one-clause design with shared Cells. Adds C1 \= C2 to require
different colors.

Cell grid_arithmetic: xf_cells_added, xf_cells_removed, xf_cells_kept use subtract/3 (from
library(lists)) and findall+memberchk for the intersection. xf_overlap_count wraps
xf_cells_kept with length.

xf_any_d4: Tries all 8 D4 ops via member, applies each to the normalized Obj1 cells,
sorts, and tests against the normalized Obj2 cells. A cut after the first match makes
the predicate deterministic (returns the first matching op in the canonical order).

xf_scale_factor: Uses integer arithmetic (mod, //) to test exact divisibility and
return the scale ratio. Returns N=1 when both objs have the same number of cells.

xf_merge: Uses append/3 followed by sort/2. sort/2 deduplicates overlapping cells
and produces a canonical sorted list. Colors must unify, preventing merge of
different-colored objects.

Private helper xf_cell_d4_: The same 8-case D4 transform as in the pair pack, defined
locally to keep the pack self-contained.

Tests: 42 PLUnit tests (3 per predicate). All pass with no warnings.

END OF ARCH-138


ARCH-139: QUERY PACK (qu_*, Layer 152)

Pack: packs/query/
Files:
  pack.pl               (name, version, requires)
  prolog/query.pl       (14 qu_* predicates, 2 private helpers)
  test/test_query.pl    (42 PLUnit tests)

Layer: 152 (aggregate queries over object lists)
Module: query
Prefix: qu_

Design

The query pack treats a list of obj(Color, Cells) terms as the unit of analysis and
answers aggregate questions about that collection. All 14 public predicates are
deterministic.

Two-Phase Count Pattern

qu_count_by_color, qu_count_by_size, and qu_count_by_form all use the same two-phase
pattern:
  1. Collect all key values with findall; sort/2 deduplicates.
  2. For each distinct key, count matching objs with a nested findall + length.
This produces a sorted list of Key-N pairs without requiring any assert/retract or
dynamic state.

Exact Form vs D4-Invariant Shape

The "form" of an object (used by qu_count_by_form and qu_all_same_form) is its
origin-normalized cell list: the cell set translated so that the minimum row and
column are both zero, then sorted. This is an exact structural match, not D4-invariant.
Two L-shaped objects rotated by 90 degrees have different forms even though they are
D4-equivalent shapes. The private qu_norm_ helper (two-step findall: extract row/col
minimums, then translate) implements this normalization. It is deliberately kept
self-contained rather than importing normalization from the pair or xform packs.

Tie-Breaking

qu_most_frequent_color and qu_least_frequent_color break ties by returning the smallest
color value. Since qu_count_by_color returns pairs sorted by color (ascending), the
first matching pair in the list is always the smallest color at the target count.
qu_largest_obj and qu_smallest_obj break ties by returning the first object in the
input list. findall preserves input order, so the first member+cut match is the
correct tie-break.

Uniformity Tests

qu_all_same_color, qu_all_same_size, and qu_all_same_form use the pattern:
  findall all values -> sort -> require [_] (singleton after deduplication).
This is concise and idiomatic. Fails for empty lists (findall returns [], sort gives
[], not a singleton), but empty object lists are not valid inputs for these predicates.

Cut Usage

The five extremum predicates (qu_most_frequent_color, qu_least_frequent_color,
qu_largest_obj, qu_smallest_obj) all end with member(Key-Obj, List), !. The member
call finds the first match; the cut prevents any further backtracking so the predicate
is deterministic and leaves no choicepoints.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, min_list/2, max_list/2, sum_list/2.
Built-ins: findall/3, sort/2, length/2.

Tests: 42 PLUnit tests (3 per predicate). All pass with no warnings.

END OF ARCH-139


ARCH-140: SIFT PACK (si_*, Layer 153)

Pack: packs/sift/
Files:
  pack.pl               (name, version, requires)
  prolog/sift.pl        (14 si_* predicates, 2 private helpers)
  test/test_sift.pl     (42 PLUnit tests)

Layer: 153 (object list filtering by attribute predicates)
Module: sift
Prefix: si_

Design

The sift pack is the set-theoretic complement to the query pack. Where query asks
aggregate questions ("how many objects are color 1?", "what is the most frequent
color?"), sift returns the subset of objects satisfying a given predicate. All 14
predicates use findall to collect matching objects into an output list. Empty output
is valid: no predicate fails when no objects match.

findall-Based Filtering Pattern

Every predicate body has the form:
  findall(O, (member(O, Objs), O = obj(...), <condition>), Out)
The member call iterates the input list; the unification pattern extracts color and
cells; the condition applies the test. This is uniform, deterministic, and preserves
input list order.

Self-Contained Normalization

si_by_form uses a private si_norm_ helper for origin normalization, identical in
logic to qu_norm_ in the query pack but defined locally. This keeps the sift pack
independent without requiring imports from other packs.

si_max_size and si_min_size vs qu_largest_obj and qu_smallest_obj

The query pack's qu_largest_obj and qu_smallest_obj return only the FIRST tied
object (member+cut). The sift pack's si_max_size and si_min_size return ALL tied
objects. This is the appropriate behavior for filtering: the caller often wants all
objects at the extreme ("keep all the biggest ones"), not just the first. Two-phase
approach: collect all sizes, find the extreme, then select all objects at the extreme.

si_unique_color and si_shared_color

Both use the same two-phase count pattern as the query pack's qu_count_by_color:
  1. Collect all colors -> sort for distinct keys -> count per key.
  2. Collect colors with count = 1 (unique) or count > 1 (shared).
  3. Filter the original Objs list keeping only objects with a selected color.

Border Detection

si_on_border_ is a four-clause helper with cuts. The first matching clause fires and
commits:
  - R =:= 0 (top row)
  - R =:= H-1 (bottom row)
  - C =:= 0 (left column)
  - C =:= W-1 (right column)
The cuts in the first three clauses prevent evaluating subsequent clauses once a
border condition is found.

si_on_border uses member to find any border cell, succeeding on the first.
si_off_border uses \+ (member + si_on_border_) to test absence of any border cell.
The \+ operator in SWI-Prolog is the standard negation-as-failure, which is
appropriate here: an object is off the border if no cell matches the border condition.

Singleton variable suppression: the first (R=:=0) and third (C=:=0) clauses of
si_on_border_ don't need all four head arguments; unused arguments are named _H, _W
to suppress singleton warnings while keeping the arity consistent.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, memberchk/2, min_list/2, max_list/2.
Built-ins: findall/3, sort/2, length/2.

Tests: 42 PLUnit tests (3 per predicate). All pass with no warnings.

END OF ARCH-140


ARCH-141: PIGMENT PACK (pg_*, Layer 154)

Pack: packs/pigment/
Files:
  pack.pl               (name, version, requires)
  prolog/pigment.pl     (14 pg_* predicates, 1 private helper)
  test/test_pigment.pl  (42 PLUnit tests)

Layer: 154 (bulk color operations on object scenes)
Module: pigment
Prefix: pg_

Design

The pigment pack operates at the scene level (list of obj terms), in contrast to the
xform pack which operates on individual obj terms. Every predicate takes an Objs list
and returns a new list Out.

If-Then-Else Inside findall

Many pigment predicates use the pattern:
  findall(O, (member(obj(C,Cells), Objs), (Cond -> O=ObjA ; O=ObjB)), Out)
This applies a conditional transformation to every object in a single findall. The
if-then-else inside findall is a standard SWI-Prolog idiom: because findall creates
a fresh scope, backtracking from if-then-else does not affect the outer scope.

pg_apply_table vs pg_apply_table_strict

pg_apply_table is lenient: objects not found in the table keep their original color.
This models "apply the rule where it applies, keep everything else unchanged."

pg_apply_table_strict is a filter: objects not found in the table are excluded from
the output entirely. This models "only objects that follow the rule appear in output."

pg_infer_table: Identity of Cell Sets

pg_infer_table matches objects by identical cell sets (same position, same shape).
This is stricter than shape-equivalence (D4): two objects must have exactly the same
sorted r(R,C) list. This is appropriate for inferring color maps between input and
output scenes where objects stay in place but change color.

Frequency-Targeted Recoloring

pg_majority_to, pg_minority_to, pg_unique_to, and pg_shared_to all follow the same
structure: (1) compute color counts via pg_count_by_color_; (2) identify the target
color(s); (3) apply conditional recoloring via findall + if-then-else.

The private helper pg_count_by_color_ encapsulates the two-phase findall+sort count
pattern shared by these four predicates.

pg_zip_recolor: Recursive with Cuts

pg_zip_recolor uses three clauses with cuts on the two base cases. The first clause
handles empty Objs (stop regardless of Colors), the second handles empty Colors (stop
regardless of Objs), and the third recurses. Cuts prevent the SWI-Prolog indexer
from leaving choicepoints when one list ends before the other.

pg_consistent: Negation-as-Failure

pg_consistent uses \+ to test the absence of a contradiction. The inner goal succeeds
if any pair of entries shares a From color but maps to different To colors. \+ negates
this: the predicate succeeds iff no such contradiction exists. This is idiomatic
Prolog for "there is no X satisfying P(X)."

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, memberchk/2, min_list/2, max_list/2.
Built-ins: findall/3, sort/2, length/2.

Tests: 42 PLUnit tests (3 per predicate). All pass with no warnings.

END OF ARCH-141


ARCH-142: Delta Pack (dl_* Prefix, Layer 155)

Location: packs/delta/prolog/delta.pl
Pack manifest: packs/delta/pack.pl
Tests: packs/delta/test/test_delta.pl

The delta pack occupies Layer 155 and provides scene-level delta analysis. It operates exclusively on the obj(Color, Cells) scene representation (lists of obj terms) and computes what changed between two scenes.

Dependencies: none. Uses member/2 and sum_list/2 from library(lists); all other predicates (findall/3, sort/2, length/2, \+) are built-ins.

Interface: 14 dl_* predicates exported from module delta. Predicate groups:
- Change decomposition: dl_added/3, dl_removed/3, dl_recolored/3, dl_unchanged/3
- Matching: dl_matched/3
- Color analysis: dl_color_gain/3, dl_color_loss/3
- Numeric metrics: dl_count_diff/3, dl_size_diff/3
- Change type tests: dl_is_added_only/2, dl_is_removed_only/2, dl_is_recolor_only/2, dl_is_stable/2
- Composite: dl_scene_diff/3

Matching semantics: object matching is by exact cell-set equality via Prolog unification. This is consistent with the pigment pack's pg_infer_table approach and requires no external imports.

Test count: 42 (3 per predicate).


ARCH-143: Group Pack (gp_* Prefix, Layer 156)

Location: packs/group/prolog/group.pl
Pack manifest: packs/group/pack.pl
Tests: packs/group/test/test_group.pl

The group pack occupies Layer 156 and partitions object scenes into Key-[Objs] groups. It extends the scene-analysis stack beyond query (statistics), sift (filtering), pigment (recoloring), and delta (change detection) by enabling partition-then-operate patterns required by ARC-AGI-2 compositional rules.

Dependencies: none. Uses member/2, memberchk/2, min_list/2, max_list/2 from library(lists); built-ins findall/3, sort/2, length/2.

Private helper: gp_norm_/2 computes origin-normalized form (same algorithm as qu_norm_ in query pack and si_norm_ in sift pack, but privately defined for self-containment).

Interface: 14 gp_* predicates in five categories:
- Partition: gp_by_color/2, gp_by_size/2, gp_by_row/2, gp_by_col/2, gp_by_form/2
- Aggregate: gp_size_of/2, gp_flatten/2, gp_group_sizes/2, gp_all_same_size/1, gp_keys/2
- Extrema: gp_largest_group/2, gp_smallest_group/2
- Filter: gp_singleton_groups/2, gp_shared_groups/2

Determinism: gp_largest_group and gp_smallest_group use cut after finding the extremal cardinality and memberchk for final Key-Grp retrieval. All other predicates are deterministic via findall.

Test count: 42 (3 per predicate).

ARCH-156: objchain pack

Pack: objchain
Module: objchain
Prefix: ch_

Purpose: Linear chain analysis for obj(Color, Cells) collections. Depends on: (none)
Exports: os_bbox/5, os_normalize/2, os_translate/4, os_reflect_h/2, os_reflect_v/2, os_rotate180/2, os_rotate90/2, os_is_hsymm/1, os_is_vsymm/1, os_is_rot180/1, os_is_rot90/1, os_has_symmetry/1, os_symmetries/2, os_equivalent/2

Purpose: Bounding-box-relative symmetry analysis for obj(Color, Cells) terms. os_bbox extracts the bounding box (min/max row and column). os_normalize translates the object so its bbox top-left is at r(0,0). os_translate shifts all cells by (DR, DC). os_reflect_h mirrors each cell left-right about the vertical center axis (new C = MinC+MaxC-C). os_reflect_v mirrors top-bottom (new R = MinR+MaxR-R). os_rotate180 applies both flips simultaneously. os_rotate90 performs 90-degree CW rotation normalized to origin (new NR = C-MinC, new NC = MaxR-R). Symmetry tests compare msorted cell sets of original vs. transformed. os_is_rot90 normalizes both before and after rotation for position-independent comparison. os_has_symmetry succeeds on the first passing test (cut). os_symmetries builds a list of symmetry atoms via findall and case dispatch. os_d4_orbit_ (private) generates all 8 D4 orientations by applying 3 additional 90-degree rotations and the reflection-then-rotation variants. os_equivalent normalizes Obj1, then iterates os_d4_orbit_(Obj2) until a matching sorted cell set is found (cut after first match); color is ignored.

ARCH-158: objbound pack

Pack: objbound
Module: objbound
Prefix: ob_
Layer: 171
Depends on: (none)
Exports: ob_bbox_h/2, ob_bbox_w/2, ob_bbox_area/2, ob_is_rect/1, ob_is_hline/1, ob_is_vline/1, ob_is_single/1, ob_is_square_bbox/1, ob_holes/2, ob_n_holes/2, ob_is_hollow/1, ob_is_frame/1, ob_perimeter/2, ob_dense_hull/2

Purpose: Shape classification and bounding-box analysis for obj(Color, Cells) terms. Private ob_bbox_ helper collects row and column indices via findall then applies min_list/max_list. ob_bbox_h and ob_bbox_w compute height (MaxR-MinR+1) and width (MaxC-MinC+1). ob_bbox_area multiplies them. ob_is_rect compares cell count to bbox area. ob_is_hline and ob_is_vline test H=1 or W=1. ob_is_single tests both. ob_is_square_bbox tests H=W. ob_holes uses findall with between/3 over the bbox and \+ memberchk exclusion. ob_n_holes delegates to length. ob_is_hollow tests N>0. ob_is_frame requires H>=3, W>=3, forall border cells memberchk, and \+ existential test for interior cells. ob_cell_exposed_ is a private helper that counts non-object 4-adjacent neighbors via findall. ob_perimeter sums ob_cell_exposed_ over all cells and uses sum_list. ob_dense_hull generates all cells in the bbox with between/3 and packages with the original color.

ARCH-159: Objrel Pack (or_*, Layer 172)

Pack: objrel
Layer: 172
Depends on: (none)
Exports: or_overlap/2, or_shared_cells/3, or_n_shared/3, or_touch4/2, or_touch8/2, or_contains/2, or_union_cells/3, or_dist/3, or_manhattan/3, or_direction/3, or_aligned_h/2, or_aligned_v/2, or_gap_rows/3, or_gap_cols/3

Purpose: Pairwise geometric and spatial relation predicates for obj(Color, Cells) terms. Colors are ignored throughout. Private or_centroid_ computes floating-point centroid (sum_rows/N, sum_cols/N) via findall and sumlist. Private or_bbox_ collects row/col extremes via findall and min_list/max_list. Private or_dir_ maps centroid delta (DR, DC) to a compass direction atom (n/s/e/w/ne/nw/se/sw/same) using arithmetic comparisons. or_overlap: member + memberchk with cut. or_shared_cells: findall + memberchk filter. or_n_shared: length of shared cells. or_touch4: \+ overlap guard then member pair with Manhattan distance = 1 and cut. or_touch8: \+ overlap guard then member pair with max(|DR|,|DC|) = 1 and cut. or_contains: forall + memberchk. or_union_cells: append + sort. or_dist: sqrt of squared centroid deltas. or_manhattan: abs sum of centroid deltas. or_direction: centroid deltas fed to or_dir_. or_aligned_h/v: centroid row/col arithmetic equality. or_gap_rows/cols: max(0, max(MinR1,MinR2) - min(MaxR1,MaxR2) - 1) formula applied to bbox extremes.

ARCH-160: Objfilter Pack (of_*, Layer 173)

Pack: objfilter
Layer: 173
Depends on: (none — all shape tests re-implemented with private helpers)

Both are declared with :- meta_predicate.

ARCH-161: Canvas Pack (cv_*, Layer 174)

Pack: canvas
Module: canvas
Prefix: cv_
Layer: 174
Depends on: (none)
Exports: cv_blank/4, cv_size/3, cv_paint/3, cv_paint_all/3, cv_paint_at/5,
         cv_paint_clip/3, cv_paint_bg/4, cv_erase/4, cv_extract/3,
         cv_extract_all/3, cv_render/5, cv_move/6, cv_stamp/3, cv_blit/5

Purpose: Grid canvas creation and obj(Color, Cells) rendering. cv_blank creates

at a given position. Private helpers cv_paint_cells_ and cv_erase_cells_ perform
single-pass grid rebuilds using findall with nth0 enumeration.

ARCH-172: ruleinfer Pack (ri_*, Layer 185)

Purpose: Infers which scene-level transformation was applied to a Before scene

ARCH-173: sceneapply Pack (sa_*, Layer 186)

Pack: sceneapply
Prefix: sa_*
Layer: 186
Directory: packs/sceneapply/
Entry point: packs/sceneapply/prolog/sceneapply.pl
Test file: packs/sceneapply/test/test_sceneapply.pl
WP: 207

Purpose: Applies symbolic rule terms to obj(Color, Cells) scene lists. Complements
ruleinfer (ri_*, Layer 185) which infers rules from Before-After pairs.

Rule term vocabulary: recolor(Old,New), recolor_all(New), color_map(Map),
shift(DR,DC), to_origin, reflect_h(Width), reflect_v(Height), remove_color(Color),
keep_color(Color), sort_size_desc, sort_size_asc, sort_pos, top_n(N), dedup_form.

Single-rule evaluation: sa_apply dispatches on rule term structure to the
appropriate private helper (maplist, include, msort-keyed sort, accumulator).

Sequential evaluation: sa_apply_seq is a recursive descent over a rule list,
threading the scene through each rule in order.

Verification: sa_verify and sa_verify_seq apply the rule(s) and compare the
result to the expected output using msort (order-insensitive comparison).

Multi-pair verification: sa_verify_all and sa_verify_seq_all use forall over
a list of Before-After pairs.

Classification: sa_rule_type maps each rule term to its category;
sa_is_color_rule, sa_is_spatial_rule, sa_is_filter_rule delegate to it.

Composition utilities: sa_compose, sa_seq_len, sa_colors_affected, sa_rule_invertible.

Private helpers: sa_color_, sa_size_, sa_norm_, sa_topleft_, sa_recolor_atom_,
sa_set_color_, sa_apply_map_, sa_shift_obj_, sa_reflect_h_obj_, sa_reflect_v_obj_,
sa_is_color_, sa_not_color_, sa_scene_bbox_, sa_dedup_form_acc_.

Dependencies: None. Uses library(lists) and library(apply).

Position in dependency graph: Layer 186. Paired with ruleinfer (Layer 185, ri_*)
to form the complete rule-learn-and-apply cycle at the scene level.

ARCH-174: condxf Pack (xc_*, Layer 187)

Pack: condxf
Prefix: xc_*
Layer: 187
Directory: packs/condxf/
Entry point: packs/condxf/prolog/condxf.pl
Test file: packs/condxf/test/test_condxf.pl
WP: 208

Purpose: Applies transformations to a subset of objects in an obj(Color, Cells)
scene list — those satisfying a condition — while leaving the remaining objects
unchanged. Complements scenexf (sx_*, Layer 184), which applies transformations
uniformly to all objects.

Color-based conditional: xc_split_color partitions by color atom equality;
xc_recolor_matching, xc_shift_color, xc_move_color, xc_swap_colors all operate
only on objects matching a color condition.

Size-based conditional: xc_recolor_by_size uses a comparison operator (gt/lt/eq/
ge/le) against a cell-count threshold. xc_split_size partitions by the same
comparison. xc_largest and xc_smallest select the extreme objects by cell count;
xc_recolor_largest and xc_recolor_smallest recolor them. xc_unique_size selects
objects whose cell count appears exactly once.

Tie-breaking: xc_largest and xc_smallest use msort with keyed pairs (-N-Obj and
N-Obj respectively). When sizes are equal, standard term order on the obj term
breaks ties deterministically.

Grouping utilities: xc_merge concatenates two object groups; xc_split_color and
xc_split_size partition a scene into two groups.

Private helpers: xc_color_/2, xc_size_/2, xc_size_cmp_/3, xc_recolor_if_match_/4,
xc_shift_if_color_/5, xc_swap_one_/4, xc_recolor_if_size_/5, xc_recolor_if_obj_/4.

Dependencies: None. Uses library(lists) and library(apply).

Position in dependency graph: Layer 187. Natural partner to scenexf (Layer 184,
uniform transforms) and sceneapply (Layer 186, rule-term dispatch). Together they
provide both uniform and selective scene transformation.

ARCH-175: scenepair Pack (ps_*, Layer 188)

Pack: scenepair
Prefix: ps_*
Layer: 188
Directory: packs/scenepair/
Entry point: packs/scenepair/prolog/scenepair.pl
Test file: packs/scenepair/test/test_scenepair.pl
WP: 209

Purpose: Analyzes a Before and After scene pair holistically, computing
scene-level observables useful for transformation rule hypothesis ranking.
Given two obj(Color, Cells) lists, it answers: did the object count change?
what was added or removed? did the color set change? what color substitutions
occurred? was this a uniform shift, a shift to origin, or a recolor-all?

Object identity: ps_added_objs and ps_removed_objs use color-atom equality and
normalized form equality (translate min-row/col to 0, msort cells) to define
object matching. This is more robust than positional identity.

Color observables: ps_color_set_before/after compute sorted dedup color lists;
ps_same_color_set compares them; ps_color_delta computes a list of Old-New pairs
from position-matched object pairs; ps_is_recolor detects single-color replacement
via set differences; ps_is_recolor_all detects uniform recolor.

Spatial observables: ps_is_shift derives a candidate (DR, DC) from the first
object, then verifies across the entire scene with msort. A cut after verification
makes it deterministic. ps_is_to_origin checks shift-to-bounding-box-origin.

Structure observables: ps_same_n_objs checks count equality; ps_size_preserved
checks position-matched cell-count equality.

Private helpers: ps_color_/2, ps_cells_/2, ps_size_/2, ps_norm_/2, ps_match_/2,
ps_distinct_colors_/2, ps_dedup_/2, ps_topleft_/2, ps_scene_bbox_/5,
ps_shift_obj_/4, ps_color_delta_acc_/3, ps_same_size_/2.

Dependencies: None. Uses library(lists) and library(apply).

Position in dependency graph: Layer 188. Builds on the scene representation
established by all prior scene-level packs (scenecmp, scenexf, ruleinfer,
sceneapply, condxf) but does not import any of them. Provides the observational
layer for rule hypothesis ranking packs that follow.

ARCH-176: scenerank Pack (rk_*, Layer 189)

Pack: scenerank
Prefix: rk_*
Layer: 189
Directory: packs/scenerank/
Entry point: packs/scenerank/prolog/scenerank.pl
Test file: packs/scenerank/test/test_scenerank.pl
WP: 210

Purpose: Ranks candidate symbolic rule terms by coverage and consistency across
a list of Before-After scene pair training examples. Provides the selection step
of the learn-and-apply cycle: after inferring or generating candidate rules, use
scenerank to determine which rule best explains all training pairs.

Coverage: rk_pair_ok_ applies a rule to a Before scene and compares the result
to After using msort (order-insensitive). rk_coverage_pairs collects all pairs
that a rule explains (via include). rk_coverage counts them.

Consistency: rk_consistent uses maplist with rk_pair_ok_ to verify that a rule
works on every pair. rk_inconsistent_pairs finds the failures.

Ranking: rk_rank_rules builds a negated-coverage keyed list and sorts with
msort. rk_rank_candidates retains the coverage count in the output as
Coverage-Rule pairs. rk_best_rule takes the head of the ranked list.

Filtering: rk_all_consistent, rk_filter_min_coverage, and rk_perfect_rules all
use include with helper predicates for encapsulated filter logic.

Ratio and count: rk_coverage_ratio returns Num/Den for display; rk_n_pairs
returns the total pair count.

Top-N selection: rk_top_n_rules combines ranking with a length-and-append prefix
extraction (fallback to all if fewer than N candidates exist).

Internal rule engine: rk_apply_ implements the same dispatch vocabulary as
sceneapply (recolor, recolor_all, color_map, shift, to_origin, reflect_h,
reflect_v, remove_color, keep_color, sort_size_desc, sort_size_asc, top_n).
This makes scenerank self-contained without importing sceneapply.

Dependencies: None. Uses library(lists) and library(apply).

Position in dependency graph: Layer 189. Uses the pair representation established
by scenepair (Layer 188) and the rule vocabulary of sceneapply (Layer 186) without
importing either. Provides the ranking step needed by any full inference pipeline.

ARCH-181: sceneinv Pack Architecture (Layer 194)

Location: packs/sceneinv/
Module: sceneinv
Prefix: si_*
Layer: 194 (Data Layer)
Dependencies: library(lists) [member/2, list_to_set/2, sum_list/2],
              library(apply) [maplist/2, maplist/3]
No cross-pack dependencies.

Predicate inventory (14):
  si_n_before/2, si_n_after/2 - single-pair object count
  si_all_n_before/2, si_all_n_after/2 - count lists over all pairs
  si_const_n_before/2, si_const_n_after/2 - constant-count invariants
  si_n_preserved/1 - count preservation invariant
  si_colors_before/2, si_colors_after/2 - single-pair color sets
  si_const_colors_before/2, si_const_colors_after/2 - constant-color-set invariants
  si_colors_preserved/1 - color-set preservation invariant
  si_total_cells_before/2 - total cell count in Before of one pair
  si_cells_preserved/1 - cell-count preservation invariant

Design notes:
- Pairs are Before-After terms; Before and After are obj(Color,Cells) lists.
- Constancy is tested by collecting values into a list and reducing with list_to_set;
  a single-element set proves all values are equal.
- Preservation predicates use maplist over a helper that computes both sides and
  requires equality.
- si_cells_preserved uses sum_list/2 so it handles objects with multiple cells.
- All "const_*" predicates fail on empty Pairs (no claim can be made).
- All "preserved" predicates succeed vacuously on empty Pairs.


ARCH-182: seqinfer Pack Architecture (Layer 195)

Location: packs/seqinfer/
Module: seqinfer
Prefix: sq_*
Layer: 195 (Data Layer)
Dependencies: library(lists) [member/2, last/2, subtract/3, nth1/3],
              library(apply) [maplist/2, maplist/3, include/3]
No cross-pack dependencies.

Predicate inventory (14):
  sq_apply/3, sq_verify/3 - core application and verification
  sq_consistent/2, sq_coverage/3 - multi-pair evaluation
  sq_rank_seqs/3, sq_all_consistent/3 - sequence ranking and filtering
  sq_infer_2step/3, sq_infer_3step/3 - sequence search
  sq_default_rules/1, sq_solve/3 - default rules and combined solver
  sq_coverage_ratio/3, sq_n_pairs/2 - utility
  sq_explain/3, sq_verify_all/2 - explanation and batch verification

Design notes:
- sq_apply_one_/3 is a self-contained dispatch engine; it replicates the base
  rule vocabulary from sceneapply/gridsolve to avoid cross-pack dependencies.
- sq_infer_2step enumerates O(|Candidates|^2) combinations; suitable for
  candidate lists of up to ~30 rules (900 combinations per pair).
- sq_infer_3step enumerates O(|Candidates|^3); use only with small candidate lists.
- sq_verify uses msort-based equality to be order-independent.
- sq_solve tries 2-step first (full coverage), then falls back to best 1-step.
- min_list/2 and max_list/2 are imported from library(lists) for reflect ops.


ARCH-183: gridquery Pack Architecture (Layer 196)

Location: packs/gridquery/
Module: gridquery
Prefix: gq_*
Layer: 196 (Data Layer)
Dependencies: library(lists) [member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, last/2],
              library(apply) [maplist/2, maplist/3, maplist/4]
No cross-pack dependencies.

Predicate inventory (14):
  gq_size/3, gq_at/4 - dimension and cell access
  gq_row/3, gq_col/3 - row and column extraction
  gq_colors/2, gq_n_cells/3, gq_most_freq_color/2 - color statistics
  gq_region/6 - rectangular sub-grid extraction
  gq_diff/3, gq_n_diff/3, gq_same_size/2 - grid comparison
  gq_transpose/2 - structural operation
  gq_replace/5, gq_fill_region/7 - cell modification

Design notes:
- Raw grid format: list of rows, each row a list of color atoms; 0-indexed.
- gq_transpose uses gq_col to map column indices, producing one deterministic result.
- gq_replace and gq_fill_region reconstruct the grid entirely; no in-place mutation.
- gq_diff uses between/3 for index enumeration and produces r(R,C) terms consistent
  with the obj(Color, [r(R,C),...]) cell representation in scene-level packs.
- gq_most_freq_color uses the same keyed-msort pattern as multicolor (mc_dominant_color).


ARCH-184: gridparse Pack Architecture (Layer 197)

Location: packs/gridparse/
Module: gridparse
Prefix: gp_*
Layer: 197 (Data Layer)
Dependencies: library(lists) [member/2, nth0/3, memberchk/2, subtract/3, numlist/3],
              library(apply) [maplist/2, maplist/3, include/3, foldl/4]
No cross-pack dependencies.

Predicate inventory (14):
  gp_bg_color/2, gp_grid_cells/3 - grid inspection
  gp_color_components/3 - 4-connected component extraction (BFS)
  gp_grid_to_scene/3, gp_scene_to_grid/5 - format conversion
  gp_n_objects/3, gp_object_colors/3 - scene statistics
  gp_largest_object/3, gp_smallest_object/3, gp_objects_by_size/3 - size ordering
  gp_grid_from_rows/4, gp_paint_obj/3, gp_paint_scene/3 - grid construction
  gp_grid_equal/2 - equality test

Design notes:
- BFS flood fill in gp_partition_comps_ uses Prolog lists as sets; memberchk
  for O(1) lookup intent but actual O(N) in pure Prolog — acceptable for ARC
  grid sizes (up to 30x30 = 900 cells).
- gp_paint_obj uses foldl over Cells, calling gp_paint_cell_ per cell.
  Each cell rebuilds the modified row and then the modified grid.
- gp_grid_equal uses == (structural unification) for efficiency.
- gp_grid_to_scene lists objects in sort order of color, then flood-fill
  discovery order within each color.
- Round-trip guarantee: gp_grid_to_scene then gp_scene_to_grid with the same
  background color reproduces the original grid (verified by test round_trip_ring
  and round_trip_blue_square).

ARCH-189: gridscale Pack (Layer 202, gsc_*, Work Package 223)

Purpose: Integer block-pixel scaling of raw grids — upsample, downsample,
majority-vote downscale, scale-factor detection, tile inference, nearest-neighbor
resize, stride subsampling, border padding, and factor-aligned cropping.

Module: packs/gridscale/prolog/gridscale.pl
Prefix: gsc_
Layer: 202
Dependencies: library(lists), library(apply) — no cross-pack dependencies.

Exported predicates:
  gsc_upsample/3, gsc_downsample/3, gsc_block_majority/3,
  gsc_scale_factor/3, gsc_is_scale_of/3,
  gsc_block_at/5, gsc_block_uniform/5, gsc_all_uniform/2,
  gsc_infer_tile/2, gsc_factors/2,
  gsc_resize/4, gsc_subsample/3,
  gsc_pad/4, gsc_crop_to_factor/3

Private helpers:
  gsc_dims_/3: height and width from a grid
  gsc_cell_/4: value at (R,C)
  gsc_subgrid_/6: extract SH x SW sub-grid starting at (SR,SC)
  gsc_majority_/2: most frequent element of a flat list

Key design decisions:
- gsc_downsample calls gsc_all_uniform before findall to ensure failures
  from non-uniform blocks propagate correctly (findall silences failures).
- gsc_infer_tile searches from largest valid divisor down using reverse/2
  to find the coarsest valid block size.
- gsc_resize uses nearest-neighbor (floor-division mapping) for both
  upsampling and downsampling to arbitrary target sizes.

Layer table addition: Layer 202 -> gridscale (gsc_*)


ARCH-190: gridrun Pack (Layer 203, grl_*, Work Package 224)

Purpose: Run-length encoding and stripe analysis of raw grids — encode rows
and columns as Color-Length run lists, decode back to flat lists, test row/column
uniformity, detect horizontal and vertical striped grids, return stripe colors,
find the longest run in a row, and test for strictly alternating patterns.

Module: packs/gridrun/prolog/gridrun.pl
Prefix: grl_
Layer: 203
Dependencies: library(lists), library(apply) — no cross-pack dependencies.

Exported predicates:
  grl_row_runs/3, grl_col_runs/3, grl_all_row_runs/2, grl_all_col_runs/2,
  grl_decode/2, grl_run_count/3, grl_uniform_row/3, grl_uniform_col/3,
  grl_is_striped_h/1, grl_is_striped_v/1,
  grl_stripe_colors_h/2, grl_stripe_colors_v/2,
  grl_max_run/4, grl_alternating/2

Private helpers:
  grl_dims_/3: height and width from a grid
  grl_list_runs_/2: encode a flat list to run-length pairs
  grl_run_acc_/4: tail-recursive accumulator for run encoding
  grl_col_list_/3: extract column C as a flat list

Key design:
- grl_stripe_colors_h/v fails if any row/column is not uniform by checking that
  the number of collected colors equals H or W respectively.
- grl_alternating uses list_to_set to count distinct colors and requires
  exactly 2; all run lengths must be 1.

Layer table addition: Layer 203 -> gridrun (grl_*)


ARCH-191: gridflood Pack (gf_*, Layer 204)

Location: packs/gridflood/prolog/gridflood.pl
Test: packs/gridflood/test/test_gridflood.pl
Pack descriptor: packs/gridflood/pack.pl

Layer 204 sits immediately above gridrun (Layer 203) in the PrologAI dependency chain.
No cross-pack imports; uses library(lists) [nth0/3, member/2, memberchk/2, append/2,
append/3, list_to_set/2, subtract/3, min_list/2, max_list/2] and library(apply) [foldl/4].

Exported predicates (14):
  gf_fill/5          - 4-connected flood-fill from seed cell
  gf_fill8/5         - 8-connected flood-fill from seed cell
  gf_recolor/4       - global palette swap OldColor to NewColor
  gf_isolate/5       - extract one 4-connected region onto blank background
  gf_region_cells/4  - list all cells in 4-connected region at seed
  gf_region_size/4   - count cells in 4-connected region
  gf_region_bbox/7   - bounding box (MinR,MinC,MaxR,MaxC) of 4-connected region
  gf_enclosed_cells/3 - BgColor cells not reachable from grid border
  gf_fill_enclosed/4 - fill enclosed BgColor cells with FillColor
  gf_components/3    - list of cell-lists, one per 4-connected Color region
  gf_n_components/3  - count 4-connected Color regions
  gf_largest/3       - cell-list of largest 4-connected Color region
  gf_is_connected/3  - succeed if all Color cells form one connected region (4 or 8)
  gf_boundary_fill/6 - flood-fill stopping at BoundaryColor cells

Private helpers: gf_dims_/3, gf_cell_/3, gf_bfs4_/7, gf_bfs8_/7,
gf_set_cells_/4, gf_keep_larger_/3, gf_extract_components_/6.

Design decision: BFS uses an explicit queue (list) accumulated via append/3 to avoid
the stack-depth limitations of recursive DFS on large grids. The visited list is
maintained as a flat list; memberchk/2 provides O(n) lookup which is acceptable for
grid sizes typical of ARC-AGI tasks.

gf_enclosed_cells seeds BFS from the union of all border cells of BgColor, which
correctly handles multi-cell border seeds and empty borders alike.
gf_is_connected/3 for connectivity=4 delegates to gf_n_components which returns 0
for absent colors (vacuously connected).


ARCH-192: gridpath Pack (gpa_*, Layer 205)

Location: packs/gridpath/prolog/gridpath.pl
Test: packs/gridpath/test/test_gridpath.pl
Pack descriptor: packs/gridpath/pack.pl

Layer 205 sits immediately above gridflood (Layer 204). No cross-pack imports;
uses library(lists) [nth0/3, member/2, memberchk/2, append/2, append/3] only.

Exported predicates (14):
  gpa_shortest_path/7  - BFS shortest 4-path from (R1,C1) to (R2,C2) avoiding ObsColor
  gpa_path_length/7    - step count of shortest 4-path (cells - 1)
  gpa_reachable/6      - succeed if (R2,C2) reachable from (R1,C1) via 4-path
  gpa_all_reachable/5  - all cells reachable from seed via 4-connected non-Obs walk
  gpa_distance_map/5   - BFS distance triples R-C-Dist for all reachable cells
  gpa_nearest/6        - nearest reachable cell of TargetColor (tie-break by BFS order)
  gpa_flood_n/6        - cells reachable in at most N steps from seed
  gpa_wavefront/6      - cells at exactly N BFS steps from seed
  gpa_straight_h/4     - cells on horizontal segment R,C1..C2 inclusive
  gpa_straight_v/4     - cells on vertical segment C,R1..R2 inclusive
  gpa_line_of_sight/6  - same row or col with no ObsColor strictly between
  gpa_between_h/4      - cells strictly between C1 and C2 on row R
  gpa_between_v/4      - cells strictly between R1 and R2 on column C
  gpa_region_path/5    - shortest path between any Color1 and any Color2 cell

Private helpers: gpa_dims_/3, gpa_cell_/4, gpa_path_bfs_/9,
gpa_reach_bfs_/7, gpa_dist_bfs_/7.

Design decision: gpa_path_bfs_ stores the full reverse path in each BFS queue
entry (node(R, C, RevPath)). For typical ARC-AGI grids (< 30x30 cells) this
is memory-efficient enough; the BFS is guaranteed to find a shortest path
because we process nodes in FIFO order.

gpa_nearest uses gpa_distance_map + msort on D-NR-NC to find the closest
TargetColor cell; this avoids running a separate BFS per candidate.

gpa_region_path iterates over all (Color1, Color2) cell pairs and picks the
shortest successful path, which is correct but quadratic in the number of
region cells. For ARC-AGI grid sizes this is acceptable.


ARCH-193: gridmask Pack (gm_*, Layer 206)

Location: packs/gridmask/prolog/gridmask.pl
Test: packs/gridmask/test/test_gridmask.pl
Pack descriptor: packs/gridmask/pack.pl

Layer 206 sits immediately above gridpath (Layer 205). No cross-pack imports;
uses library(lists) [nth0/3, member/2, memberchk/2, append/2, append/3] only.

Exported predicates (14):
  gm_overlay/5     - overlay GridB (non-BgColor) onto GridA (BgColor cells transparent)
  gm_union/4       - union of non-background regions (GridA color wins ties)
  gm_intersect/5   - intersection: FgColor where both non-BgColor, else BgColor
  gm_difference/5  - A minus B: keep GridA where GridB is BgColor, else BgOut
  gm_invert/4      - swap foreground and background colors
  gm_mask_apply/5  - gate Grid through Mask: non-Bg passes, Bg cells -> FillColor
  gm_extract/4     - keep only named R-C cells; all others become BgColor
  gm_stamp/5       - paste Stamp at (OR,OC); all Stamp cells overwrite; out-of-bounds skipped
  gm_compare/4     - list of R-C positions where two grids differ
  gm_equal/2       - succeed if two grids are identical (unification)
  gm_sub/6         - extract Height x Width sub-grid at (R0,C0); fails if out of bounds
  gm_paste/6       - transparent paste: non-BgColor Patch cells overwrite Grid
  gm_border_mask/3 - binary mask: N-layer border cells = 'border', interior = 'interior'
  gm_color_mask/4  - binary mask: target Color cells = FgColor, others = 'bg'

Private helpers: gm_dims_/3, gm_cell_/4, gm_build_/4.

Design decision: gm_build_/4 is a single generic grid constructor that takes a
closure (R, C, V)>>(body) and calls it for each cell. This avoids duplicating
the double findall pattern across all 14 predicates.

gm_stamp uses subtraction (SR=R-OR) to map grid coordinates to stamp coordinates,
skipping cells outside stamp bounds with a guard. gm_paste is similar but uses
catch/3 to handle Patch cell access that falls outside Patch bounds, making it
robust to arbitrary (R0, C0) placements. gm_equal uses unification (=) which is
cheaper than cell-by-cell comparison when the grids are already ground.

ARCH-197 - gridstitch Pack (Layer 210)

Location: packs/gridstitch/
  pack.pl                     - pack descriptor
  prolog/gridstitch.pl        - module gridstitch, exports 14 gst_* predicates
  test/test_gridstitch.pl     - 44 PLUnit acceptance tests

Layer: 210 (Data Layer)
Dependencies: library(lists) [nth0/3, append/2, append/3]
No cross-pack dependencies.

Private helpers:
  gst_dims_/3   - grid height and width
  gst_cell_/4   - cell value at (R,C)
  gst_build_/4  - build H x W grid using lambda Goal(R,C,V)
  gst_fill_/4   - build H x W constant-fill grid (used internally)

Design notes:

gst_concat_h uses maplist/4 with an append lambda to zip row lists horizontally.
This is more concise than a manual recursive loop and handles arbitrary-length rows.

gst_hstack and gst_vstack are left-associative recursive reducers. The singleton
clause uses a cut (!) to prevent a choice point when the list has exactly one
element, ensuring deterministic behavior.

gst_split_h uses Prolog's append/3 with a length-constrained first argument
as the split mechanism (length(Top, R), append(Top, Bottom, Grid)). This avoids
explicit nth0 indexing.

gst_split_v uses maplist/4 over rows, splitting each row independently with the
same (length(LRow, C), append(LRow, RRow, Row)) pattern.

gst_tile_grid uses a two-level findall: the outer findall collects one band per
row position, and the inner findall collects sub-grids for that band using
arithmetic index computation (Start = (RowIdx-1)*NC + ColOffset).

gst_add_border uses gst_build_ with a conditional: if the mapped source cell
(OR, OC) falls within the original grid bounds, copy the cell value; otherwise
emit the border color. This handles the general case without separate border
and interior passes.


ARCH-198 - gridedge Pack (Layer 211)

Location: packs/gridedge/
  pack.pl                    - pack descriptor
  prolog/gridedge.pl         - module gridedge, exports 14 ge_* predicates
  test/test_gridedge.pl      - 44 PLUnit acceptance tests

Layer: 211 (Data Layer)
Dependencies: library(lists) [nth0/3, member/2]
No cross-pack dependencies.

Private helpers:
  ge_dims_/3   - grid height and width
  ge_cell_/4   - cell value at (R,C)
  ge_build_/4  - build H x W grid using lambda Goal(R,C,V)
  ge_nbr4_/4   - generate 4-connected neighbor (R,C) -> (NR,NC); backtracks through all 4
  ge_nbr8_/4   - generate 8-connected neighbor (R,C) -> (NR,NC); backtracks through all 8
  ge_boundary_to_nonbg_/3 - BgColor cells adjacent to any non-BgColor cell

Design notes:

ge_nbr4_ and ge_nbr8_ use member/2 over a list of offset pairs to generate
all four (or eight) neighbor directions on backtracking. They succeed for all
offsets including those that would produce out-of-bounds coordinates; callers
must follow up with ge_cell_ which will fail for out-of-bounds via nth0 failure.

The critical correctness invariant: any predicate that uses "does this cell have
at least one neighbor satisfying property P?" must wrap the neighbor check in
once/1 to ensure each qualifying cell appears exactly once in findall output.
Without once, a cell adjacent to k qualifying neighbors would appear k times.
This invariant applies to: ge_edge_cells, ge_edge_cells8, ge_boundary,
ge_boundary_to_nonbg_, ge_outer_border.

Predicates that COUNT neighbors (ge_corners, ge_endpoints, ge_smooth_cells)
use their own inner findall for the counting step and are not affected by the
once invariant.

ge_transition_map uses gst_build_ with a per-cell inner findall that counts
differently-colored 4-neighbors. Cell values are integers in [0..4].


ARCH-199: gridmorph Pack (gmo_*, Layer 212)

File: packs/gridmorph/prolog/gridmorph.pl
Test: packs/gridmorph/test/test_gridmorph.pl
Pack: packs/gridmorph/pack.pl

Layer 212 sits immediately above gridedge (Layer 211).
Uses library(lists): nth0/3, member/2, append/3. No cross-pack dependencies.

Private helpers:
- gmo_dims_/3: grid height and width
- gmo_cell_/4: cell value at row R, column C (0-indexed); fails out of bounds
- gmo_build_/4: build H x W grid using lambda Goal(R, C, V)
- gmo_nbr4_/4: generate one 4-connected neighbor on backtracking (4 choices)
- gmo_bg_color_/3: find first non-FgColor cell in row-major order
- gmo_dilate1_step_/3: one dilation iteration
- gmo_erode1_step_/4: one erosion iteration (requires BgColor)
- gmo_dilate_n_/4: iterate N dilation steps (base case N=0 cuts choicepoint)
- gmo_erode_n_/5: iterate N erosion steps (base case N=0 cuts choicepoint)
- gmo_small_cells_/6: BFS to classify components as small or large
- gmo_bfs_/6: generic BFS from seeds through TargetColor cells

Design notes:

Erosion boundary behavior: grid boundary cells have no out-of-bounds neighbors.
Corner cells of a FgColor region may survive erosion when all their in-bounds
neighbors are FgColor (e.g., a 2x2 block corner in a 3x3 grid).

The once/1 invariant applies to gmo_boundary_inner and gmo_boundary_outer:
any predicate asking "does this cell have at least one qualifying neighbor?"
must wrap the neighbor check in once/1 inside findall to prevent a cell with
k qualifying neighbors from appearing k times.

gmo_connected_border BFS: Seeds may include grid border cells reachable via
both row-sweep and column-sweep (corners counted twice). The memberchk(RC,Visited)
check handles duplicates. BlockColor is passed for interface consistency but is
not used in BFS expansion; only TargetColor cells are traversed.

gmo_fill_holes uses memberchk on the OpenBg list for O(|OpenBg|) membership
tests, acceptable for ARC-AGI grid sizes. gmo_remove_small uses BFS per
unprocessed FgColor cell; large components are re-processed but correct.


ARCH-200: gridconv Pack (gcv_*, Layer 213)

File: packs/gridconv/prolog/gridconv.pl
Test: packs/gridconv/test/test_gridconv.pl
Pack: packs/gridconv/pack.pl

Layer 213 sits immediately above gridmorph (Layer 212).
Uses library(lists): nth0/3, member/2, append/3. msort/2 is a built-in.
No cross-pack dependencies.

Private helpers:
- gcv_dims_/3: grid height and width
- gcv_cell_/4: cell value at row R, column C; fails out of bounds
- gcv_cell_fill_/5: cell value with fallback Fill for out-of-bounds
- gcv_build_/4: build H x W grid using lambda Goal(R, C, V)
- gcv_inbounds_vals_/6: collect all in-bounds values in (2N+1)x(2N+1) window
- gcv_mode_/2: most frequent element in a list (ties by term order via msort)
- gcv_max_run_/7: recursive accumulator for finding longest run in sorted list
- gcv_all_eq_/1: test whether all list elements are equal
- gcv_count_inbounds_/5: count in-bounds cells in window (any color)
- gcv_match_at_/4: test whether Pattern exactly matches Grid at top-left (R,C)

Design notes:

Window radius convention: radius N gives a (2N+1) x (2N+1) window. Radius 0
gives a 1x1 window (just the cell itself). Radius 1 gives 3x3, etc.

gcv_count_in ignores out-of-bounds positions (no phantom fill). gcv_window
uses explicit Fill for all positions including out-of-bounds.

gcv_erode_sq correctness: a FgColor cell survives only if EVERY in-bounds
window cell is FgColor. This is implemented by comparing the Color count to
the total in-bounds count (not to (2N+1)^2). Near-boundary cells have smaller
effective windows and may therefore survive erosion when they would not if the
window were padded.

gcv_match_at_ uses negation-as-failure: it fails if any Pattern cell does not
match the corresponding Grid cell (or if Grid cell is out of bounds).

gcv_replace_pattern replaces cells in the match region using row/column
arithmetic within gcv_build_; all other cells pass through unchanged.


ARCH-201: gridgraph Pack (ggr_*, Layer 214)

File: packs/gridgraph/prolog/gridgraph.pl
Test: packs/gridgraph/test/test_gridgraph.pl
Pack: packs/gridgraph/pack.pl

Layer 214 sits immediately above gridconv (Layer 213).
Uses library(lists): nth0/3, member/2, append/3, list_to_set/2, subtract/3.
msort/2 is a built-in (not imported from library). No cross-pack dependencies.

Private helpers:
- ggr_dims_/3: grid height and width
- ggr_cell_/4: cell value at row R, column C; fails out of bounds
- ggr_nbr4_/4: generate one 4-connected neighbor on backtracking
- ggr_colors_/2: list of all distinct colors in Grid (via list_to_set)
- ggr_bfs_same_/6: BFS through same-color cells from a seed list
- ggr_count_components_/5: recursive component counter using BFS and subtract
- ggr_partition_components_/5: recursive component cell partitioner

Design notes:

ggr_adj_colors uses once/1 implicitly (not needed here since pairs are
deduplicated via list_to_set). However, the inner loop may produce the same
pair multiple times from different boundary cells; list_to_set handles this.

ggr_shared_border uses once/1 to ensure each C1 cell appears at most once
regardless of how many C2 neighbors it has.

ggr_enclosed_colors uses negation-as-failure with two independent \+ guards:
one for border presence, one for foreign-color neighbor presence.

ggr_spanning_h and ggr_spanning_v enumerate all grid colors and check border
presence; the outer findall may produce duplicates (one per color occurrence),
which list_to_set removes.

ggr_bfs_same_ uses memberchk for visited-set membership and subtract for
removing component cells from the remaining set. For ARC-AGI-2 grid sizes
(typically <= 30x30 = 900 cells), this O(|Component|^2) approach is acceptable.

  ggl_common/4   - agreement (both same non-bg → value; else bg)
  ggl_differ/4   - disagreement (both non-bg and different → Grid1; else bg)
  ggl_any/3      - list-wise OR (first non-bg across list wins; else bg)
  ggl_all/3      - list-wise AND (unanimous non-bg agreement; else bg)
  ggl_majority/3 - plurality vote (most frequent non-bg if >N/2; else bg)
  ggl_unanimous/3 - all-grids strict agreement including bg/non-bg; else bg
  ggl_mask/5     - masking (keep Grid where Mask=MaskColor; else bg)
  ggl_if/5       - conditional selection (CondColor → Then; else → Else)
  ggl_filter/4   - color filtering (keep cells in Colors list; else bg)
